1 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Clark


NO. 2012-KA-0508


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-0508 (La. 12/19/16); 220 So. 3d 583; 2016 La. LEXIS 2512



December 19, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Clark, 2017 La. LEXIS 494 (La., Mar. 13, 2017)
Petition for certiorari filed at, 06/10/2017


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTIETH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF WEST FELICIANA.
State v. Clark, 39 So. 3d 594, 2010 La. LEXIS 1726 (La., July 17, 2010)



DISPOSITION: CONVICTION AND SENTENCE AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was properly convicted of first degree murder of a correctional officer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14.30 as the State presented sufficient evidence of defendant's specific intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm as required by § 14:30(A)(1) and (2); [2]-Direct and circumstantial evidence linked defendant to the first degree murder of the officer, and the totality of the evidence was sufficient to convince beyond a reasonable doubt the jury, who resolved issues of credibility against defendant, that defendant had formed the requisite specific intent to take the life of the officer; [3]-Sufficient evidence was presented to the jury from which the jury clearly concluded that neither the degree of defendant's participation nor mental state at the time of the attempted escape and murder of the officer would exempt him from imposition of the death penalty.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

2 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Chester


No. 15-KP-2304


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-2304 (La. 12/16/16); 208 So. 3d 338; 2016 La. LEXIS 2506



December 16, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Teddy Chester; - Defendant; Applying For Supervisory and/or Remedial Writs, Parish of Jefferson, 24th Judicial District Court Div. K, No. 96-2598.
State v. Chester, 724 So. 2d 1276, 1998 La. LEXIS 3501 (La., Dec. 1, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's death penalty case, counsel was not ineffective in litigating the motion to suppress his custodial statements because defendant appeared completely coherent and, before giving his second statement in which he placed himself inside the taxi, was again advised of his rights and waived them; defendant's conduct thus indicated he made a knowing and intelligent waiver; [2]-Counsel's decision not to draw further attention to the letters and seek their admission in full form under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:450 was strategic because the damaging nature of much of the content that was admitted suggested that other redacted portions might have been harmful to the defense; defendant therefore could not shown that counsel unprofessionally erred by failing to introduce the letters in complete form.


OUTCOME: The writ was denied.

 

3 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Johno v. Doe


NO. 2016-CA-0087


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2016-0087 (La. 12/06/16); 218 So. 3d 1004; 2016 La. LEXIS 2480



December 6, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES.
Johno v. Doe, 187 So. 3d 581, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 480 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2016)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800.17, which provided retroactive statutory immunity to the government and its agents for certain actions taken in the wake of a hurricane, was constitutional as applied to a homeowner whose house was demolished prior to the implementation of the immunity statute. HOLDINGS: [1]-The homeowner could not be retroactively deprived of causes of actions which vested when his house was demolished prior to the implementation of the immunity statute. Thus, La. Rev. Stat. § 9:2800.17 was unconstitutional as applied retroactively, because the homeowner's causes of action arising from the demolition of his house accrued before the effective date of the statute.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

4 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Arrow Aviation Co., LLC v. St. Martin Parish Sch. Bd. Tax Sales Dep't


NO. 2016-CA-1132


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2016-1132 (La. 12/06/16); 218 So. 3d 1031; 2016 La. LEXIS 2482



December 6, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPEAL FROM THE 16TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D)(1) required the Louisiana Legislature when it enacted a tax exclusion to treat tax authorities in all parishes the same or to make tax authorities in all parishes act the same. HOLDINGS: [1]-Under La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D)(1), a legislative tax exclusion must treat all local tax authorities the same. Because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(14)(g)(i)(bb) (2013) (current version at La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(14)(g)(i)(bb)(I)) mandates that tax authorities in East Feliciana Parish, Louisiana apply the exclusion--but for tax authorities in all other parishes application of the exclusion remains optional--La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(14)(g)(i)(bb) is unconstitutional; [2]-Severance of the offending mandatory language in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301(14)(g)(i)(bb) applicable to tax authorities in East Feliciana Parish was appropriate.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed, and matter remanded for further proceedings.

6 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Mayeux v. Charlet


NO. 2016-CA-1463


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2016-1463 (La. 10/28/2016); 203 So. 3d 1030; 2016 La. LEXIS 2144



October 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE HONORABLE R. MICHAEL CALDWELL, JUDGE.
Parents of Minor Child v. Charlet, 135 So. 3d 1177, 2014 La. LEXIS 765 (La., 2014)



DISPOSITION: DECLARATION OF UNCONSTITUTIONALITY VACATED; and REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in declaring La. Child. Code Ann. art. 609 unconstitutional in a suit filed by plaintiff parents alleging defendant priest negligently failed to report a minor child's sexual abuse to police and plaintiffs under art. 609 after she told him about the abuse during confession. HOLDINGS: [1]-When hearing a confession, the priest was not a "mandatory reporter" under former La. Child. Code Ann. art. 603 such that art. 609 required him to report information learned during a sacramental confession, because former art. 603(15)(c) specifically exempted confidential communication to clergy that were privileged under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 511; [2]-Because the priest was not a mandatory reporter under the circumstances of the case, there had been no need for the trial court to declare art. 609 unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The trial court's declaration of unconstitutionality was vacated.

 

7 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Morgan v. State


No. 2015-KH-0100


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-0100 (La. 10/19/16); 217 So. 3d 266; 2016 La. LEXIS 2077



October 19, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Morgan, 786 So. 2d 983, 2001 La. App. LEXIS 615 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 21, 2001)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to correct a 99-year sentence without parole for an armed robbery he committed while a juvenile. HOLDINGS: [1]-Though this was not a life sentence expressly prohibited by Graham v. Florida, as he would not be parole-eligible until age 101, it was functionally equivalent to life without parole and violated Graham's rule that a juvenile convicted of a non-homicide offense could not be incarcerated for the duration of his life without a meaningful opportunity for release; [2]-The high court construed La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(D)'s parole eligibility provision as applying not just to juvenile offenders serving life sentences for non-homicide offenses, but to those like defendant serving an effective life sentence for a single non-homicide offense that was not deemed so serious as to warrant an automatic life sentence.


OUTCOME: The high court ordered the deletion of defendant's parole ineligibility from his sentence.

 

8 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Fecke v. Bd. of Supervisors of La. State Univ. & Agric. & Mech. College


No. 2015-C-1806 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 2015-C-1807


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1806 (La. 09/23/16); 217 So. 3d 237; 2016 La. LEXIS 1803



September 23, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by, in part, Rehearing denied by, in part, Modified by Fecke v. Bd. of Supervisors of La. State Univ., 2016 La. LEXIS 2081 (La., Oct. 19, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Fecke v. Bd. of Supervisors of La. State Univ., 180 So. 3d 326, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1357 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; AND TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court held that a plaintiff who is awarded future medical care pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(B)(3)(c) is not entitled to legal interest on the award and may not recover attorney's fees or costs from the award prior to its placement into the Future Medical Care Fund (FMCF); [2]-The Court further held that a plaintiff who was unemployed at the time of the injury may recover the loss of future earnings, as defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5106(D)(2); [3]-The Court held that, as a result, the judgment was reversed, in part, as to the finding that plaintiff was entitled to legal interest on an award for future medical care and that said interest was to be paid into the FMCF.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, in part; trial court judgment reinstated, in part.

 

9 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Arceneaux v. Amstar Corp.


NO. 2015-C-0588


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-0588 (La. 07/09/16); 200 So. 3d 277; 2016 La. LEXIS 1675



September 7, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Arceneaux v. Amstar Corp., 2016 La. LEXIS 2099 (La., Oct. 19, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Arceneaux v. Amstar Corp., 161 So. 3d 115, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 378 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a dispute between an insured and insurer regarding the duty to defend underlying claims, arising from long latency disease cases alleging hearing loss suffered by the insured's workers, the duty to defend was to be prorated between the parties because the insurer's occurrence-based policies provided coverage for only 26 months of the approximately 60-year period during which exposure occurred; [2]-Moreover, application of the pro rata allocation method for defense costs was supported by the policy language, which limited coverage to bodily injury that occurred during the policy period, and it did not violate the reasonable expectations of the parties; [3]-In determining the formula for pro ration, the court determined that the amount of time an insurer was on the risk seemed appropriate, as there were periods where they was no policy in effect and thus no policy limits.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; matter remanded for further proceedings.

 

10 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Sims


No. 2015-KA-2163


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-2163 (La. 06/29/16); 195 So. 3d 441; 2016 La. LEXIS 1559



June 29, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In quashing a charge of trafficking of children for sexual purposes in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:46.3, the trial court erred in ruling that § 14:46.3(C)(2), which provided that lack of knowledge of a victim's age was not a defense, was unconstitutional; § 14:46.3(C)(2) did not irreconcilably conflict with § 14:46.3(A)(1)'s knowledge requirement, but instead modified the word "knowingly" in § 14:46.3(A)(1), removing any doubt that knowledge of the victim's age was not an element of the offense; [2]-Section 14:46.3(C)(2) was not unconstitutional solely because it was a strict liability statute, as scienter was not a required element of a crime where the underlying conduct would be illegal without the strict liability element, particularly where the offense involved juveniles and addressed conduct that was illegal notwithstanding the victim's age.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

11 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Free


No. 2016-O-0434


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2016-0434 (La. 06/29/16); 199 So. 3d 571; 2016 La. LEXIS 1569



June 29, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Free, 158 So. 3d 771, 2014 La. LEXIS 2623 (La., 2014)



DISPOSITION: SUSPENSION ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court agreed with the findings of the Judiciary Commission of Louisiana that there was clear and convincing evidence that a judge committed violations of La. Code Jud. Conduct Canon 1, 2, 2(A), 3(A)(1)-(3), and 3(C), as well as La. Const. art. V, § 25(C) by, inter alia, interrupting a private meeting involving parties in a criminal case before him, abusing his contempt authority under La. Code Crim. Proc. arts. 21 and 22, making inappropriate comments, and exhibiting a lack of proper decorum and temperament; [2]-The Commission's recommendation of a one-year suspension, without pay, was deemed appropriate based on, inter alia, review of the Chaisson factors, including that his actions had a negative impact on the integrity and respect for the judiciary, and he largely failed to accept responsibility for his conduct.


OUTCOME: Suspension imposed on judge.

State v. Montgomery


No. 2013-KP-1163


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-1163 (La. 06/28/16); 194 So. 3d 606; 2016 La. LEXIS 1539



June 28, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Montgomery, Henry; - Defendant; Applying For Supervisory and/or Remedial Writs, Parish of E. Baton Rouge, 19th Judicial District Court Div. G, No. 48-489; to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, No. 2013 KW 0442.
Montgomery v. Louisiana, 136 S. Ct. 718, 193 L. Ed. 2d 599, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 862 (U.S., 2016)



DISPOSITION: On remand from United States Supreme Court. Remanded to district court for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The district court, on remand from the United States Supreme Court, was to determine whether a juvenile, and other prisoners like him, would be granted or denied parole eligibility after being sentenced to life imprisonment for first- or second-degree murder because the juvenile was entitled to an opportunity to demonstrate maturity and rehabilitation, and although the Legislature was unable to enact legislation during the 2016 Regular Session, it provided general sentencing guidelines in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 894.1 that the district court might deem relevant in accordance with La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 878.1(B).


OUTCOME: Sentence vacated and matter remanded.

State ex rel. Jack v. State


NO. 2015-KH-1341


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1341 (La. 06/17/16); 194 So. 3d 600; 2016 La. LEXIS 1440



June 17, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Clarence Jack; - Plaintiff; Applying For Supervisory and/or Remedial Writs, Parish of St. Mary, 16th Judicial District Court Div. A, No. 123348; to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, No. 2015 KW 0479. ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARY.
State v. Jack, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1230 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 22, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-With regard to petitioner's tenth application for post conviction relief, the Supreme Court found that petitioner did not satisfy the exception to the two-year time limitation provided for in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.8(A); [2]-Petitioner's conviction and sentence became final in May 1990, and his right to file an application for post-conviction relief expired in 1992; [3]-Petitioner's latest application for post conviction relief was untimely; [4]-Petitioner's claim also failed under the provisions of La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 930.4(D), as it failed to raise a new or different claim.


OUTCOME: Application denied and dismissed.

19 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Tillman ex rel. Tillman v. State


NO. 2015-CC-1114 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2015-CC-1263 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2015-CC-1264


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1114 (La. 03/15/16); 187 So. 3d 445; 2016 La. LEXIS 605



March 15, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
Miller v. Tulane Lakeside Hosp., 178 So. 3d 577, 2015 La. LEXIS 2245 (La., 2015)
Tillman v. State (In re Tillman), 178 So. 3d 576, 2015 La. LEXIS 2249 (La., 2015)
Miller v. Tulane Lakeside Hosp., 178 So. 3d 577, 2015 La. LEXIS 2244 (La., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the Louisiana Division of Administration (DOA) acted in accordance with applicable law in stamping fax-filed requests for review of claimants' medical malpractice claims as filed on the business day following facsimile transmission of the requests. HOLDINGS: [1]-Because the claimants' requests for review of their medical malpractice claims were received by the DOA, via the designated fax system, prior to midnight on the last day of the prescriptive period, they were received prior to the expiration of the last day of the prescriptive period, in accordance with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 and La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 3454, 3456, and 3492, and were timely filed pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1231.8(A)(2)(b). Therefore, the intermediate appellate court decisions erred in sustaining the health care providers' peremptory exceptions pleading the objection of prescription.


OUTCOME: Judgments of the intermediate appellate court reversed, and cases remanded with instructions.

 

20 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Coastal Drilling Co., LLC v. Dufrene


NO. 2015-C-1793


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1793 (La. 03/15/16); 198 So. 3d 108; 2016 La. LEXIS 594



March 15, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Coastal Drilling Co., L.L.C. v. Dufrene, 2016 La. LEXIS 1060 (La., May 2, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ST. MARY.
Coastal Drilling Co., L.L.C. v. Dufrene, 174 So. 3d 673, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1165 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Court reversed the decree of unconstitutionality of La. Admin. Code tit. 61, § I:4403(A) and (B)(2) and ordered summary judgment in favor of the drilling company and the refund of all taxes paid under protest, along with interest as allowed by law because the broad legislative intent of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.1 includes, within the purview of the exemption, reconstruction efforts that are the commercial equivalent to original or new construction and nothing in the plain language of § 47:305.1(A) restricts the reading to a more narrow definition; [2]-The Court declared La. Admin. Code tit. 61, § I:4403(A) and (B)(2) valid inasmuch as it did not exceed the authority granted to the agency by the legislature, nor did it exceed the scope of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.1.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed; judgment rendered in favor of taxpayer.


 

21 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dahlem


NO. 2014-KO-1555


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2014-1555 (La. 03/15/16); 197 So. 3d 676; 2016 La. LEXIS 590



March 15, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Dahlem, 2016 La. LEXIS 1061 (La., May 2, 2016)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Dahlem v. Poret, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 138861 (E.D. La., Jan. 24, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF WASHINGTON.
State v. Dahlem, 148 So. 3d 591, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 1585 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 18, 2014)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether defendant was denied a fair trial and due process of law because he was, without contemporaneous objection at trial, tried by a six-person jury, instead of a twelve-person jury, on a fourth offense driving while intoxicated (DWI) charge. HOLDINGS: [1]-Although the trial court may have considered the documentary evidence necessary to impose the enhanced provisions set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:98(E)(4)(a) (amended), as evidenced by the trial court's original sentence, the reviewing court was unable to reach the jury composition issue. Even assuming a possible jury composition error, it was rendered moot by defendant's multiple offender status, which required that he be sentenced under the mandatory hard labor requirement set forth in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1(G).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State ex rel. Guidry v. State

PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. MARTIN.

23 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Foret


NO. 2015-C-1298


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1298 (La. 01/27/16); 188 So. 3d 154; 2016 La. LEXIS 117



January 27, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
State v. Foret, 174 So. 3d 700, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1178 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where plaintiff had pled guilty to health care fraud in federal court, the Sledge Jeansonne Louisiana Insurance Fraud Prevention Act could not be applied retroactively to his criminal misconduct, which would have constituted insurance fraud in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1924, and which occurred prior to the Act's effective date, as the Act operated prospectively only, since retroactive application would impermissibly apply new consequences to past events; that he pled guilty after the Act's effective date was immaterial, as the Act regulated criminal conduct, not a subsequent guilty plea to such conduct; [2]-For the same reasons, the Louisiana Unfair Trade Practice and Consumer Protection Act (LUPTA) could not be applied retroactively to defendant's criminal misconduct that occurred prior to its effective date; LUPTA operated prospectively only.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

24 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nunez


NO. 2015-KK-1473 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2015-KK-1486


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1473 (La. 01/27/16); 187 So. 3d 964; 2016 La. LEXIS 110



January 27, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Nunez, 2016 La. LEXIS 610 (La., Mar. 15, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Brown, 174 So. 3d 95, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1355 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2015)
State v. Nunez, 174 So. 3d 105, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 1354 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendants' due process rights were not violated by Orleans Parish Criminal District Court's case allotment system, which randomly assigned cases to different District Judges based on the first date of the first alleged offense as the District Attorney's actions did not drive the selection of Judges and the allotment system adequately minimized the risk of docket manipulation by either side since the prosecutor was constrained by defendants' conduct in selecting the date of the earliest charged offense; [2]-An allotment procedure did not violate due process principles or the requirements of La. Dist. Ct., R. 14 by merely being susceptible to manipulation; [3]-The burden was on defendants to show some actual manipulation or prejudice; [4]-Defendants did not show manipulation or prejudice as the dates selected by the District Attorney were highly reasonable.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed, in part, and affirmed, in part. Case remanded.

 

25 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Shepherd v. Schedler


NO. 2015-CA-1750


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2015-1750 (La. 01/27/16); 209 So. 3d 752; 2016 La. LEXIS 120



January 27, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing granted by Shepherd v. Schedler, 2016 La. LEXIS 1034 (La., May 2, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Shepherd v. Schedler, 178 So. 3d 574, 2015 La. LEXIS 2221 (La., 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the trial court erred in declaring void an amendment to La. Const. art. I, § 10 which limited felons from seeking public office. HOLDINGS: [1]-Plaintiff had standing to bring the constitutional challenge based on his status as a convicted felon whose candidacy was challenged under the amendment, as his right to run for public office was one of the "full rights of citizenship" under La. Const. art. I, § 20; [2]-Though the election had occurred while the case was pending, the high court considered the appeal because the "capable of repetition, yet evading review" exception to the mootness doctrine applied; [3]-The amendment was void because it was not properly enacted under La. Const. art. XIII, § 1, since the language presented to the voters for ratification as a constitutional amendment was not the language adopted by the legislature.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Bank of N.Y. Mellon v. Smith


NO. 2015-C-0530


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2014-0530 (La. 10/14/15); 180 So. 3d 1238; 2015 La. LEXIS 2177



October 14, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF GRANT.
Bank of N.Y. Mellon v. Smith, 159 So. 3d 1088, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 259 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2015)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A borrower's action against private attorneys for her lender under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 failed to state a claim because, although the lender failed to obtain two witnesses when executing the promissory note and mortgage as required by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 2635(A)(2), this failure was not attributable to the attorneys who sought executory process; [2]-Although the failure to provide the required notice pursuant to the mortgage provisions could serve as a basis to claim misapplication of executory process, the borrower was personally served with notice of the petition for executory process documents, and no unconstitutional seizure occurred; [3]-Any negligence by the attorneys was not sufficient to make them liable to a non-client.


OUTCOME: Judgment of the court of appeal reversed and judgment of the district court reinstated.

31 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Faulk v. Union Pac. R.R. Co.


NO. 2014-CQ-1598


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2014-1598 (La. 06/30/15); 172 So. 3d 1034; 2015 La. LEXIS 1498



June 30, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON CERTIFIED QUESTION FROM THE UNITED STATES FIFTH CIRCUIT COURT OF APPEALS.
Faulk v. Union Pac. R.R. Co., 576 Fed. Appx. 345, 2014 U.S. App. LEXIS 14286 (5th Cir. La., 2014)



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:394, which prevented closure of private railroad crossings without prior approval by the Louisiana Public Service Commission (LPSC), constituted a taking of a railroad's private property that violated La. Const. art. I, § 4 (a question certified by the United States Court of Appeals, Fifth Circuit). HOLDINGS: [1]-The railroad was not entitled to exclusive use of the land on which it had only a right of use servitude, because under Louisiana law, a right of use was a limited personal servitude, not ownership; [2]-Section 48:394 applied retroactively because it was a procedural law that did not impair contractual obligations or disturb vested rights; [3]-Until the LPSC ruled on the railroad's intent to close the private crossings, the railroad's claim that § 48:394 effected a temporary physical taking of its property was not ripe for adjudication.


OUTCOME: The high court answered the question in the negative.

LaPointe v. Vermilion Parish Sch. Bd.


NO. 2015-CA-0432


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA

June 30, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by LaPointe v. Vermilion Parish Sch. Bd., 177 So. 3d 799, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 2177 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 4, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF VERMILION.
LaPointe v. Vermilion Parish Sch. Bd., 158 So. 3d 257, 2015 La. App. LEXIS 186 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The court of appeal erred in declaring La. Rev. Stat. § 17:443, as amended by 2012 La. Acts 1 provided extensive post-termination procedures sufficient to ensure due process because the teacher could seek expedited judicial review of her case if unsatisfied with the panel's recommendation and the superintendent's action.


OUTCOME: Order reversed.

State v. Eberhardt

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-2306 (La. 07/01/14); 145 So. 3d 377; 2014 La. LEXIS 1570



July 1, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY.

ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
State v. Eberhardt, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 1794 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 9, 2013)



DISPOSITION: TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED; TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.1, barring a felon's firearm possession, did not facially violate La. Const. art. OUTCOME: Judgments reversed, affirmed.

State v. Webb


NO. 2013-KK-1681


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-1681 (La. 05/07/14); 144 So. 3d 971; 2014 La. LEXIS 1148



May 7, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Webb, 126 So. 3d 474, 2013 La. LEXIS 2645 (La., 2013)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(E)'s enhancement of the penalty for possessing illegal drugs while in carrying a firearm was not an unconstitutional abridgement of the fundamental right under La. Const. art. I, § 11 to keep and bear arms since when a person was engaged in the unlawful conduct of possessing illegal drugs, the person's own unlawful actions had qualified his right to engage in what would otherwise be the exercise of that fundamental right; [2]-The State had a compelling state interest in public safety by restricting the simultaneous possession of illegal drugs and firearms and preventing drug trafficking; [3]-Section 14:95(E) was narrowly tailored to serve the State's compelling interest as it did not apply to every situation of possessing controlled substances and a firearm since there were limitations placed upon cases of constructive possession.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Matter remanded.

State v. Gates

DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE LOWER COURTS VACATED; CASE REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The Fourth Amendment and La. Const. art. State v. Davenport


NO. 2013-KK-1859


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-1859 (La. 05/07/14); 147 So. 3d 137; 2014 La. LEXIS 1149



May 7, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Davenport, 2014 La. LEXIS 1604 (La., July 1, 2014)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Davenport v. Richardson, 2015 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 175035 (W.D. La., Apr. 29, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF SABINE.
State v. Davenport, 116 So. 3d 1038, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 1384 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2013)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 778 was explicitly limited to bench trials, a trial judge was without legal power to acquit an aggravated rape defendant before the jury returned a verdict, and the judge's grant of an acquittal was void and of no effect; this was distinct from comparable cases in which the judge merely acted erroneously; [2]-Defendant was constitutionally and statutorily entitled to have his trial proceed to a verdict by the jury, La. Const. art. I, § 17(A); [3]-The trial judge's grant of a mistrial following its erroneous and void acquittal was proper under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 775(5), because the jury had been dismissed and it was physically impossible to continue the trial; [4]-Because a legally ordered mistrial was declared, a retrial of defendant would not constitute double jeopardy under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 591.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeal's judgment, reinstated the trial court's order of mistrial, and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43(E)(2).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Smith

13-2318 (La. 01/28/14); 144 So. 3d 867; 2014 La. LEXIS 201

CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Prohibiting defendant from serving as the billing agent for Medicaid providers, after being excluded from doing so because of allegations of past fraud and misconduct, was not the type of conduct that the U.S. Supreme Court, or the Supreme Court of Louisiana, had ever recognized as conduct protected by the First Amendment of the U.S. Constitution; [2]-The First Amendment was not implicated in the receipt of Medicaid or Medicare benefits; [3]-Defendant's overbreadth argument failed no matter how La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:126.3.1(A)(3) was interpreted because the statute did not reach a substantial amount of constitutionally protected conduct.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed. Matter remanded.

State ex rel. J.M.


NO. 2013-CK-1717 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2013-KA-1772


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-1717 (La. 01/28/14); 144 So. 3d 853; 2014 La. LEXIS 206



January 28, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE JUVENILE COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.

ON APPEAL FROM THE JUVENILE COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE PAMELA TAYLOR JOHNSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-La. Const. art. I, § 11, as amended to delete language authorizing the passage of laws regarding the carrying of concealed weapons, did not invalidate La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95(A)(1) or restrict the legislature's ability to pass such laws; [2]-Because La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:95.8 was narrowly tailored to serve the compelling government interest in preventing youths who might be immature and impulsive from easily accessing handguns, to reduce the incidence of accidents or violent crime, § 14:95.8 withstood the strict scrutiny analysis required by La. Const. art. I, § 11, as amended; [3]-As applied to a juvenile in a delinquency proceeding, § 14:95(A)(1) also met the requirement of strict scrutiny, in light of the compelling government interest in restricting concealed weapons to protect public safety and the statute's narrow tailoring to achieve this legitimate purpose.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

Krielow v. La. Dep't of Agric. & Forestry

55 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brown


NO. 12-KP-0872


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


12-0872 (La. 05/07/13); 118 So. 3d 332; 2013 La. LEXIS 1075



May 7, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRIT TO THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
State v. Brown, 98 So. 3d 320, 2012 La. LEXIS 2614 (La., 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was found guilty of aggravated kidnapping and four counts of armed robbery for crimes committed when defendant was 16 years old, and the trial court imposed a mandatory term of life imprisonment without parole for the kidnapping and four 10-year terms, also without benefit of parole, for the armed robberies, but subsequently amended the sentences. The Court of Appeal, Louisiana, affirmed. The State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Louisiana Supreme Court held that parole eligibility restrictions were proper on defendant's four 10-year sentences for four armed robberies. No Eighth Amendment violation arose from the 70-year sentence that resulted from combining the 40 years for armed robberies with a consecutive sentence of life for aggravated kidnapping, with parole possible after 30 years under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:574.4(D). The court held that although the Eighth Amendment's prohibition of cruel and unusual punishment forbade the imposition of life in prison without parole for juveniles committing non-homicide crimes, that holding of the U.S. Supreme Court applied only to sentences of life in prison without parole, and did not apply to a sentence of years without the possibility of parole. Nothing in U.S. Supreme Court case law addressed the current situation: a defendant convicted of multiple offenses and given term-of-year sentences, that, if tacked onto his life sentence parole eligibility date, equated to a possible release date when defendant reached the age of 86. The trial court properly amended defendant's life sentence to allow parole eligibility.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court amending defendant's four 10-year sentences for four armed robberies, affirmed the amended life sentence for kidnapping, and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

56 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



La. Fedn. of Teachers v. State


NO. 2013-CA-0120 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2013-CA-0232 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2013-CA-0350


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2013-0120 (La. 05/07/13); 118 So. 3d 1033; 2013 La. LEXIS 1077



May 7, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE TIMOTHY E. KELLEY, JUDGE.
La. Fed'n of Teachers v. State, 95 So. 3d 1058, 2012 La. LEXIS 2254 (La., 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART, AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff teachers' unions brought a declaratory judgment action against defendants Department of Education and Board of Elementary and Secondary Education (BESE) in the 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, seeking a declaration that La. Senate Concurrent Resolution No. 99 and 2012 La. Acts 2 were unconstitutional. This district court found both measures unconstitutional, and defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Resolution 99 and Act 2 were part of a comprehensive school choice program. The most essential funding effect of Resolution 99 was that it provided funding for voucher programs and a Course Choice Program to be paid to nonpublic entities from the Minimum Foundation Program (MFP), pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 17:4017. La. Const. art. VIII, § 13(B), clearly restricted the use of MFP funds to parish and city school systems. Under Section 13(A), assistance could be given to nonpublic schools in the form of textbooks and other instructional materials; under Section 13(B), the MFP funds were reserved for "parish and city school systems." The court did not need to determine whether local funds were also diverted to nonpublic schools because the MFP formula considered both state and local funds and MFP funds were being unconstitutionally diverted to nonpublic entities. Additionally, Resolution 99 was enacted in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 2(A)(3)(a), because it was introduced on the 57th calendar day of the regular session of the Senate. The bill did not contain incongruous and unrelated matters in violation of the single object rule, La. Const. art. III, § 15(A) and (C).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the holding that 2012 La. Acts 2 was unconstitutional and rendered judgment declaring Resolution 99 as void from the outset.


 

57 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bazile


NO. 2012-KA-2243


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-2243 (La. 05/07/13); 144 So. 3d 719; 2013 La. LEXIS 1082



May 7, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE MICHAEL R. ERWIN, JUDGE.
State v. Bazile, 85 So. 3d 1, 2012 La. LEXIS 17 (La., Jan. 24, 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a second degree murder case, the trial court granted defendant's motion to declare La. Const. art. I, § 17(A), as amended in 2010, unconstitutional after he was prohibited from making an untimely waiver of his right to a jury trial. The State took a writ to the Court of Appeal of Louisiana, which was denied by a vote of 2-1. The state supreme court granted the State's application for review.


OVERVIEW: La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) was enacted to limit the time period in which a criminal defendant charged with a non-capital offense could exercise his constitutional right to waive a jury trial. The trial court erred by granting defendant's motion to declare La. Const. art. I, § 17(A), as amended in 2010, unconstitutional after he was prohibited from making an untimely waiver of his right to a jury trial in a second degree murder case. The Supreme Court of Louisiana held that the provisions of La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) at issue were constitutional under U.S. Const. amend. VI and XIV and the state constitution. Although the right to trial by jury was constitutionally protected under both the federal and state constitutions, there was no federal or state constitutional right to demand trial before a judge sitting alone.


OUTCOME: The district court's ruling granting defendant's motion was reversed and vacated; the matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

 

58 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Quantum Res. Mgmt., L.L.C v. Pirate Lake Oil Corp.


No. 2012-C-1472


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-1472 (La. 03/19/13); 112 So. 3d 209; 2013 La. LEXIS 570



March 19, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Haydel v. Zodiac Corp., 187 L. Ed. 2d 45, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 5623 (U.S., 2013)
Appeal after remand at, Costs and fees proceeding at Quantum Res. Mgmt., L.L.C. v. Pirate Lake Oil Corp., L.L.C., 2013 La. App. LEXIS 2188 (La.App. 5 Cir., Oct. 30, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
Quantum Res. Mgmt., L.L.C. v. Pirate Lake Oil Corp., 98 So. 3d 394, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 750 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Record landowner sought review of a decision from the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson, Louisiana, which affirmed a district court's decision to grant summary judgment in a concursus proceeding filed by plaintiff oil, gas, and mineral interest owners.


OVERVIEW: The case involved a 1925 tax sale where there was a failure to give notice of the pending tax sale to the property owner. The district court found that the tax sale was an absolute nullity and dismissed the landowner's claim based on a violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV under Mennonite Board of Missions v. Adams. The appellate court affirmed. In reversing, the supreme court determined that Mennonite could not have been applied retroactively to invalidate the instant 1925 tax sale for lack of adequate notice. Under the United States Supreme Court's retroactivity jurisprudence, a new rule of constitutional law announced by the Court applied to all future cases and cases pending on direct review on the date the Court's decision was rendered. Further, retroactivity was limited by the doctrines of res judicata and statutes of limitations or repose. The instant case was not pending on direct review at the time Mennonite was decided, and a suit to annul the tax sale was perempted fifty-three years before Mennonite. Summary judgment was inappropriate because there were genuine issues of material fact regarding ownership of the disputed property.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower courts were reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.


 

59 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Oliphant


NO. 2012-K-1176


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-1176 (La. 03/09/13); 113 So. 3d 165; 2013 La. LEXIS 568



March 19, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at State v. Oliphant, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 974 (La.App. 2 Cir., Apr. 9, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF MOREHOUSE.
State v. Oliphant, 93 So. 3d 603, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 360 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, SENTENCE VACATED, and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to vehicular homicide under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:32.1. The district court sentenced him to 25 years at hard labor, with the first fifteen years without benefit of probation, parole, or suspension of sentence. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana affirmed the conviction, reversed the sentence, and remanded the case for resentencing. The state supreme court granted a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: In a vehicular homicide case, defendant drove his SUV in an extremely intoxicated state and struck the victim with sufficient force to kill upon impact. The offense of vehicular homicide fit the definition of a crime of violence under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2, because it required (1) the use of physical force; (2) the substantial risk that force would be used against another person; and (3) the use of a dangerous weapon. Defendant's vehicle was a multi-ton instrumentality likely to produce death or great bodily harm, and therefore, a dangerous weapon. Because vehicular homicide was crime of violence, defendant was required to serve 85% of his sentence before becoming eligible for parole pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. § 15:574.4(B)(1).


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, the sentence was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

60 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Overstreet


No. 12-KA-1854


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


12-1854 (La. 03/19/13); 111 So. 3d 308; 2013 La. LEXIS 566



March 19, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Honorable Donald R. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had been found not guilty by reason of insanity of attempted aggravated rape in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana). After undergoing 14 years of treatment, defendant asked for a determination that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:541(7) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 were unconstitutional. The district court declared the statutes unconstitutional, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was diagnosed as schizophrenic and treated with antipsychotic drugs for 14 years. During that time he professed no memory of his attacks on the two victims and refused to participate in sex offender treatment. He contended that the registration requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:541(7) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:542 were unconstitutional as applied to one found not guilty by reason of insanity. The district court decided that these statutes were unconstitutional based on its decision that a person found not guilty by reason of insanity lacked capacity to follow the registration requirements. This was not one of the grounds raised by defendant. The court held that the district court erred in ruling based on grounds other than those asserted by defendant because the sua sponte grounds were not adequately briefed and argued.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court.

 

61 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



TIN, Inc. v. Wash. Parish Sheriff's Office


NO. 12-C-2056


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


12-2056 (La. 03/19/13); 112 So. 3d 197; 2013 La. LEXIS 577



March 19, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF WASHINGTON.
Tin, Inc. v. Wash. Parish Sheriff's Office, 97 So. 3d 1105, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 936 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A taxpayer sought review by writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana) of a judgment affirming the district court's dismissal of the taxpayer's petition for review of a tax collector's denial of refund requests.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer requested a refund of use taxes alleged to have been inadvertently paid on raw material purchases. The tax collector denied the request without stating any reasons. The taxpayer submitted further requests adding a second raw material and more tax years. After failing to respond to a second and third request, the collector denied a fourth request. The taxpayer requested a redetermination hearing within 30 days of the denial and promptly filed suit after the collector declined to reconsider the denial. The court held that the taxpayer was not limited under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:337.63(A)(1)(a), 47:337.77(F), 47:1576(A), 47:1621(F) to the protest procedure as its remedy under La. Const. art. VII, § 3(A) because the collector had not informed the taxpayer of the amount due or of any interpretation of law precluding a refund. The collector's failure to act made the time periods for appeals and requests for redetermination under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:1625, 47:337.81(A) inapplicable, except as to the fourth request, on which the taxpayer timely acted. The taxpayer timely requested a refund under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:337.79, 47:1623 and thus could pursue its suit.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the lower courts and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.


 

62 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lewis


NO. 2012-K-1021


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-1021 (La. 03/19/13); 112 So. 3d 796; 2013 La. LEXIS 567



March 19, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ denied by State v. Lewis, 171 So. 3d 252, 2015 La. LEXIS 1429 (La., 2015)
On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Lewis, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 2460 (La.App. 4 Cir., Dec. 29, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Lewis, 96 So. 3d 1165, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 469 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of second degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1 and sentenced to life imprisonment at hard labor. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences. Defendant again appealed.


OVERVIEW: In an alleged act of retaliation, defendant fired shots into the victim's home, striking and killing two victims. A survivor identified defendant as one of the shooters. Before he died, the victim told witnesses that defendant shot him. During jury voir dire, defense counsel attempted to use a back strike under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 799.1, but the district court refused, advising that it only permitted back strikes on a "per panel" basis. In rebuffing defendant's attempt to peremptorily back strike the juror (provisionally selected as a juror from the first voir dire panel) at the end of the fourth panel, but before the jury panel was sworn in as a whole, the district court violated art. 799.1. The court concluded that a harmless error analysis applied, but that the court of appeal had misapplied it; the State had the burden of showing that the jury's verdicts were surely unattributable to the presence of the juror. Given that the verdicts were less than unanimous and the objectionable juror was identified before jury selection was concluded, the State failed to meet this burden.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeal, vacated defendant's convictions and sentences, and remanded the matter to the district court for a new trial.

State v. La. Land & Exploration Co.

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA

January 30, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State v. La. Land & Exploration Co., 2013 La. LEXIS 898 (La., Apr. 26, 2013)
Writ denied by State v. La. Land & Exploration Co., 2015 La. LEXIS 882 (La., Mar. 27, 2015)
Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. La. Land & Exploration Co., 2015 La. LEXIS 925 (La., Mar. 27, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF VERMILION.
State v. La. Land & Exploration Co., 85 So. 3d 158, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 102 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2012)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant oil companies filed a writ seeking review of two rulings from the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), which reversed the trial court's partial summary judgments limiting plaintiff landowners' potential recovery of damages for alleged pollution and dismissing one of the oil companies.


OVERVIEW: The petition alleged that oil and gas exploration and production under a mineral lease had polluted the owners' property. During discovery, one of the companies admitted responsibility under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:29(C) for environmental damage and moved to refer the case to the Louisiana Department of Natural Resources to develop a remediation plan. The court held that pursuant to § 30:29(H), the landowners were not precluded from receiving an award in addition to the remediation damages that would be paid into court to fund the plan under § 30:29(D)(1). As a procedural statute, § 30:29 did not limit the substantive rights of landowners arising out of either the implied obligation to repair or restore a thing leased under La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 2683, 2686, 2687, 2692 or the implied remediation obligation arising out of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 31:122 where a mineral lessee acted unreasonably or excessively. Determinations regarding those implied obligations, as well as tort claims arising under La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 2315, were for the finder of fact. The dismissal of one company was improper because a genuine issue of material fact existed as to its alleged successor status.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed both rulings of the court of appeal and remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

64 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


La. High Sch. Ath. Ass'n v. State


No. 2012-CA-1471


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-1471 (La. 01/29/13); 107 So. 3d 583; 2013 La. LEXIS 247



January 29, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE TODD W. HERNANDEZ, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in Part; Reversed in Part; Rendered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Louisiana High School Athletic Association (LHSAA) said La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:176(F) and (G), 17:236.3, 24:513(J)(4)(a) and (b), and 24:513(A)(1)(b)(v) were unconstitutional, and the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), partly granted its summary judgment motion. Defendants, the State of Louisiana and the Louisiana State Board of Elementary and Secondary Education (BESE), and LHSAA, appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 17:176(F), 17:176(G), and 17:236.3 violated La. Const. art. III, § 12. The supreme court held the statutes were not local laws because they were not limited to some localities. They were special laws because (1) they did not apply to all Louisiana athletic associations doing the same function as the LHSAA, and (2) they concerned prohibited subject matter by amending a private corporate charter. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 24:513(A)(1)(b)(v) did not apply to the LHSAA because it was not subject to the Open Meetings Law, La. Rev. Stat. § 42:11 et seq., as no public entity formed it. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 24:513(J)(4)(a) violated equal protection because (1) it treated LHSAA differently from similar groups by subjecting it to the Louisiana Legislative Auditor's authority based on the BESE's decision to adopt its scholastic rules, and (2) it furthered no legitimate state interest, as the state had no such interest in looking at LHSAA's finances, nor was it rationally related to this interest. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 24:513(J)(4)(b) was unconstitutional because it was not severable from La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 24:513(J)(4)(a).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment granting summary judgment was affirmed, and the trial court's judgment denying summary judgment was reversed.

 

65 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Prejean v. Barousse


No. 2012-C-1177


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2012-1177 (La. 01/29/13); 107 So. 3d 569; 2013 La. LEXIS 236



January 29, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ACADIA.
Prejean v. Barousse, 90 So. 3d 477, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 291 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother sought a writ of mandamus against respondents court clerk and state, seeking to enforce La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4210 and withhold part of a trial judge's salary for failing to issue judgment within 30 days from the close of trial. The trial court denied the petition, and the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Acadia, Louisiana, affirmed, holding on its own motion that § 13:4210 was unconstitutional. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The last day of trial in the underlying child custody proceeding was March 18, 2011. When the district judge court did not render judgment within thirty days, as required by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4207, the mother filed her writ. The mother argued that the court of appeal was not procedurally correct in raising the issue of constitutionality on its own motion. The court noted that there was an exception to this rule if a statute was unconstitutional on its face. In this case, the statute was unconstitutional on its face. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4210 ran afoul of the constitutional mandate in La. Const. art. V § 25(C), granting exclusive original jurisdiction over judicial discipline to the Louisiana Supreme Court. It also conflicted with La. Const. art. V, § 21, which provided that the term of office, retirement benefits, and compensation of a judge shall not be decreased during the term for which he is elected.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was affirmed. The court decreed that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:4210 was unconstitutional and without effect.

State v. Garcia


NO. 09-KA-1578


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


09-1578 (La. 11/16/12); 108 So. 3d 1; 2012 La. LEXIS 3085



November 16, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Garcia, 2013 La. LEXIS 420 (La., Jan. 25, 2013)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Garcia v. La., 2013 U.S. LEXIS 4859 (U.S., June 24, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE EIGHTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF WEST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE J. ROBIN FREE, JUDGE.
State v. Garcia, 80 So. 3d 1150, 2011 La. LEXIS 2076 (La., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Eighteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of West Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which convicted him of first-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed after he was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death, but the supreme court affirmed, stating in part that because there was no actual conflict of interest, the district court's actions comported with applicable law and the defendant received constitutionally effective, conflict-free representation. Furthermore, any failure to fully disclose the specifics of a deal, which importantly was not effectuated until six months after trial, did not in any way undermine confidence in the outcome of defendant's trial. Accordingly, no Brady violation occurred. The sentence was proper because the jury's finding of two aggravating circumstances was supported by the evidence. One victim testified that she and the other victim, her boyfriend, were robbed of approximately $30 by defendant and his two co-conspirators, while the three men were all armed with a variety of knives, machetes, and samurai swords. She further testified she and her boyfriend were taken from where they had been sleeping, blindfolded, and then led into the woods by the three men, who all brutally raped her in front of her boyfriend.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Duheart


No. 12-KA-0085


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


12-0085 (La. 10/26/12); 125 So. 3d 1054; 2012 La. LEXIS 2896



October 26, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Duheart, 120 So. 3d 239, 2013 La. LEXIS 1306 (La., June 14, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of East Baton Rouge. Honorable Donald R. Johnson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, granted defendant's motion to suppress, because it found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:101 failed to give adequate notice to individuals that certain contemplated conduct was proscribed and failed to provide adequate standards for those charged with determining the guilt or innocence of the accused, and was therefore unconstitutionally vague. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that defendant did not challenge the constitutionality of the enactment. The district court sua sponte raised the issue of whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:101 was unconstitutionally vague and then suppressed the evidence based on a determination that it was. The district court erred in doing so. A court could not raise a constitutional question on its own because none of the parties were given an opportunity to research and fully brief the issue for the trial court. The State's remaining contention was not considered in the appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the district court for reconsideration of its ruling on the motion to suppress and further proceedings.

 

68 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Marcile v. Dauzat


No. 11-CC-1509


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


11-1509 (La. 10/16/12); 103 So. 3d 335; 2012 La. LEXIS 2706



October 16, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Marcile v. Dauzat, 2012 La. LEXIS 3521 (La., Nov. 30, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF AVOYELLES.
Marcile v. Dauzat, 85 So. 3d 99, 2012 La. LEXIS 1105 (La., 2012)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and employee, filed a writ of certiorari application, challenging the judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Avoyelles, Louisiana, finding no error in the trial court's ruling that defendants' demand for trial by jury under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105 was unconstitutional by violating the right to equal protection of plaintiffs, driver and passengers. The writ application was granted.


OVERVIEW: The employee struck a vehicle operated by the driver while he was backing an emergency fire department vehicle into a fire station. Plaintiffs filed suit, and defendants requested a trial by jury. The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion to strike the jury trial, and ordered the case be tried as a bench trial. Defendants argued plaintiffs were not denied equal protection of the law because plaintiffs had several opportunities to demand a jury trial after the city passed the resolution. The reviewing court held that the resolution passed by the city satisfied the requirement that the waiver pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(D) be a blanket waiver, waiving the right to a non-jury trial in all cases, not in a specific suit. Also, plaintiffs were afforded the opportunity to request a jury trial within ten days of service of defendants' supplemental answer pursuant to La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1733. The fact that the city's resolution was passed after the original petition was filed did not deprive plaintiffs of the opportunity to later file a motion for jury trial.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

69 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Small


No. 11-K-2796


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


11-2796 (La. 10/16/12); 100 So. 3d 797; 2012 La. LEXIS 2705



October 16, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo.
State v. Small, 78 So. 3d 825, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1386 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The supreme court granted defendant's writ application to determine whether she could be guilty of second-degree murder for leaving her two small children home alone in the middle of the night, during which time a fire broke out and one of her children died in the fire. The trial court found defendant guilty of second-degree murder and the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) affirmed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court granted the application to determine whether defendant could be guilty of second-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30.1(A)(2) for leaving her two small children home alone in the middle of the night, during which time a fire broke out and one of her children died in the fire. The supreme court reversed, finding that the conviction could not be supported because defendant's criminally negligent act of leaving her young children alone in the middle of the night was not a direct act of killing, but was instead a criminally negligent act of lack of supervision that resulted in her child's death. Defendant was instead found guilty of the lesser-included offense of negligent homicide. Because there was doubt that the legislature intended to expand second-degree murder to a case such as this one, the supreme court applied the rule of lenity to overturn defendant's conviction for second-degree murder.


OUTCOME: The lower courts' judgments were reversed and defendant was found guilty of the lesser-included offense of negligent homicide.

 

70 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Camese


No. 11-KA-2534


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


11-2534 (La. 09/12/12); 99 So. 3d 636; 2012 La. LEXIS 2267



September 12, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Criminal District Court, For the Parish of Orleans. Honorable Frank A. Marullo, Jr., Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information with distribution of cocaine. Defendant subsequently indicated, through counsel indicated that she would like to withdraw her request for a bench trial. The Criminal District Court, For the Parish of Orleans, Louisiana, granted defendant's request and declared that La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) violated the Sixth Amendment of the United States Constitution. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court had previously found that a trial judge erred in raising sua sponte the issue of whether La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) conflicted with the U.S. Constitution when defendant did not challenge the constitutionality of the jury waiver procedure contained in La. Const. art. I, § 17(A). In the present case, defendant did not challenge the constitutionality of the jury waiver procedure contained in La. Const. art. I, § 17(A). Also, no parties were given an opportunity to research and brief that issue for the trial court. Further, no parties argued the constitutionality of La. Const. art. I, § 17(A). Instead, the district court sua sponte raised the issue of whether La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) conflicted with the U.S. Constitution and then ruled. Based on the case law, the supreme court found that the district court erred in doing so.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the district court's judgment and remanded the case to the district court for further proceedings.

La. Fedn. of Teachers v. State


No. 2011-CA-2226


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2226 (La. 07/02/12); 94 So. 3d 760; 2012 La. LEXIS 1948



July 2, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE R. MICHAEL CALDWELL, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state appealed the judgment of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, (La), that found in favor of appellee teachers association and declared Act 749 of the 2010 Legislative Session, La. Rev. Stat. § 17:4041 et seq., known as the Red Tape Reduction and Local Empowerment Waiver Program, unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Act authorized the Board of Secondary and Elementary Education (BESE) to grant waivers exempting school districts and individual schools from complying with a number of statutes provided for in Title 17, the Education Code. Under the Act, a waiver could not be presented to the BESE unless a majority of the classroom teachers employed in the school, voting by secret ballot, vote in favor of inclusion of such school in the waiver request. At this point, no waiver had been granted under the Act, or even requested. The association asserted that the Act improperly delegated legislative authority to the BESE, it was a prohibited local or special law, it violated due process and equal protection and it improperly allowed the BESE to suspend law. The supreme court found that the instant case presented no justiciable controversy currently amenable to resolution by this court. The association failed to demonstrate any real hardship requiring pre-enforcement review of the statute. It was not certain that a waiver would be requested or granted under the statute, and the association would not be harmed by declining review of the statute at this point in time.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

State v. Williams


No. 2011-KA-0958


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-0958 (La. 07/02/12); 94 So. 3d 770; 2012 La. LEXIS 1968



July 2, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE DONALD R. JOHNSON, JUDGE.
State v. Williams, 57 So. 3d 611, 2011 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 70 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2011)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for second degree murder. He filed a motion to quash the indictment, contending that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 404(B) was a special or local law prohibited by La. Const. art. III, § 12. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), granted defendant's motion, and the State appealed. The court of appeal transferred the appeal to the court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 404(B), which provides that the judicial administrator of the 19th Judicial District Court shall perform the function of jury commission in East Baton Rouge Parish, was a special or local law prohibited by La. Const. art. III, § 12. In granting the motion to quash, the trial court refused to declare the article unconstitutional, but nevertheless quashed the indictment based on the underlying unconstitutionality of the article. The court determined this was a substantive declaration of unconstitutionality, so that the case was within the court's jurisdiction under La. Const. art. V, § 5(d). The court determined that because defendant neither alleged nor proved that the subject article had any serious effect on his rights, he lacked standing to challenge the constitutionality of the article. He failed to show that the circumstances of his indictment would have been any different had the grand jury selection process been conducted by a jury commission, rather than by the judicial administrator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's granting of defendant's motion to quash his indictment, and remanded to that court for further proceedings.

State v. Trosclair


NO. 2011-KA-2302


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2302 (La. 05/08/2012); 89 So. 3d 340; 2012 La. LEXIS 1315



May 8, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE ROSS P. LADART, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: WRIT GRANTED; JUDGMENT OF THE COURT OF APPEAL REVERSED; JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion challenging the retroactive application of the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:561.2 as a violation of the Ex Post Facto Clause. The district court denied the motion, but the Court of Appeal of Louisiana granted writs and found the amendment could not be applied retroactively to defendant. The State appealed to the state supreme court in accordance with La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to sexual battery of a child, for which he was sentenced to 36 months' imprisonment at hard labor without benefit. Shortly after his incarceration, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:561.2 was amended to provide for lifetime supervision. Upon his release from custody, defendant was placed under lifelong supervision in accordance with the amended provision. The Supreme Court of Louisiana held that the amended supervised release provisions were predominantly nonpunitive in both intent and effect; and therefore, their retroactive application to defendant did not offend the Ex Post Facto Clauses of U.S. Const. art. I, §§ 9, 10 and La. Const. art. I, § 23.


OUTCOME: The State's application for supervisory writ was granted, the judgment of the court of appeal was reversed, and the district court's judgment was reinstated.
