ANR Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n


No. 2011-C-2078


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2078 (La. 05/08/12); 94 So. 3d 734; 2012 La. LEXIS 1311; 179 Oil & Gas Rep. 738



May 8, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Judgment entered by Martin v. ANR Pipeline Co., 93 So. 3d 575, 2012 La. LEXIS 1313 (La., May 8, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
ANR Pipeline Co. Tenn. Gas Pipeline Co. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 76 So. 3d 521, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 987 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; EXCEPTION OF NO RIGHT OF ACTION IS OVERRULED; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant local assessors sought certiorari review of a decision from the Court of Appeal, First Circuit (Louisiana), which upheld the district court's dismissal of their cross-claims and reconventional demands/cross-appeals in a suit brought by appellee taxpayers for judicial review of the ad valorem taxes assessed against the taxpayers' natural gas pipelines.


OVERVIEW: In accordance with a court order on remand, the Louisiana Tax Commission (LTC) obtained the assessors' assistance in reappraising and reassessing the taxpayers' pipelines, which were public service properties as defined in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851(M). The court held that because the LTC had a constitutional and statutory duty to appraise, value, and assess the pipeline properties as provided in La. Const. art. VII, § 18(D) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:1853, 47:1957(A), the reassessments were central assessments, not local assessments. Obtaining the assistance of assessors, even when pursuant to a court order, did not constitute a delegation of the LTC's authority to the assessors relative to the assessment of the public service properties. Accordingly, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1856 governed the taxpayers' rights in the proceedings. The court concluded that the assessors could challenge the LTC's final determination of the reassessment valuations on cross-appeal, notwithstanding case law that precluded assessors from initiating such challenges, because the assessors did not initiate the action; rather, the taxpayers amended their pleadings to join the assessors as defendants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a ruling that the reassessments were central assessments, reversed the dismissal of the assessors' cross-claims and reconventional demands/cross-appeals, overruled the taxpayers' exception of no right of action, and remanded to the district court for further proceedings.


 

75 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Trascher v. Territo


No. 2011-CC-2093


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2093 (La. 05/08/12); 89 So. 3d 357; 2012 La. LEXIS 1316



May 8, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRIT TO THE CIVIL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS.
Trascher v. Territo, 76 So. 3d 1187, 2011 La. LEXIS 3148 (La., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, an employer and its insurer, sought review of an order from the Civil District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which denied their motion to strike the deposition testimony of a deceased employee in a wrongful death and survival action brought by plaintiffs, the employee's wife and daughters.


OVERVIEW: The employee sought an ex parte order to perpetuate his testimony, alleging that he had been diagnosed with asbestosis and that it was unlikely that he would survive more than six months. The trial court granted the ex parte order. After 15 minutes of direct examination by his attorney, the employee indicated he was too fatigued to continue. He died eight days later. Plaintiffs brought a wrongful death and survival action against defendants. The trial court denied defendants' motion to strike the deposition, ruling that it could be read at trial. On appeal, the court held that the employee's testimony was inadmissible as a deposition under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1450 because defendants did not have the opportunity to cross-examine him. The employee's testimony was inadmissible as a dying declaration under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 804(B)(2) because the deposition was not taken when he believed his death was "imminent," but was scheduled because his doctor attested that he might not survive for more than six months. His testimony was admissible, however, under La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(3) because it was a statement of his then existing state of mind and physical condition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed in part and reversed in part. The only portion of the employee's deposition that would be admissible at trial was the part that met the requirements of La. Code Evid. Ann. art. 803(3). The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.


 

76 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic


No. 2011-C-2132 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 2011-C-2139 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 2011-C-2142


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2132 (La. 03/13/12); 85 So. 3d 39; 2012 La. LEXIS 506



March 13, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU.
Oliver v. Magnolia Clinic, 71 So. 3d 1170, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 1013 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; AFFIRMED IN PART. TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a nurse practitioner, her insurer, the clinic she owned and operated, and the Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund (PCF), sought review of an order from the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which held that the cap enunciated in the Louisiana Medical Malpractice Act (MMA), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B), was unconstitutional to the extent it included nurse practitioners within its ambit.


OVERVIEW: The parents brought a medical malpractice action against petitioners, claiming that the nurse's delayed diagnosis and treatment of their child caused the severity of her injuries. The trial court reduced the jury's award in favor of the parents to comply with § 40:1299.42(B). The court of appeals reversed the trial court's judgment and held that the cap in § 40:1299.42(B) was unconstitutional to the extent it included nurse practitioners within its ambit. On review, the court held that the cap in § 40:1299.42(B) was constitutional and applied to all health care providers under the MMA, including nurse practitioners. The court of appeals did not err in upholding an award of pretrial medical and related benefits outside of those awarded by the jury. Including the word "past" in the judgment did not result in a double recovery for the parents. Rather, the term merely reiterated what was already contemplated in the definition of "future medical care and related benefits" in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.43(B)(1)(a) and (b). The court of appeals did not err in upholding an award of judicial interest to the parents on past medical expenses paid by Medicaid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals with regard to its holding that § 40:1299.42(B), was unconstitutional. The trial court judgment was reinstated in full. The court affirmed the remainder of the judgment of the court of appeals.


 

77 of 2253 DOCUMENTS



McLane S., Inc. v. Bridges


NO. 11-C-1141


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


11-1141 (La. 01/24/12); 84 So. 3d 479; 2012 La. LEXIS 101



January 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at McLane Southern, Inc. v. Bridges, 2013 La. App. LEXIS 762 (La.App. 1 Cir., Mar. 21, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
McLane Southern, Inc. v. Bridges, 64 So. 3d 886, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 614 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer, a wholesale dealer of smokeless tobacco products, filed a petition for a refund of an excise tax it paid under protest pursuant to the Tobacco Tax Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:841 et seq. The district court granted appellee Department of Taxation's motion for summary judgment, dismissing the claim. The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), reversed. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal held that the taxpayer and all other tobacco dealers were not liable for the tobacco tax on smokeless tobacco products under the provisions of the Tobacco Tax Law. It held the other issues surrounding the interpretation of the invoice price and the constitutionality of the definition of invoice price were moot given its determination that the taxpayer was not liable for the tax. However, the court of appeal erred in its determination. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:841 and 47:854 imposed an excise tax of 20 percent on smokeless tobacco products to be paid by the dealer who first sold, used, consumed, handled, or distributed the product in Louisiana. The statutory wording and the intent of the legislature were clear, yet the legislature did not correctly draft and amend all the necessary sections of the statutory scheme to reflect that intent. Because the language and intent of both statutes was clear, the statutes were read to impose an excise tax on smokeless tobacco products. Because the finding that the taxpayer did not owe the excise tax was reversed, remand was necessary to consider the two pretermitted issues.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal and remanded the case to the court of appeal for a determination of all pretermitted issues.


 

78 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carter


No. 2010-KA-0614


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-0614 (La. 01/24/12); 84 So. 3d 499; 2012 La. LEXIS 108



January 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Carter v. La., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 7095 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF RED RIVER. HONORABLE LEWIS O. SAMS, JUDGE.
State v. Carter, 10 So. 3d 720, 2009 La. LEXIS 2094 (La., 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Red River (Louisiana) of first degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred in permitting the withdrawal of his motion for new trial without first appointing a sanity commission to determine defendant's competence under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 643. The supreme court disagreed. Defendant did not show the existence of any mental disease or defect that could diminish his capacity to understand the proceedings against him or assist in his defense. Defendant's answers were articulate, cogent, and indicated that he fully comprehended the rights he was foregoing, and the gravity of withdrawing the motion. Because the trial court's interview established that defendant clearly had the capacity to understand the proceedings against him and to assist in his defense, the trial court did not err in failing to appoint a sanity commission to determine defendant's competence. Defendant also failed to demonstrate that counsel labored under an actual conflict of interest under U.S. Const. amend. VI because, although counsel was under investigation by a different prosecutor, the pending charges against counsel were not related in any way to the murder charge against defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

79 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Arshad v. City of Kenner


No. 2011-CC-1579 CONSOLIDATED WITH No. 2011-CC-1814


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-1579 (La. 01/24/12); 95 So. 3d 477; 2012 La. LEXIS 20



January 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by Arshad v. Congemi, 2014 La. App. LEXIS 2579 (La.App. 5 Cir., Oct. 29, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
Arshad v. City of Kenner, 74 So. 3d 712, 2011 La. LEXIS 2513 (La., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff family filed a negligence action against defendants, a city, a police department, the chief and certain police officers, and two insurers. The trial court granted the city's request for a jury trial, finding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105(D) permitted the city to waive the prohibition against jury trials on a case-by-case basis. The Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), reversed. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The family alleged that police officers falsely arrested the decedent, subjecting her to unnecessary force and battery, and improperly left decedent unattended in a police car, where she died. The family's petition requested trial by jury, but the family later moved to strike the jury demand. The following day, the city council enacted a resolution, pursuant to § 13:5105(D), waiving the prohibition against jury trials in this specific case and filed a request for a jury trial. The court of appeals held that the resolution was a prohibited special law because it waived the prohibition against jury trials only in this single case. The supreme court, applying different reasoning, found that the plain language of § 13:5105(D) did not permit a political subdivision to waive the prohibition against jury trials in a single case. Furthermore, the political subdivision's insurer was not entitled to trial by jury where the political subdivision had not waived the prohibition, and the insurer's liability was vicarious, not independent. Therefore, in suits against a political subdivision and its insurer where there were no other nongovernmental defendants, a bifurcated trial was unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

80 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bazile


No. 2011-KK-2201


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-2201 (La. 01/24/12); 85 So. 3d 1; 2012 La. LEXIS 17



January 24, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Bazile, 144 So. 3d 719, 2013 La. LEXIS 1082 (La., May 7, 2013)
Writ denied by, As moot State v. Bazile, 2017 La. App. LEXIS 886 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 18, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON SUPERVISORY WRITS TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
State v. Bazille, 74 So. 3d 728, 2011 La. LEXIS 2497 (La., Oct. 14, 2011)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for second degree murder; he waived his right to trial by jury. However, the State objected, noting that under La. Const. art. I, § 17, the defendant was required to make the waiver 45 days prior to the trial date. The 19th Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), found that defendant could waive a jury trial at any time before trial and that the time limit was unconstitutional. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the district court could not refuse to enforce a law on the grounds that the district court on its own motion found the law unconstitutional. The district judge lacked standing to raise a constitutional challenge to the laws the judge was charged by judicial oath to enforce. The district court owed an equal duty to apply and enforce a presumptively constitutional legislative act as it did the state constitution. The district court therefore erred in declaring that the jury waiver procedure described in La. Const. art. I, § 17(A) was unconstitutional without the issue being properly raised by the parties. Additionally, because the parties did not themselves raise and brief the issue, the record was not fully developed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Simmons


No. 11-K-1280


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


11-1280 (La. 01/20/12); 78 So. 3d 743; 2012 La. LEXIS 8



January 20, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Simmons, 85 So. 3d 743, 2012 La. App. LEXIS 183 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 15, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
IN RE: State of Louisiana; - Plaintiff; Applying For Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of Orleans, Criminal District Court Div. E, No. 491-760; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, No. 2010-KA-1508;
State v. Simmons, 67 So. 3d 525, 2011 La. App. LEXIS 618 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2011)



DISPOSITION: Granted.

DECISION OF THE COURT OF APPEAL REVERSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of cocaine with intent to distribute. The State filed notice under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:501(A) of its intent to introduce the crime lab's certificate of analysis as prima facie evidence that individually wrapped objects police officers observed defendant discard contained cocaine. The State challenged a judgment of the Fourth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana), which reversed defendant's conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant opposed the State's notice just before jury election was to begin. The State notified the trial court that the analyst who conducted the testing worked for a crime lab located in another parish and was not immediately available. The trial court denied defendant's objection as untimely. The court of appeal ruled that introduction of the crime lab report, as opposed to presenting live testimony from the analyst, violated defendant's Sixth Amendment right to confront the witnesses against him. The supreme court held that the trial court properly admitted the analyst's certificate in lieu of the analyst's live testimony under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:500. Defendant waived his Sixth Amendment right of confrontation by failing to timely request a subpoena for the analyst who performed the test on the rocks of cocaine. States remained free to impose reasonable restrictions on a defendant's assertion of his or her confrontation rights. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in failing to issue an instanter subpoena for the out-of-parish criminalist at the risk of delaying a one-day trial after defendant failed to timely request that a subpoena issue for the witness.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision of the court of appeal and remanded the case to that court.

 

82 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan


NO. 2011-C-0097


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-0097 (La. 12/16/11); 79 So. 3d 987; 2011 La. LEXIS 3014



December 16, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Rehearing denied by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan (Parish of Jefferson), 2012 La. LEXIS 12 (La., Jan. 20, 2012)
Subsequent appeal at, Application granted by Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 85 So. 3d 73, 2012 La. LEXIS 908 (La., 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by La. Citizens Prop. Ins. Corp. v. Oubre, 133 S. Ct. 30, 183 L. Ed. 2d 677, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 4758 (U.S., 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIFTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.
Oubre v. La. Citizens Fair Plan, 53 So. 3d 492, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1554 (La.App. 5 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; DISTRICT COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a class action, the district court granted summary judgment to plaintiff insureds for penalties provided by former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:658(A)(3) arising out of defendant insurer's failure to timely initiate loss adjustment on the enumerated class members' insurance claims. The insurer appealed. The Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), reversed. The insureds appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal held that a factual determination of whether the insurer breached its duty of good faith was required before assessing penalties under § 22:658(A)(3). The supreme court granted the writ of certiorari to resolve a split in the circuits regarding the proof necessary to award penalties for failure to timely initiate loss adjustment under § 22:658(A)(3) and, correspondingly, former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(C). The plain language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:2658(A)(3) did not require a showing of bad faith by the insurer, but simply required proof of notice and inaction for over 30 days. Therefore, because no genuine issue of material fact existed regarding whether the insurer timely initiated loss adjustment, summary judgment in favor of the insureds was appropriate. Furthermore, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1220(C) capped the penalties for such inaction at five thousand dollars when damages were not proven. Accordingly, the district court did not err in awarding each individual insured five thousand dollars in statutory penalties, subject to a credit in the insurer's favor for those insureds who executed binding releases or opted out of the class.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal and reinstated the district court's judgment.

State v. Odenbaugh


NO. 10-KA-0268


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


10-0268 (La. 12/6/11); 82 So. 3d 215; 2011 La. LEXIS 2888



December 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Odenbaugh, 2012 La. LEXIS 11 (La., Jan. 20, 2012)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Odenbaugh v. La., 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6958 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTH DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF OUACHITA. HONORABLE CARL VAN SHARP, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Fourth District Court for the Parish of Ouacita, Louisiana, that convicted him of two counts of first-degree murder and one count of attempted first-degree murder and that imposed the death penalty, arguing that the trial court erred in granting the State's challenge for cause to a juror who was against the death penalty and in admitting into evidence during the penalty phase letters he wrote while in prison.


OVERVIEW: Following a domestic dispute, defendant shot his wife, his mother-in-law, and his stepdaughter; only his stepdaughter survived. On review, the court held that the juror was properly excused for cause under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 798 on the basis that she was unable to consider rendering a death verdict. The juror clearly stated that she would automatically vote for a life sentence if defendant was found guilty of first-degree murder and would not consider the possibility of the death sentence because that she believed a life sentence would cause defendant to suffer more. Further, letters in which defendant implicitly admitted to shooting his stepdaughter and expressed a desire to escape from jail and "finish the job" or to hire a hitman to do so were relevant and admissible under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.2 in the penalty phase of trial to prove defendant's character. Despite the fact that there was no evidence that defendant took any steps, beyond mailing the letters, to carry out the plans described, defendant's statements in both letters were directly relevant to the defendant's character and violent propensities, even while confined by the prison walls.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed.

 

84 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rochon


No. 2011-KA-0009


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2011-0009 (La. 10/25/11); 75 So. 3d 876; 2011 La. LEXIS 2595



October 25, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS. HONORABLE FRANK A. MARULLO, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When defendant failed to appear at an arraignment, the State requested that an arrest warrant be issued pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 496. The warrant was issued and an indigent defender subsequently challenged its issuance and the constitutionality of art. 496. The Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) found the article unconstitutional and recalled the warrant. The State sought review.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant eventually appeared in court and the State entered a nolle prosequi, the issue was ripe for review, the matter was capable of repetition, yet evaded review, and the appeal presented a justiciable question. In the indigent defender's written motion, the district court was asked to deny the State's request for the arrest warrant absent a judicial determination of probable cause. The district court erred in declaring art. 496 unconstitutional under U.S. Const. amends. IV and XIV, and La. Const. art. I, § 5 because the district court could have instead adopted a narrowing construction of the article. Although art. 496 did not expressly require a judicial determination of probable cause before a warrant was issued, the general requirements for issuing an arrest warrant under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 202 applied. Articles 202 and 496 should have been read in pari materia, such that an arrest warrant could have issued upon the basis of a bill of information only if an affidavit filed with the information showed probable cause for the arrest. Accordingly, art. 496 was constitutional under the narrow construction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

Silver Dollar Liquor, Inc. v. Red River Parish Police Jury


NO. 2010-C-2776


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-2776 (La. 09/07/11); 74 So. 3d 641; 2011 La. LEXIS 1909



September 7, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RED RIVER.
Silver Dollar Liquor, Inc. v. Red River Parish Police Jury, 56 So. 3d 265, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 1584 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff liquor store owner filed a declaratory judgment action against defendant Parish Police Jury seeking to have Red River Parish, La. Code § 3-18 declared invalid. The Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Red River (Louisiana), found in favor of the Police Jury. Because the decision created a split in the circuits, the owner's writ of application was granted to resolve the split.


OVERVIEW: Section 3-18 prohibited the Sunday sale of alcoholic beverages. The owner alleged that § 3-18 was invalid because there had never been a local option election in the district pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:191. However, the Police Jury had authority under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 to regulate the sale of alcoholic beverages. Red River Parish, La. Code § 3-18 was valid. The Police Jury had the power under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 to regulate the sale of alcohol, even if the sale occurred on Sundays. To the extent Red River Parish, La. Code § 3-18 was impacted by both La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 26:493 and 51:191, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:493 was the more specific statute, and thus controlling. The parish had the authority to disallow Sunday alcohol sales under § 26:493.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State v. Jones


NO. 2010-K-0762


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-0762 (La. 09/07/11); 74 So. 3d 197; 2011 La. LEXIS 1908



September 7, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RAPIDES.
State v. Jones, 32 So. 3d 1084, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 359 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; JURY VERDICT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of forcible rape, violations of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42.1, and indecent behavior with a juvenile, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81(A)(1). The jury found him not guilty on both rape counts, but guilty of attempted indecent behavior under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:27. Defendant appealed. The Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) reversed. The State's writ application was granted.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile victim went into a bedroom where defendant was located, asked defendant for a ride to the store, and defendant told him he would do it if the victim put his penis in defendant's mouth. Defendant was the assistant chief of police, an authoritative figure, and the request was made in the bedroom of a transvestite who was present and who also made lewd requests of the victim. If the victim had acquiesced in this intimidating environment, the crime would have completed. A rational trier of fact could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant's conduct constituted attempt to commit indecent behavior with a juvenile. In reviewing the evidence and the totality of the facts and circumstances, a rational jury could have found beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant committed an act for the purpose of and tending directly toward the accomplishing of indecent behavior with a juvenile. While most other crimes required an overt physical act in order for an attempt to occur, the completed crime of indecent behavior with a juvenile was accomplished by the mere communication of lewd or lascivious conduct, text, or images.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal and reinstated the jury verdict.

 

87 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Golston


NO. 2010-KA-2804


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-2804 (La. 07/01/11); 67 So. 3d 452; 2011 La. LEXIS 1595



July 1, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 15, 2011.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE BONNIE FOSTER JACKSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In five consolidated criminal cases involving convicted sex offenders, defendants underwent the Sex Offender Assessment Panel (SOAP) process under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:560 et seq. Following a hearing, the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:560 et seq. unconstitutional. The State filed a motion for direct appeal pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: The district court found La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:560 et seq. to be unconstitutionally vague, and held that the statutory definitions of "child sexual predator" (CSP), "sexually violent predator" (SVP), and "mental abnormality" were circular and insufficient guideposts for both the offenders and panel members. Additionally, the district court concluded that the penalties imposed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:560.3 were deprivations to the offender's liberty and property that had to meet the requirements of due process at both the panel hearings and court hearings. However, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:560 et seq. was a regulatory, rather than criminal statutory scheme, and, therefore, was not subject to a void for vagueness analysis. Further, even applying a due process analysis, the SOAP statutory scheme did not violate due process. The SOAP statutory scheme provided offenders with notice and a meaningful opportunity to be heard at a court hearing to determine SVP or CSP status. Finally, the statutory definitions were constitutionally sufficient to allow the panel to make its recommendation and the court to make a determination of SVP or CSP status.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the district court's finding, and remanded for further proceedings.

Gathen v. Gathen


No. 2010-CJ-2312


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-2312 (La. 05/10/11); 66 So. 3d 1; 2011 La. LEXIS 1121



May 10, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 1, 2011.
Rehearing denied by Gathen v. Gathen, 2011 La. LEXIS 1666 (La., July 1, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LAFOURCHE.
Gathen v. Gathen, 46 So. 3d 283, 2010 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 525 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The supreme court granted the father's writ application to determine the appropriate standard of review of a trial court's decision in a child relocation case. The Court of Appeals (Louisiana) found that a de novo review of the record was necessary.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court granted the father's writ application to determine the appropriate standard of review of a trial court's decision in a child relocation case when the trial court did not expressly analyze each factor under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:355.12 in determining whether relocation was in the best interest of the child. The supreme court reversed the appellate court's determination and found that while § 9:355.12 mandated that the trial court consider all 12 factors listed, its failure to expressly each factor in its written or oral reasons did not constitute an error of law such that de novo review was appropriate. Where the trial court had considered the factors listed under § 9:355.12 in determining whether relocation was in the best interest of the child or children, that determination was reviewed for abuse of discretion. Utilizing the correct standard, there was no abuse of discretion in the trial court's decision to deny the mother's relocation request. Thus, the supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated the trial court's judgment denying relocation.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the appellate court's judgment and reinstated the trial court's judgment denying relocation.

State v. Sparks


NO. 1988-KA-0017


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


1988-0017 (La. 05/10/11); 68 So. 3d 435; 2011 La. LEXIS 1122



May 10, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Sparks, 2011 La. LEXIS 1898 (La., Sept. 2, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by El-Mumit v. Louisiana, 566 U.S. 908, 132 S. Ct. 1794, 182 L. Ed. 2d 621, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 2358 (Mar. 26, 2012)
Writ granted by State v. Sparks, 2016 La. App. LEXIS 846 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 2, 2016)
Decision reached on appeal by, Motion granted by State v. Sparks, 2017 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 56 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 17, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF LIVINGSTON. HONORABLE ROBERT H. MORRISON, III, JUDGE.
State v. Sparks, 483 So. 2d 1246, 1986 La. App. LEXIS 6112 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 14, 1986)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed under La. Const. art. V, § 5(D), from an order of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), convicting him, upon a jury's verdict, of first-degree murder, and sentencing him to death, after finding an aggravating circumstance under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.4, that the victim was a peace officer engaged in his lawful duties.


OVERVIEW: During an arrest following an armed bank robbery, defendant pulled a gun from his waist and shot and killed a sheriff's deputy. Defendant's motion to suppress his statement was properly denied because defendant failed to show that he did not make a knowing and intelligent waiver or that he was under the influence of fear and duress sufficient to vitiate voluntariness. Further, defendant failed to show that the pretrial publicity colored the jurors' voir dire responses to the point of making them unreliable or that any of the challenged jurors could not have rendered an impartial verdict based upon the law and evidence. Next, security concerns specifically related to defendant were sufficient to support the trial court's determination that the shackling of defendant was necessary during the trial. There was evidence before the court that the warden had learned that defendant and other inmates had formulated an escape plan and a shank was found in the cell of one of the inmates. With regard to the penalty phase, the court could not tell from the record the extent, if any, of counsel's investigation for mitigating evidence. Thus, remand for an evidentiary hearing was necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's first-degree murder conviction and conditionally affirmed the imposition of the death sentence, remanding to the district court for an evidentiary hearing on whether defendant received effective assistance of counsel at the penalty phase of the trial.

 

90 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Wooley v. Lucksinger


NO. 2009-C-0571, CONSOLIDATED WITH NOS. 2009-C-0584, 2009-C-0585, AND 2009-C-0586


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-0571 (La. 04/01/11); 61 So. 3d 507; 2011 La. LEXIS 706



April 1, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Wooley v. Lucksinger, 2011 La. LEXIS 1265 (La., Apr. 29, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Wooley v. Lucksinger, 14 So. 3d 311, 2008 La. App. LEXIS 1863 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, receivers of health maintenance organizations (HMOs), sued defendant, the HMOs' seller, on a guarantee and for various tort claims. The trial court and a jury awarded the receivers compensatory and punitive damages. The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) affirmed a reduction of damages for breach of the guarantee and reversed the judgments on the tort claims. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: The receivers, three states' HMO regulators, contested how the seller sold the HMOs. The supreme court held damages for breach of a guarantee were properly reduced because it only promised to fund an HMO for the minimum required by former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:2010. A breach of fiduciary duty charge was proper because (1) no instruction on former Tex. Bus. Corp. Act art. 2.21 was needed, as no shareholder was sought to be held liable for corporate acts, (2) the HMOs' directors would likely be held to owe the HMOs a fiduciary duty, and (3) the directors could be liable under Tex. Ins. Code Ann. § 843.401. A fraud charge did not fatally err because (1) former Tex. Bus. Corp. Act art. 2.21 did not apply to the seller's pre-sale acts, (2) it correctly instructed on fraud by deception, and (3) error in stating traditional fraud elements did not mislead the jury. It was proper to instruct on deceptive acts in insurance, under former Tex. Ins. Code art. 21.21, because the statute applied to the seller. A civil conspiracy charge was not defective because it did not let jurors eliminate intentional or knowing elements and required a finding of an underlying unlawful act.


OUTCOME: The court of appeal's ruling on the guarantee was affirmed, but its rulings on tort claims were reversed, and the verdict and trial court judgment were reinstated, as were compensatory and punitive damages awards. The trial court's ruling on two receivers' attorneys fees and punitive damages claims was affirmed. Its ruling reducing the seller's fault percentage was reversed. Its ruling allocating costs was reinstated and remanded.

 

91 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 10-KK-1514


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-1514 (La. 03/15/11); 60 So. 3d 1189; 2011 La. LEXIS 599



March 15, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Supervisory Writs to the Eleventh Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Sabine.
State v. Williams, 38 So. 3d 1180, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 771 (La.App. 3 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: COURT OF APPEAL DECISION REVERSED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with false swearing for purposes of violating public health or safety in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:126.1. He filed a motion to quash the bill of information, contending that § 14:126.1 was unconstitutionally vague. The motion was denied. The State challenged an order of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), which set aside that ruling and ordered the prosecution quashed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeals read the title of the statute, which referred to "false swearing," into the body of the law. It ruled that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:126 and § 14:126.1 operated in tandem, and consequently, had to be read in para materia to require in the latter case that the offender make the alleged false statement under oath or an equivalent affirmation. The supreme court held that § 14:126.1 did not require that the offender make the alleged false statement under oath or equivalent affirmation. Removing the title of § 14:126.1 as an interpretative guide to the language of the text cured any vagueness that could arise from using the term "false swearing" to describe the making or communicating of "false statements." The court of appeal erred in its analysis because § 14:126.1 did not form part of the comprehensive set of criminal laws adopted by the legislature in the Criminal Code of 1942, 1942 La. Acts 43, and which set out the crimes of perjury and false swearing, including the parallel provisions that addressed the evidentiary import of the making of subsequent statements inconsistent with a statement made under oath or equivalent affirmation.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the decision and remanded the case to the court of appeal to address the defendant's other assignments of error.

 

92 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Taranto v. La. Citizens Prop. Ins. Corp.


NO. 2010-C-0


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2019-0105 (La. 03/15/11); 62 So. 3d 721; 2011 La. LEXIS 604



March 15, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Taranto v. La. Citizens Prop. Ins. Corp., 2011 La. LEXIS 1447 (La., May 20, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
Taranto v. La. Citizens Prop. Ins. Corp., 28 So. 3d 543, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 2147 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs property owners filed a petition against defendant insurance company seeking payment of their policy limits and damages from property losses caused by hurricane Katrina. The district court granted insurance company's Exception of Prescription and dismissed the owners' claims with prejudice. The court of appeal (Louisiana) reversed. Insurance company filed a writ of certiorari, and the supreme court granted the writ application.


OVERVIEW: Insurance company argued, inter alia, argued that La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 596 did not apply to the "contractual limitations" period contained in the insurance policy because it only applied to "liberative prescription." The supreme court disagreed. The property owners were putative members of a class action who were excluded by a later class restriction. Pursuant to La. Code. Civ. Proc. art. 596, the liberative prescription that was suspended with the filing of the class action petition, commenced to run again 30 days after publication of notice of the class restriction. Since notice was provided on April 24, 2008, then, the suspended period ended on May 24, 2008, and the prescription commenced to run anew. The property owners then had until May 31, 2009 to file suit. They filed suit on June 27, 2008, and pursuant to art. 596, the suit was timely filed.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was affirmed.

Burge v. State


No. 10-C-2229


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-2229 (La. 02/11/11); 54 So. 3d 1110; 2011 La. LEXIS 283



February 11, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.

IN RE: Burge, Gerald; - Plaintiff; Applying For Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of E. Baton Rouge, 19th Judicial District Court Div. E, No. C557608; to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, No. 2010 CA 0051;
Burge v. State, 43 So. 3d 235, 2010 La. App. LEXIS 895 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Court of Appeals affirmed the district court's dismissal of plaintiff's wrongful conviction compensation application based upon the State's exception of insufficiency of service. Plaintiff sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court concluded that the appellate court erred in affirming the district court's ruling. The only relevant authority governing plaintiff's application was contained in the Wrongful Conviction Compensation Statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:572.8, which explicitly required the district court to submit the application to the Attorney General, the prosecuting district attorney, and the court that reversed the conviction. The statute set out a unique notice procedure and placed the notice requirement not on plaintiff, but on the court. So, it was fair to say that the ordinary requirements for service of petition involving claims against the State did not apply to this unique situation.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's ruling was reversed, and the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Castillo


No. 09-KK-1358


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


57 So. 3d 1012; 2011 La. LEXIS 256



January 28, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at State ex rel. Castillo v. State, 2011 La. LEXIS 2895 (La., Nov. 23, 2011)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Castillo v. Louisiana, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8740 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson.
State v. Castillo, 21 So. 3d 296, 2009 La. LEXIS 3202 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: DECREE. REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of speeding, driving with a suspended driver's license, and driving with an expired license. He twice moved the Parish Court for review of his convictions and requested the assistance of counsel; these requests were denied. The Court of Appeal, Fifth Circuit, Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana) ordered that counsel be appointed, and the Jefferson Parish Indigent Defender Board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the State was not required to provide counsel to an indigent defendant to assist in the preparation of an application for discretionary writ review following his convictions for misdemeanor traffic violations. Louisiana's interest in limiting the burden imposed on taxpayers by state-paid counsel provided a rational basis for limiting access to state-provided counsel in discretionary review of traffic and petty misdemeanor convictions. Louisiana's statutory scheme, which did not provide for court-appointed counsel in review of petty misdemeanor offenses, is an exercise of legislative choice based on difficult policy considerations and the allocation of scarce financial resources.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeal.

Deer Enters., LLC v. Parish Council of Wash. Parish


No. 2010-CA-0671


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-0671 (La. 01/19/11); 56 So. 3d 936; 2011 La. LEXIS 103



January 19, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF WASHINGTON HONORABLE REGINALD T. BADEAUX, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff retail store owner was denied a permit to sell alcoholic beverages. The owner filed suit, and the Twenty-Second Judicial District Court for the Parish of Washington (Louisiana) declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:583(C)(2) to be a local or special law in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 12(A). It also held that § 26:583(C)(2) violated the owner's equal protection rights under La. Const. art. I, § 3. Defendant parish council appealed.


OVERVIEW: Electors in Ward 3 of the parish voted to prohibit the sale of alcoholic beverages in the ward pursuant to a local-option election. Ward 8, in contrast, voted to permit the sale of alcoholic beverages. Years later, the parish adopted a home-rule charter, replacing its police-jury system with a parish council. The council district comprised parts of Wards 3 and 8. The owner's convenience store was located in a portion of Ward 3 contained in the council district. The population classification contained in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:583(C)(2) persuaded the appellate court that it was not prohibited as a local law in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 12(A). Further, although § 26:583(C)(2) had characteristics of a special law, it was not aimed at special interests and affected parish residents generally, not business owners specifically. Finally, § 26:583(C)(2) did not violate the owner's equal protection rights pursuant to La. Const. art. 1, § 3 because the amendment did not classify individuals; rather, it classified parishes.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

97 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cooper


NO. 2010-KK-2344


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2010-2344 (La. 11/16/10); 50 So. 3d 115; 2010 La. LEXIS 2373



November 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Cooper, 2010 La. LEXIS 3046 (La., Nov. 24, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LAFAYETTE.
State v. Cooper, 51 So. 3d 1, 2010 La. LEXIS 2370 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a motion for random allotment, challenging the method by which non-capital felony criminal cases were assigned in the Fifteenth Judicial District. The State sought review of a judgment of the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Lafayette (Louisiana), which reversed an order denying the motion and found that the system for allocating non-capital criminal cases violated La. Dist. Ct. app. 3, R. 14.0.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court held that the local rules at issue did not offend the uniform rules of allotment, statutes, or the constitutional rights due to a criminal defendant. The plan did not violate La. Dist. Ct. app. 3, R. 14.0. A majority of the Fifteenth Judicial District judges adopted the plan as provided in La. Dist. Ct. app. 14.0A. The judges were not in error in taking into account considerations of judicial efficiency and costs in developing the plan, as long as their method of case allotment did not otherwise violate the law. The so-called "geographical assignments" were only for the first two years of the plan's operation. Thereafter, the judges wold be assigned to the tracks district-wide on a random basis. The plan did not violate the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:502. The supreme court provided a framework in the uniform rules whereby individual judicial districts could develop a plan to randomly allot cases in a way that worked best for that district. The plan did not create a specialized criminal court. It merely provided a mechanism whereby the non-capital criminal cases were allotted to particular divisions within the district court.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment of the court of appeal.

 

98 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smalls


No. 2009-KK-2695


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-2695 (La. 10/19/10); 48 So. 3d 212; 2010 La. LEXIS 2257



October 19, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Smalls, 31 So. 3d 1056, 2010 La. LEXIS 981 (La., 2010)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND TRANSFERRED TO THE CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT TO BE RE-ALLOTTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with simple criminal damage to property. Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:1347, his case was allotted to an appointed commissioner in the criminal district court's magistrate section. After entering a plea of not guilty, he sought to declare § 13:1347 unconstitutional. Defendant's motion was denied. The Court of Appeal Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), denied defendant's writ application. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because they were not elected judges, the commissioners of the magistrate section of the criminal district court could not exercise the adjudicatory power of the State to dispose of misdemeanor cases by accepting guilty pleas or conducting trials. Furthermore, § 13:1347 did not grant to the nonelected commissioners the same adjudicatory powers of the elected magistrate judges of the criminal district court. Consequently, the criminal district court's practice of allotting misdemeanor criminal cases to the commissioners of the magistrate section of the court for accepting guilty pleas and conducting trials, violated La. Const. art. V, §§ 1 and 22. Accordingly, the scope of § 13:1347 was clarified in conformity with the state constitution to provide that the commissioners of the magistrate section of the criminal district court could not conduct trials or accept guilty pleas in misdemeanor case because they were not elected judges and the commissioners could not lawfully exercise the adjudicatory power of the State.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling, and transferred the matter to the criminal district court, which was ordered to reallot the case to a magistrate judge or another section of the criminal district court.

In re Gisclair


No. 10-C-0563


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


10-0563 (La. 09/24/10); 44 So. 3d 272; 2010 La. LEXIS 1949



September 24, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Gisclair v. La. Tax Comm'n, 49 So. 3d 878, 2010 La. LEXIS 2625 (La., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
IN RE: Louisiana Tax Commission; - Defendant; Applying For Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of E. Baton Rouge, 19th Judicial District Court Div. F, No. 579 264; to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, No. 2009 CA 2047.
Gisclair v. La. Tax Comm'n, 2010 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 296 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 12, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), a tax assessor challenged the constitutionality of the Louisiana Tax Commission's (LTC) administration of ad valorem taxes assessed against public service property. The assessor challenged the LTC's application of the tax valuation methodology set forth in La. Const. art. VII, §§ 18(D), 21(F), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 47:1853, 47:1854, 47:2321.


OVERVIEW: The LTC sought to determine the value of a company's public service property that was subject to taxation in the parish by subtracting the book value of the company's tax exempt property from the fair market value of the company's property that was subject to taxation by the parish and its various taxing and tax-recipient bodies. The substantive right at issue was the right to challenge the application of the relevant laws governing the tax valuation of public service properties. The legislature under the clear and explicit language of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1856(G) granted the right to bring an as applied challenge regarding the tax valuation of public service property solely to the public service taxpayer, and not to the assessor. Further, the assessor did not have authority to challenge the special provisions governing the assessment of public service properties under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1998(C). Therefore, because the petition failed to disclose a right of action in the assessor, the peremptory exception of no right of action was properly noticed and sustained by the court under the authority of La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 927.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ and rendered judgment sustaining the peremptory exception of no right of action noticed on the court's own motion and dismissing the assessor's petition with prejudice.

State v. Dressner


NO. 08-KA-1366


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-1366 (La. 07/06/10); 45 So. 3d 127; 2010 La. LEXIS 1656



July 6, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Dressner, 2010 La. LEXIS 3045 (La., Sept. 3, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dressner v. Louisiana, 131 S. Ct. 1605, 179 L. Ed. 2d 500, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 1966 (U.S., 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FOURTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF JEFFERSON, HONORABLE HANS J. LILJEBERG, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), which convicted him of first-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The supreme court affirmed, stating that he was not deprived of his fundamental right to present a defense under U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV, and La. Const. art. I, § 16. Nothing in the record suggested that defendant's homicidal actions were the result of immediate provocation sufficient to deprive an average person of his self-control and cool reflection. Under those circumstances, defendant failed to carry his burden of proof that such evidence was even relevant much less mitigating under La. Code Evid. Ann. arts. 402 and 403. Thus, there was no abuse of the district court's discretion in granting the State's motion in limine and the district court did not deprive defendant of his fundamental right to present a defense. Defendant's death sentence was proper because he subjected the victim to the pitiless infliction of unnecessary pain prior to death. The serious physical, mental, and emotional abuse that the victim had to have suffered moments before death amounted to torture and defendant carried out the death in a particularly inhumane manner.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Tietjen v. City of Shreveport


NO. 2009-C-2116


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-2116 (La. 05/11/10); 36 So. 3d 192; 2010 La. LEXIS 1215



May 11, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit Parish of Caddo.
Tietjen v. City of Shreveport, 17 So. 3d 17, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 825 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, property owners and their mortgagee, brought suit against defendants city and tax sale purchaser seeking to annul a tax sale. The trial court entered judgment for the owners and mortgagee, finding the tax sale null and void. The city appealed. The Court of Appeal, Second Circuit Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, reversed, finding that the notice to the owners was sufficient. The property owners and mortgagee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners purchased a lot and mortgaged it to the mortgagee. Ad valorem property taxes for 2001 were not paid. The city sold the property at tax sale to the purchaser in 2002. The property owners learned of the sale in 2006 when they attempted to sell the property. The mortgagee did not receive notice of the delinquent taxes nor notice of the pending sale. The trial court found notice of the pending sale provided to an employee of the owners' corporation was inadequate notice to the individual property owners and that the lack of proper notice to the owners and mortgagee constituted a due process violation under both federal and state constitutions. The city argued that the notice given to the employee at the property location was proper and that it was not required to send notice to the mortgagee because the bank failed to request notice pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2180.1. The court held that the court of appeal erred because it did not review the judgment under the manifest error standard of review. Because the trial court judgment holding the tax sale was null and of no effect was supported by the evidence of record, the judgment should not have been overturned.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeal is reversed and reinstated the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Montejo


NO. 2006-KA-1807


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2006-1807 (La. 05/11/10); 40 So. 3d 952; 2010 La. LEXIS 1219



May 11, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Montejo, 2010 La. LEXIS 3049 (La., June 25, 2010)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Montejo v. Louisiana, 131 S. Ct. 656, 178 L. Ed. 2d 513, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 9104 (U.S., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-SECOND JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF ST. TAMMANY, HONORABLE DONALD M. FENDLASON, JUDGE. ON REMAND FROM THE UNITED STATES SUPREME COURT.
Montejo v. Louisiana, 129 S. Ct. 2079, 173 L. Ed. 2d 955, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 3973 (U.S., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death by a jury in the trial court. The conviction was affirmed by the court on appeal. The United States Supreme Court granted defendant's writ application to consider whether a confession letter was improperly admitted. The Court overruled Michigan v. Jackson, 475 U.S. 625, 89 L.Ed.2d 631 (1986), and remanded the case for consideration of further issues.


OVERVIEW: While being taken by officers to locate evidence, defendant wrote a letter of apology and confession to the murder victim's wife in which he described details of the crime. Because the motion to suppress was made on the basis of Jackson, the United States Supreme Court held that defendant should be given a chance to contend that letter should have been suppressed under the rule of Edwards v. Arizona, 451 U.S. 477, 101 S.Ct. 1880, 68 L.Ed.2d 378 (1981), under which a defendant in custody could not be interrogated once he asserted a right to counsel unless he initiated further communications. The court held that defendant's arguments for exclusion of the letter were precluded because he did not raise them at the trial court in a motion to suppress. He failed to argue that he made a clear assertion of his right to counsel on the day of the letter such that the protections of Edwards would apply, or that his subsequent waiver was invalid because it was based on misrepresentations by police, as grounds for suppressing the evidence in the district court. His trial testimony came too late to affect the admissibility of the letter. In addition, admission of the letter was harmless.


OUTCOME: The court reaffirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc.


NO. 2009-C-572


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-572 (La. 03/16/10); 35 So. 3d 215; 2010 La. LEXIS 568



March 16, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 2010 La. LEXIS 1067 (La., May 7, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FIRST CIRCUIT. ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF IBERVILLE.
Rainey v. Entergy Gulf States, Inc., 6 So. 3d 877, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 232 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant, a contractor's employee, brought an action for damages against respondent principal employer after the employee was injured at work. The trial court denied the employer's affirmative defense of immunity as a statutory employer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1061. The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Iberville (Louisiana), reversed the trial court's judgment. The employee's application for writ of certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: Preliminarily, the employee's argument that the state constitution required a majority of the full complement of the appellate court to concur to render judgment was rejected. The plain and unambiguous language of La. Const. art. V, § 8 required only a majority of the judges sitting to concur to render the judgment. The en banc composition in the instant case consisted of eleven judges as one judge was recused. Thus, six judges concurring in the judgment composed a constitutional majority. With regard to the employer's affirmative defense, a contract addendum was valid and effective to create a statutory employment relationship between the employee and the principal employer under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1061, although the principal's representative affixed a typewritten signature and there was insufficient evidence to determine if the signature was authorized, because the addendum was prepared by the principal and signed by the contractor's authorized representative. The party that prepared the contract and proposed its terms was bound even if its signature was missing. Accordingly, the principal was a statutory employer entitled to tort immunity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the court of appeal.
