Transcon. Gas Pipeline Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n


NO. 2009-CA-1988 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-CA-1989 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-CA-1990 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-CA-1991 CONSOLIDATED WITH NO. 2009-CA-1992


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-1988 (La. 03/16/10); 32 So. 3d 199; 2010 La. LEXIS 592; 172 Oil & Gas Rep. 322



March 16, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE KAY BATES, JUDGE.
Transcon. Gas Pipe Line Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 15 So. 3d 385, 2009 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 523 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2009)
Transcon. Gas Pipe Line Corp. v. La. Tax Comm'n, 23 So. 3d 329, 2009 La. App. LEXIS 1470 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff interstate gas pipeline companies brought an action against defendants, the Louisiana Tax Commission and various local sheriffs and assessors, challenging an ad valorem tax scheme, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:1851(K), (M), as unconstitutional. The trial court granted partial summary judgment in favor of the companies. The Louisiana First Circuit Court of Appeal affirmed and declared § 47:1851(K), (M) unconstitutional. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The interstate companies all paid their ad valorem taxes under protest for the years in dispute and brought actions, which were consolidated. The companies alleged that the ad valorem tax scheme was violative of the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3, in that it imposed a greater tax burden on interstate companies than it did upon intrastate companies. Under the tax scheme, all interstate companies were classified as "public service property" subject to a 25 percent ad valorem tax, while some intrastate companies were classified as "other property" subject to a 15 percent tax. The higher tax assessment was not based on whether the company was engaged in intrastate or interstate commerce, but on whether the company was rate-regulated or non rate-regulated. Accordingly, the tax scheme was not discriminatory on its face, and the court of appeal erred in so finding. Moreover, the interstate companies failed to meet their burden of proving that the tax scheme burdened interstate commerce because they failed to show that the differential treatment caused by the tax scheme's classifications somehow benefited intrastate companies at the expense of interstate companies.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.


 

107 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. 2003 Infiniti G35


No. 2009-CC-1193


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-1193 (La. 01/20/10); 27 So. 3d 824; 2010 La. LEXIS 9



January 20, 2010, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LAFOURCHE.
State v. 2003 Infiniti G35, 18 So. 3d 98, 2009 La. LEXIS 2760 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant owner's car was seized pursuant to the Seizure and Controlled Dangerous Substances Property Forfeiture Act of 1989 (the Act), La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2601 et seq. The trial court denied the State's motion to strike a notice of claim filed under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2610. The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Lafourche (Louisiana), denied the State's writ application. The State's petition for supervisory writ was granted.


OVERVIEW: The State complied with the requirements for commencing a forfeiture proceeding under the Act. The parish drug task force properly followed the requirements for seizing the vehicle. The district attorney ensured that the owner was personally served with a Notice of Pending Service, which contained all the information required by statute. Finally, the State chose to make available a stipulation of exemption. Upon receipt of the service of the Notice of Pending Forfeiture, the owner attempted to comply with the requirements of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 40:2609-10, but failed to do so. The owner's claim did not contain the delineated averments, with the requisite specificity, to qualify as a valid claim under § 2610. The owner's failure to provide the essential and specific factual and legal assertions to support all of the necessary averments rendered his claim invalid under § 2610. The owner's constitutional challenge of the Act was likewise deficient and had no effect on the validity of the claim. The owner failed to provide any factual or legal support for his arguments that the seizure of his property was unconstitutional, that the Act as a whole was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the matter to the trial court to allow that court to determine, based solely on the submissions filed by the State, whether the court has jurisdiction, whether the State's Notice of Pending Forfeiture gave sufficient notice under the Act, and whether the facts averred to and provided by the State were sufficient to show probable cause for forfeiture.

 

108 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. A.J.


NO. 09-KA-0477


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


09-0477 (La. 12/01/09); 27 So. 3d 247; 2009 La. LEXIS 3508



December 1, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
Appeal from the Juvenile Court, Parish of Orleans, Honorable Mark Doherty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In appellee juvenile's delinquency proceeding, the Juvenile Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), declared that La. Child. Code Ann. art. 882, which denied juveniles the right to a jury trial in juvenile adjudications, violated the United States and Louisiana Constitutions where the juvenile was subject to a potential deprivation of liberty of more than six months. Appellant State sought review.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile was charged with committing six aggravated rapes upon his younger siblings. He was not entitled to a jury trial under La. Child. Code Ann. art. 882 even though the potential penalty involved a deprivation of liberty that was greater than six months. The juvenile court erred in holding that art. 882 was unconstitutional because the ruling was contrary to controlling precedent from the United States Supreme Court. It also erred by not affording art. 882 the presumption of constitutionality. The lack of jury trials in juvenile adjudications did not violate U.S. Const. amend. VI or La. Const. art. 1, § 17 because a juvenile court proceeding was not a criminal prosecution. Due process was not violated under U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. 1, § 2, because fundamental fairness did not require the State to provide a jury in a juvenile delinquency proceeding. Equal protection, U.S. Const. amend. XIV and La. Const. art. 1, § 3, did not provide for a right to trial by jury in juvenile adjudications because juvenile courts were legitimately distinct from adult criminal courts. Further, there was a rational basis for treating juveniles differently from adults.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

109 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Malone


NO. 08-KP-2253


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-2253 (La. 12/01/09); 25 So. 3d 113; 2009 La. LEXIS 3506



December 1, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, LAKE CHARLES CITY COURT.
State v. Malone, 11 So. 3d 494, 2009 La. LEXIS 2217 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of the misdemeanor of simple battery, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:35. He was sentenced to a fine or 30 days in jail. Defendant paid the fine and then appealed his conviction. The Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana), denied defendant's writ application on the basis that the case was moot. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant paid the fine because he had an interest in avoiding incarceration. Moreover, he claimed that he would have suffered collateral consequences as a result of the conviction. Defendant asserted that there was a collateral civil proceeding pending arising out of the incident in which he was sued for damages, and that under some legal theories, the conviction could have been used against him. Nonetheless, following his conviction, defendant paid his fine and costs without first filing a notice of intent to apply for a supervisory writ, without asking for a suspension of the sentence, without requesting post-conviction bail, and without making any record that the payment was made under protest or that it was made with any reservation. Defendant failed to take any action to indicate that he did not acquiesce in the judgment and sentence. Also, defendant failed to take any action demonstrating his objection to the conviction and sentence prior to his payment of the fine. Under those circumstances, the voluntary payment of the fine and costs before appeal rendered the matter moot.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

110 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jefferson


NO. 08-KA-2204


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-2204 (La. 12/01/09); 26 So. 3d 112; 2009 La. LEXIS 3505



December 1, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans. Honorable Lynda Van Davis, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with possession of marijuana, second offense, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:966. The State appealed from a judgment of the Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash and declared § 40:966(E)(2) unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that § 40:966(E)(2) improperly allowed the State to use a prior misdemeanor conviction of possession of marijuana, first offense, obtained in a proceeding in which there was no right to trial by jury, to increase the statutory maximum penalty available for a second offense possession of marijuana. The appellate court, however, held that U.S. Const. amends. VI and XIV did not preclude the sentence-enhancing use of the prior valid, fair, and reliable conviction of a misdemeanor, obtained against an adult, where the misdemeanor proceeding included all the constitutional protections applicable to such proceedings, even though those protections did not include the right to trial by jury. The statutory scheme of increased punishment for recidivist marijuana possession satisfied the requirement of due process because under the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments, states were allowed the presumption that in petty crimes and offenses, trial judges were capable of reliable fact finding. Accordingly, § 40:966(E)(2) did not suffer from a constitutional infirmity.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

 

111 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wallace


NO. 2009-KK-1621


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2009-1621 (La. 11/06/09); 25 So. 3d 720; 2009 La. LEXIS 3199



November 6, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Wallace, 17 So. 3d 365, 2009 La. LEXIS 2273 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought a writ of certiorari, challenging a magistrate's decision denying his request for release from custody pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 230.2. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans, denied relief. Defendant filed a writ of certiorari with the instant court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested without a warrant at 12:04 p.m. on Monday, June 8, 2009, for possession of cocaine; he was booked at 4:35 a.m. on June 9. Defendant appeared before a magistrate at 3 p.m. on June 9, but a probable cause determination was not made until he appeared before the magistrate on June 11. Because the probable cause determination was not made within 48 hours of defendant's arrest, his attorney moved for defendant's release pursuant to Article 230.2. The request was denied. On review, the court reversed, holding that because defendant did not receive the required probable cause determination within 48 hours of his arrest as required by the Fourth Amendment and Article 230.2, he was entitled to immediate release on his own recognizance. The court held that probable cause required under Article 230.2 was not determined at the time of arrest, as the Fourth Amendment required a judicial determination of probable cause when a person was arrested without a warrant. The time began to run when defendant was arrested and the determination could not be delayed to collect additional evidence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed. The district court was ordered to comply with the mandates of the opinion.

 

112 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Williams


No. 2007-KA-1407


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-1407 (La. 10/20/09); 22 So. 3d 867; 2009 La. LEXIS 2973



October 20, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Williams, 2009 La. LEXIS 3698 (La., Dec. 11, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Williams v. Louisiana, 560 U.S. 905, 130 S. Ct. 3278, 176 L. Ed. 2d 1184, 2010 U.S. LEXIS 3986 (2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE 19TH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE MICHAEL R. ERWIN, JUDGE.
State v. Williams, 959 So. 2d 894, 2007 La. LEXIS 1657 (La., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 19th Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, that convicted him of first-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30, arguing that the evidence support a conclusion that he was legally insane at the time of the offense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by a store security officer for shoplifting and was directed to return to the store to speak with a police officer who was on-site. Defendant scuffled with the officer, gained possession of her firearm, and fired numerous shots. He shot and killed the officer and wounded the security officer and a bystander who tried to assist in subduing defendant. On review, the court held that the evidence failed to show that defendant was insane under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:14 because the evidence reasonably supported the jury's finding that defendant could distinguish between right and wrong and was not insane where the record showed that no one stood between defendant and the exit, that several people told defendant to simply leave and not shoot, and that defendant instead aimed and fired at each of the three victims twice. Defendant exhibited full appreciation that the actions he had just taken were so serious that the only course left to him was escape. Further, the imposition of a capital sentence was not disproportionate to the severity of the offense under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.9 and La. Sup. Ct. R. 28.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and the sentence were affirmed.

 

113 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Warren v. La. Med. Mut. Ins. Co.


NO. 2007-CC-0492


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-0492 (La. 06/26/09); 21 So. 3d 186; 2009 La. LEXIS 2224



June 26, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Warren v. La. Med. Mut. Ins. Co., 21 So. 3d 186, 2008 La. LEXIS 2756 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the mother and sister of a deceased patient, brought suit against defendant medical providers. A second sister sought to join as plaintiff, and the providers filed an exception of prescription. The district court overruled the exception, and the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) denied the providers' writ. The court affirmed the court of appeal, but granted the providers' application for rehearing.


OVERVIEW: The patient died, allegedly as a result of the providers' failure to diagnose and treat a heart attack. At the time the second sister joined the suit, the action had prescribed. The district court held that under the doctrine of relation back in La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1153, and because her survival claim was the same as her mother's and sister's, the second sister's claim could proceed. The court held that article 1153 did not apply to this malpractice action because medical malpractice actions were governed by the specific provisions of the Medical Malpractice Act regarding prescription and suspension of prescription. Any general codal article which conflicted with these provisions may not be applied to such actions. The Act had no rules allowing relation back of pleadings for medical malpractice claims. The application of article 1153 would permit the adding of an plaintiff subsequent to the expiration of the three-year period provided for in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628, and would effectively read out of the statute the prescription and suspension period provisions in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628 and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47.


OUTCOME: The court vacated its decision on original hearing, reversed the judgment of the court of appeal, and ordered that the case be remanded to the district court to grant defendants' exception of prescription.

Gisclair v. La. Tax Comm'n


NO. 09-C-0007 consolidated with NO. 09-C-0008


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


09-0007 (La. 06/26/09); 16 So. 3d 1132; 2009 La. LEXIS 2220



June 26, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Gisclair v. La. Tax Comm'n, 994 So. 2d 154, 2008 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 541 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2008)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff tax recipient filed a petition seeking review of the 2007 tax assessment and valuation for public service properties belonging to defendants, owners. The owners and defendant Louisiana Tax Commission (LTC) filed declinatory exceptions of lack of subject matter jurisdiction, which were granted by the district court. The Court of Appeals, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton, Louisiana, reversed. Review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The LTC assessment, centrally valued and assessed all the owners' properties in Louisiana as of January 1, 2007, and then allocated that value among the various parishes in which the properties were located. The owners paid the ad valorem taxes without protest. The recipient challenged the assessment by the LTC. The question was whether the recipient's petition sought to challenge the correctness of the assessment at issue or the legality of it. The reviewing court ruled that the recipient sought review of the correctness of the LTC's assessment, and the district court did not have original jurisdiction over the claim. The recipient expressly and repeatedly stated he was challenging the value placed on the owners' properties by the LTC, that he challenged the method the LTC used to arrive at value, and that his prayer was for a correction of value. The recipient sought to correct the value the LTC placed on the owners' taxable properties, to correct the value the LTC placed on the owners' tax exempt properties, and to increase the percentage of the value allocated to the parish. The recipient did not seek to attack the assessment as having no legal existence.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed and the judgment of the district court was reinstated.

117 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Shirley


NO. 08-KK-2106


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-2106 (La. 05/05/09); 10 So. 3d 224; 2009 La. LEXIS 491



May 5, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF IBERVILLE.
State v. Shirley, 997 So. 2d 540, 2008 La. LEXIS 2746 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; CASE REMANDED TO THE TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was indicted for vehicular homicide. She filed a motion to suppress her oral statements made at the scene of a fatal, one-car accident in which the passenger was killed after defendant lost control of her car; defendant also sought to suppress the blood-alcohol test. Defendant's motion to suppress was granted, and the State sought review. The First Circuit Court of Appeal, Iberville Parish, Louisiana, affirmed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended defendant's statement that she had been drinking alcohol should not have been suppressed, and defendant had no basis for moving to suppress the results of the blood-alcohol test. The supreme court agreed in part, finding that when the trial court considered whether defendant was under arrest or detained when she made her statement to the officer and whether her statement that she consumed alcoholic beverages was admissible, it should have taken into consideration the chief's testimony, including the portion drawn from the officer's police report, when it ruled on defendant's motion to suppress. Further, Miranda warnings were not required because defendant was not in custody. Therefore, the trial court erred when it suppressed defendant's statements at the accident scene. However, suppression of the blood alcohol test results was proper as the State provided no testimony that a qualified person drew defendant's blood sample. Insofar as defendant's test results were sought to be used by the State as presumptive evidence of her guilt, theyh were inadmissible.


OUTCOME: The trial court's ruling was reversed to the extent it suppressed defendant's statements made at the scene of the vehicular accident; in all other respects, the State's writ application was denied.

State v. Skinner


NO. 08-KK-2522


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-2522 (La. 5/5/09); 10 So. 3d 1212; 2009 La. LEXIS 3263



May 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Skinner v. City of Natchitoches Police Dep't, 2013 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 42 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 6, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF NATCHITOCHES.
State v. Skinner, 998 So. 2d 89, 2009 La. LEXIS 2149 (La., 2009)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Natchitoches, after a lower court denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence the State seized purportedly pursuant to a subpoena duces tecum as provided in La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 66, a divided panel of the court of appeal denied defendant's writ. The instant court granted defendant's writ.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with violating La. Rev. Stat. 40:971B(l)(i), obtaining a prescription for a controlled dangerous substance from a health care practitioner without disclosing the fact of an existing prescription for a controlled dangerous substance from another health care practitioner, i.e., doctor shopping. Defendant had a reasonable expectation of privacy in her medical and prescription records such that a warrant was required for a search and seizure of these records for criminal investigative purposes. Because a warrant was required, the trial court erred in finding the remedy was for the State to comply with requirements of La. Code Crim. Proc. art. 66 and La. Rev. Stat. 13:3715.1, which the State had admittedly failed to comply with in obtaining defendant's prescription and medical records, in order for these records to be admissible at trial. Because the Fourth Amendment and La. Const. art. I, § 5 required a search warrant before a search of prescription and medical records for criminal investigative purposes was permitted, the State could not cure its warrantless search and seizure of the records by a second subpoena of these records.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower courts were reversed. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Reeves


NO. 2006-KA-2419


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2006-2419 (La. 05/05/09); 11 So. 3d 1031; 2009 La. LEXIS 1472



May 5, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Reeves, 2009 La. LEXIS 3426 (La., June 19, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Reeves v. Louisiana, 558 U.S. 1031, 130 S. Ct. 637, 175 L. Ed. 2d 490, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 8304 (2009)
Writ denied by State v. Reeves, 120 So. 3d 705, 2013 La. LEXIS 1979 (La., 2013)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by State v. Reeves, 137 So. 3d 625, 2014 La. LEXIS 1004 (La., 2014)
Writ denied by, Stay denied by State v. Reeves, 147 So. 3d 178, 2014 La. LEXIS 1741 (La., 2014)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Remanded by State v. Reeves, 2016 La. LEXIS 773 (La., Apr. 4, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU. HONORABLE G. MICHAEL CANADAY, JUDGE.
State v. Reeves, 846 So. 2d 999, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 1303 (La.App. 3 Cir., May 7, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which convicted him of first-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the first-degree murder of a four-year-old girl and received a death sentence. His first trial ended in a mistrial. The supreme court affirmed, stating that defendant was not constitutionally entitled to the counsel of his choice under U.S. Const. amend. VI and La. Const. art. I, § 13. Moreover, the district court anticipated that the appointment of qualified local counsel would facilitate prompt resolution of future funding and other questions that would arise in connection with defendant's retrial. There was seemingly insoluble funding issues that plagued the judicial district at that time and appointing local counsel allowed the district court to quickly set hearings for questions that arose pretrial. The supreme court also found that there was nothing constitutionally that supported the defense's argument that a criminal defendant had a right to a particular attorney-client relationship in the absence of a right to counsel of choice. Defendant's death sentence was appropriate under La. Const. art. I, § 20. The victim was under the age of 12 years, thus establishing an aggravating circumstance.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

120 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


In re Warner


05-B-1303


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-1303 (La. 03/17/09) 21 So. 3d 218; 2009 La. LEXIS 1054



April 17, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Warner, 2006 La. LEXIS 3649 (La., Apr. 20, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorneys and the Louisiana Office of Disciplinary Counsel filed objections to the Louisiana State Bar Disciplinary Board's recommendation based upon the attorneys' violation of La. Sup. Ct. R. XIX, § 16, arguing that the confidentiality requirement imposed by the rule violated their rights under the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I.


OVERVIEW: In civil litigation, the attorneys revealed information they gained about an adversary through in attorney disciplinary proceedings. A grievance was filed against them for violating the confidentiality rule of La. Sup. Ct. R. XIX, § 16(A) and (I), which prohibited participants in attorney disciplinary proceedings from disclosing any information about such proceedings. In reviewing the recommendation of the Disciplinary Board, the court agreed with the attorneys and the Office of Disciplinary Counsel that the confidentiality rule violated the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The confidentiality rule directly abridged speech and was a content-based regulation; as such, it could only be deemed constitutional if it satisfied the requirements of strict scrutiny. While the reputational interests of attorneys were important, they did not qualify as compelling under strict scrutiny. Accordingly, the confidentiality requirement imposed upon participants in attorney disciplinary proceedings under La. Sup. Ct. R. XIX, § 16(A) and (I) was unconstitutional and could not be enforced.


OUTCOME: The court held that the confidential provisions of La. Sup. Ct. R. XIX, § 16, constituted an impermissible content-based restriction of speech and thus violated the First Amendment. As such, the charges against the attorneys for violating this unconstitutional rule were dismissed.

State v. Bertrand


No. 2008-KA-2215, No. 2008-KA-2311


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2008-2215 (La. 03/17/09); 6 So. 3d 738; 2009 La. LEXIS 713



March 17, 2009, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU, HONORABLE WILFORD D. CARTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were each indicted, at separate times and for separate offenses, with felonies punishable by confinement at hard labor. Defendants' attorneys filed motions declare La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782 unconstitutional. The Fourteenth Judicial District Court of Calcasieu Parish, Louisiana, granted both motions that same day, stating that the statute violated U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, XIV. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State challenged the trial court's declaration in both cases that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 782 violated the U.S. Constitution. Due to the supreme court's prior determinations that art. 782 withstood constitutional scrutiny, and because the supreme court was not presumptuous enough to suppose, upon mere speculation, that the U.S. Supreme Court's still valid determination that non-unanimous 12 person jury verdicts were constitutional might someday be overturned, the Louisiana Supreme Court found that the trial court erred in ruling that art. 782 violated U.S. Const. amends. V, VI, XIV. The trial judge was not at liberty to ignore the controlling jurisprudence of superior courts.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed and the cases were remanded for further proceedings.

Rogoz v. Tangipahoa Parish Council


NO. 08-CA-2789


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-2789 (La. 01/30/09); 21 So. 3d 923; 2009 La. LEXIS 21



January 30, 2009, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at Rogoz v. Tangipahoa Parish Council, 2011 La. App. Unpub. LEXIS 318 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 6, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff saloon owner filed a petition against defendant parish council in the 21st Judicial District Court, Parish of Tangipahoa (Louisiana), seeking to have Tangipahoa Parish, La. Ordinance No. 07-39, § 5-38(b) and (c), declared unconstitutional. The district court ruled in favor of the owner, finding the ordinance unconstitutional. The council appealed pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: The owner applied to the parish for a permit to sell alcoholic beverages at his saloon. Pursuant to Tangipahoa Parish, La. Ordinance No. 07-39, § 5-38(b) and (c), he was required to obtain the written, notarized consent of all adjacent property owners. One of his five neighbors refused to consent. The owner argued that the ordinance constituted an impermissible zoning law when the parish had no zoning regulation in place. The court held that the owner failed to specially plead his constitutional challenge and failed to particularize the grounds of his claim. Even at the hearing, the owner did not specify any particular provisions of the constitution which he believed the ordinance violated. The court could not determine from the record whether the owner satisfied his burden of identifying a particular constitutional provision that limited the power of the parish to enact the ordinance. Further, the district court was required to make a specific determination that the constitutional issue was essential to the resolution of the case.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the district court and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

123 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Phillips v. Lafayette City-Parish Consol. Gov't


No. 08-CA-0922 c/w 08-CA-1253


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-0922 (La. 12/02/08); 995 So. 2d 1190; 2008 La. LEXIS 2750



December 2, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FIFTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF LAFAYETTE, HONORABLE EDWARD D. RUBIN, JUDGE.
Phillips v. Lafayette City-Parish Consol. Gov't, 984 So. 2d 4, 2008 La. LEXIS 1457 (La., 2008)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Fifteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Lafayette, Louisiana, granted summary judgment in favor of appellee resident finding that several sections of the code of ordinances promulgated by appellant city, known as the "junked vehicle ordinance," were unconstitutional on their face and as applied. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the trial court's finding that the ordinance were unconstitutional was premature. The city argued that the trial court should have first considered the non-constitutional issues raised in the resident's pleadings. The supreme court found that the trial court should have first considered whether the resident's vehicles were "junked motor vehicles" as defined by Lafayette City-Parish Consolidated Government, La., Code of Ordinances § 34-31. There were disputed facts with regard to the allegations that the city seized the vehicles without just cause and without due process of law. The trial court's consideration of the resident's' allegations should have started with application of the junked vehicle ordinance to the facts at hand. A determination of the constitutional issues raised in the alternative by the resident should only be considered after these non-constitutional issues have been resolved.


OUTCOME: The judgment declaring the ordinance to be unconstitutional was reversed and set aside; the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

124 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Fruge v. Bd. of Trs. of the La. State Emples. Ret. Sys.


NO. 08-CA-1270


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


08-1270 (La. 12/02/08); 6 So. 3d 124; 2008 La. LEXIS 2757



December 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Fruge v. Bd. of Trs. of the La. State Emples. Ret. Sys., 2009 La. LEXIS 3437 (La., Feb. 13, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court of the Parish of East Baton Rouge, Honorable Curtis A. Calloway, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a state retiree, brought a declaratory judgment action against defendant, the Board of Trustees of the Louisiana State Employees Retirement System, in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court of the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana). The retiree challenged the constitutionality of 2002 1st Ex. Sess. La. Acts No. 165 (Act 165). The district court granted summary judgment to the employee, and the trustees appealed.


OVERVIEW: Act 165 amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11:416, part of the Louisiana State Employees Retirement System, to provide for the reemployment of retirees and to provide for the benefits paid to such retirees. The retiree, who retired before the enactment of Act 165, was unable to participate. She argued, and the district court agreed, that Act 165 was unconstitutional because it did not comply with the notice and publication requirements of La. Const. art. X, § 29(C) (1974). The court held that art. X, § 29(C) applied only to bills introduced in regular sessions of the legislature and did not apply to bills introduced in an extraordinary session. Because Act 165 was introduced and enacted during an extraordinary session, it was subject only to the specific and clear notice provisions of La. Const. art. III, § 2(B) (1974). Contrary to the retiree's allegations, the governor's authority under past constitutions to convene an extraordinary session was not limited to a public emergency, but to a time frame, which could not exceed thirty days, and to the objects specially enumerated in the proclamation convening the extraordinary session. Therefore, the rationale of older cases remained valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court granting the retiree's motion for summary judgment and declaring Act 165 unconstitutional, null, void, and unenforceable. Finding that there were no disputed issues of material fact, and that the trustees were entitled to judgment as a matter of law, the court granted summary judgment to the trustees.

State v. Holmes


NO. 06-KA-2988


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-2988 (La. 12/02/08); 5 So. 3d 42; 2008 La. LEXIS 2758



December 2, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Holmes, 2009 La. LEXIS 2362 (La., Jan. 30, 2009)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Holmes v. Louisiana, 558 U.S. 932, 130 S. Ct. 70, 175 L. Ed. 2d 233, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 6508 (2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the First Judicial District Court, Form the Parish of Caddo, Honorable Scott J. Crichton, Judge.
State v. Coleman, 970 So. 2d 511, 2007 La. LEXIS 2392 (La., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the First Judicial District Court, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), which convicted her of first-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentenced her to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction and death-sentence for first-degree murder, but the supreme court affirmed, stating that the trial court did not err in ruling that defendant had the mental capacity to stand trial under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 641. In part, although a letter written by defendant to the district attorney suggested that defendant might not have understood the legal subtleties relative to the law regarding principals, in no way did it demonstrate that she could not assist counsel in her defense. Members of the sanity commission unanimously opined that defendant was competent and even a doctor, whose testimony defendant primarily relied upon in support of the claim and who admitted he did not examine her to determine competency, testified that she understood her rights and was able to communicate with her attorneys. Further, evidence relating to defendant's boyfriend's criminal punishment for his role in the offense was irrelevant and could have very well diverted the jury from the task before it; namely, the character and propensities of defendant. Defendant also failed to establish any basis for the suppression of her multiple statements.


OUTCOME: The conviction and sentence were affirmed.

 

126 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. A.M.


No. 2008-CK-2493


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2008-2493 (La. 11/21/08); 994 So. 2d 1277; 2008 La. LEXIS 2647



November 21, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
IN RE: State of Louisiana in the interest of A.M.; - Plaintiff; Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review Orleans Parish Juvenile Court, No. 2008-02-DQ-B; to the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, No. 2008-C-1166.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with the rape of an 8-year old child. He filed a motion seeking access to videotaped interviews of the child victim and also a child witness, age 12, so that his expert could assess the two children. The trial court denied the motion, but the Fourth Circuit Court of Appeal (Louisiana) reversed, allowing defendant's expert to view the videotapes. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Because the victim and eyewitness were children, they were protected persons under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:440.2(C). Under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:440.5(C), if defendant's attorney was provided a copy of the videotaped statement, only the attorney and the defendant could view the tape, and no copies could be made by any person. Defendant argued that this language should be interpreted broadly to allow a defense expert to review the videotape as an agent of the attorney, because any additional intrusion on the privacy interests of the protected person was minimal. The court held that the clear language of § 14:440.5(C) stated that only the defense attorney and the defendant could view the tape, and recent amendments made it clear that the legislature did not intend any expansive interpretation of that language. Defendant's right to confrontation was not violated because the victim and witness were available to testify at trial, and counsel could presumably cross examine them without expert assistance. Similarly, his due process right to present a defense was not violated, because it provided no greater rights than his right to confrontation.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Fourth Circuit Court of Appeal granting defendant's expert access to videotaped interviews with a child victim and a child witness and reinstated the decision of the Juvenile Parish Court for the Parish of Orleans denying defendant's motion.

Herman, Herman, Katz & Cotlar, L.L.C. v. State

128 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Anderson


No. 06-KA-2987


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-2987 (La. 09/09/08); 996 So. 2d 973; 2008 La. LEXIS 1744



September 9, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Anderson, 2008 La. LEXIS 2496 (La., Oct. 31, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Anderson v. La., 129 S. Ct. 1906, 173 L. Ed. 2d 1057, 2009 U.S. LEXIS 2653 (U.S., Apr. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Fourth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of Ouachita. Honorable Marcus R. Clark, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death, but the defendant asserted that his mental retardation precluded the death penalty, his confession was involuntary, jurors were improperly selected, and the evidence did not support the death penalty. The defendant appealed his conviction and sentence entered in the Fourth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of Ouachita (Louisiana).


OVERVIEW: The defendant contended that requiring the onset of retardation prior to age 18 was arbitrary, and that the defendant was not competent to stand trial. The defendant also argued that he did not knowingly and voluntarily waive his right to remain silent, that jurors were improperly challenged peremptorily based on race and selected based on pro-death attitudes, and the evidence did not support the aggravating factor of murder in a heinous or cruel manner. The Supreme Court of Louisiana held, however, that the defendant was properly convicted and sentenced. Any arbitrariness in the definition of mental retardation was irrelevant since there was no evidence that the defendant suffered adult-onset mental retardation from a head injury, and the jury found as a fact that the defendant was not retarded. Further, the defendant was competent to understand the proceedings against him, and the defendant repeatedly indicated that he understood he was voluntarily waiving his rights. Also, jurors were properly selected based on impartiality with regard to the death penalty and without regard to race, and heinousness was shown by multiple stab wounds of the victim who was aware of impending doom.


OUTCOME: The defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

State v. Hatton


NO. 2007-KA-2377


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-2377 (La. 7/1/08); 985 So. 2d 709; 2008 La. LEXIS 1528



July 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 15, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FOURTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF CALCASIEU. HONORABLE WILFORD D. CARTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED, VACATED, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Louisiana sought review of an order from the Fourteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana), which granted defendant's motion to quash a bill of information charging him with two counts of "Computer-Aided Solicitation for Sexual Purposes," in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:81.3, on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of "Computer-Aided Solicitation for Sexual Purposes," in violation of § 14:81.3, after he was arrested at an attempted meeting with a 14-year-old girl that he met online. He filed a motion to quash the bill of information on the basis that it failed to charge an offense punishable under a valid statute. He argued that § 14:81.3 violated the equal protection provisions of La. Const. art. I, § 3 and infringed upon his constitutional right to present a defense, contrary to the guarantees of U.S. Const. amend. VI and La. Const. art. I, § 16. The trial court granted the motion. On appeal, the court found that although the trial court discussed the constitutional grounds that were properly raised by defendant, its declaration of unconstitutionality of the statute was not based on those grounds. The trial court relied upon constitutional grounds that were not properly raised, La. Const. art. I, § 22 and La. Const. art. I, § 13, in granting the motion to quash and finding § 14:81.3 unconstitutional. It was improper for the trial court to consider grounds that were not properly raised and it erred in granting the motion to quash.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court and vacated the trial court's ruling in its entirety. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

Fransen v. City of New Orleans


NO. 2008-CA-0076 C/W NO. 2008-CA-0087


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2008-0076 (La. 7/1/08); 988 So. 2d 225; 2008 La. LEXIS 1526



July 1, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT PARISH OF ORLEANS.
Fransen v. City of New Orleans, 970 So. 2d 1, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1919 (La.App. 4 Cir., 2007)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART, AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers brought suit against defendants, a city, a tax collection firm, and law firms, challenging the assessment of penalties, interest, and attorney fees in connection with the collection of property taxes. A Louisiana trial court held that the city ordinance in question was constitutional. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), reversed and ordered a remand. The city and the other defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The ordinance in question permitted the city to place for collection with an attorney or collection agent delinquent ad valorem property taxes, to levy penalties, including a penalty to cover costs of collection by an attorney or collection agent, for delinquent ad valorem property taxes, and to sue to collect the delinquent tax. The court held that the ordinance was an unconstitutional exercise of the city's plenary power under its home rule charter because La. Const. art. VII, § 25 provided tax sales as the exclusive method for a governmental subdivision to collect delinquent ad valorem property taxes and did not allow for the imposition of a penalty for such taxes. The ordinance was unconstitutional to the extent it imposed penalties, other than interest, upon delinquent ad valorem property taxes on immovables. The constitutional provision relating to property taxation, La. Const. art. VII, § 25(B), permitted a governmental subdivision to impose only the taxes, interest, and costs in proceeding to sell the property for the delinquent ad valorem taxes.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the intermediate appellate court's judgment insofar as it held the ordinance unconstitutional with respect to provisions that permitted the city to proceed other than by tax sales to collect delinquent ad valorem property taxes and that permitted the city to impose penalties other than interest. The remainder of the judgment was vacated, and the matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

131 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Borel v. Young


NO. 07-C-0419


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-0419 (La. 7/1/08); 989 So. 2d 42; 2008 La. LEXIS 1529



July 1, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Concurring Opinion at Borel v. Lafayette Gen. Med. Ctr., 2008 La. LEXIS 1741 (La., Aug. 29, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL THIRD CIRCUIT PARISH OF LAFAYETTE ON REHEARING.
Borel v. Young, 989 So. 2d 42, 2007 La. LEXIS 2596 (La., Nov. 27, 2007)
Borel v. Young, 947 So. 2d 824, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2979 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 29, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Louisiana Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, affirmed the decision of the district court by granting defendants', medical center, doctor, and physicians' insurer, exception of prescription on plaintiff family's medical malpractice action. The supreme court granted a rehearing to consider whether the determination that the three-year time limitation in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5638 was preemptive was a correct interpretation of Louisiana law.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that 1987 La. Acts 915, § 1, amending and reenacting La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:5628, did not evidence a legislative intent to change the result of a case and make the statute's three-year period preemptive. Had the Legislature meant for the time period to be preemptive, it could have expressed its intent in the title or text of the act, or in the language of the statute itself. The supreme court erred in its original opinion concluding that § 9:5628 established a preemptive time period and the family's action against the doctor, filed over three years after the alleged act of malpractice, was extinguished by peremption. The family's claims against the doctor were properly dismissed. The family had 90 days, plus the remainder of the one-year prescriptive period that was unused at the time the request for a medical review panel was filed (282 days), or until January 29, 2003, to bring the doctor, who had been previously named in the medical review panel, into the suit. Their attempt to bring him into the lawsuit on March 15, 2005, came too late. The district court correctly sustained the peremptory exception of prescription.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was affirmed.

 

132 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


M.J. Farms, Ltd. v. Exxon Mobil Corp.


NO. 07-CA-2371


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-2371 (La. 7/1/08); 998 So. 2d 16; 2008 La. LEXIS 1527; 177 Oil & Gas Rep. 249



July 1, 2008, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE SEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF CATAHOULA. JUDGE KATHY JOHNSON, JUDGE PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Seventh Judicial District Court, Catahoula Parish, Louisiana, granted judgment in favor of appellee landowner by declaring 2006 La. Acts 312 (Act 312) unconstitutional on the grounds that it violated La. Const. art. V, § 16, the Fifth Amendment, and La. Const. art. 1, § 4. The landowner alleged defendant corporations caused environmental damages when they conducted oil and gas exploration and production activities. The corporations appealed.


OVERVIEW: Reading La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 30:29, the supreme court found it clear and unambiguous that the provisions of Act 312 were called into play when any litigation or pleading making a judicial demand arising from or alleging environmental damage was filed. It required the Department of Natural Resources (DNR) compliance by private parties involving cleanup and remediation activities subject to DNR's jurisdiction. Act 312 applied retrospectively and prospectively except for the limited number of cases for which an order had been issued or signed setting the case for trial as of March 27, 2006. Act 312 adopted a procedure and simply sought to ensure that the property that was environmentally damages was actually remediated. The district court erred when it found that Act 312 unconstitutional because its retroactive application to the lawsuit filed prior to the effective date of the act impermissibly disturbed the landowners' vested rights. Act 312 did not divest the district court of original jurisdiction. It did not deny access to the courts. The district court remained an active participant in the entire restoration process.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Burmaster v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't


No. 2007-CA-2432


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-2432 (La. 05/21/08); 982 So. 2d 795; 2008 La. LEXIS 1179



May 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 6, 2008.
Later proceeding at Burmaster v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't, 45 So. 3d 1061, 2010 La. LEXIS 2174 (La., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-FIFTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF PLAQUEMINES.
Burmaster v. Plaquemines Parish Gov't, 963 So. 2d 378, 2007 La. LEXIS 1777 (La., 2007)



DISPOSITION: DENIAL OF EXCEPTION OF NO CAUSE OF ACTION AFFIRMED; CASE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Twenty-fifth Judicial District Court, Parish of Plaquemines, Louisiana, declared as unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff property owner's individual and class actions, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800(H), on the property owner's suit against defendant, Plaquemines Parish Government (PPG), in which he sought damages to his property. The district court denied PPG's exception of no cause of action. PPG petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that the Louisiana Legislature did not intend for La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800(H) to apply to the case, which had already been filed and was pending when it became effective on June 22, 2006, because the statute did not contain an express declaration that it applied to pending cases. The supreme court noted that the statute contained an express retroactivity clause. The damages sought by the owner and the putative class were damages arising out of Hurricane Katrina, which occurred on August 29, 2005, and thus were sustained after August 26, 2005. There was no merit in the owner's argument that the statute did not apply because his claims were not based solely on La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 2317 and 2317.1. The statute clearly applied to the causes of action under La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 2317 and 2317.1 set forth by the owner and the putative class in the case. There was no merit to PPG's argument that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 9:2800(H) did not divest the owner or class of any vested rights, but merely changed the plaintiffs' burden of proof. The retroactive application of the statute would unconstitutionally divest the owner and the putative class of vested rights.


OUTCOME: The denial of PPG's exception of no cause of action was affirmed; the case was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

State v. Granger


No. 2007-KA-2285


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-2285 (La. 05/21/08); 982 So. 2d 779; 2008 La. LEXIS 1181



May 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 6, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE BONNIE P. JACKSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which dismissed defendant's motion to dismiss and then, after defendant filed a motion to reconsider ruling, held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:578.1 was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented on appeal was whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:578.1 unconstitutionally discriminated against DWI offenders who entered into pretrial diversion programs, and thus violated the equal protection guarantees of La. Const. art. I, § 3 and U.S. Const. amend. XIV. The type of classification presented within § La. R.S. 15:578.1 was not one of those specifically enumerated within La. Const. art. I, § 3. Consequently, the statute's classification was subject to the lowest level of equal protection scrutiny, and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:578.1 was presumed to be constitutional unless defendant, as the statute's challenger, was able to prove that the classification did not suitably further an appropriate state interest. The interests set forth by the State in protecting Louisiana's citizens and visitors from the dangers of intoxicated drivers were appropriate and defendant failed to offer proof to the contrary. Accordingly, the district court's judgment declaring § 15:578.1 unconstitutional was erroneous and was therefore reversed. Defendant's motion for expungement was hereby dismissed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's motion for expungement was dismissed and the judgment declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:578.1 unconstitutional was reversed.

State v. Campbell


No. 2006-KA-0286


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-0286 (La. 05/21/08); 983 So. 2d 810; 2008 La. LEXIS 1183



May 21, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 27, 2008.
Rehearing denied by State v. Campbell, 2008 La. LEXIS 1420 (La., June 27, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by, Motion granted by Campbell v. Louisiana, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8382 (U.S., Nov. 17, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the First Judicial District Court, For the Parish of Caddo. Honorable Leon L. Emanuel, III, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the First Judicial District Court, for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), convicted defendant of first-degree murder under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and recommended a sentence of death. After denying postconviction motions, the trial court sentenced defendant to death. This appeal followed.


OVERVIEW: Because defendant did not establish that reasonable grounds existed to suggest he was mentally retarded under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.5.1, his death sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment. Preliminary test results showed that defendant possibly had a low intelligence quotient, but these results were insufficient to establish mental retardation under the statute, Moreover, defendant refused to participate in further testing designed to determine whether he was mentally retarded. Also, he was never diagnosed as mentally retarded despite numerous assessments while he was in school, and his own adaptive skills such as holding a steady job negated a reasonable likelihood that he qualified as mentally retarded. Defendant was not exempt from the death penalty based on his mental age because he was 18 years old when he committed capital murder and therefore was not eligible to benefit from the bright-line exemption for offenders under age 18. Also, the record showed that he was competent to stand trial under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. § 641. Considering the offense and the offender, the death sentence imposed in this case was not disproportionately harsh.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

S. Silica of La., Inc. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n


No. 07-CA-1680


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-1680 (La. 04/08/08); 979 So. 2d 460; 2008 La. LEXIS 792



April 8, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 22, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge.
S. Silica of La., Inc. v. La. Ins. Guar. Ass'n, 966 So. 2d 45, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1449 (La.App. 1 Cir., 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, companies, filed suit for declaratory judgment that defendant Louisiana Insurance Guaranty Association (LIGA) owed it indemnity and/or defense for silicosis suits. Summary judgment was granted in favor of the LIGA. The First Circuit Court of Appeal, Parish of East Baton Rouge, Louisiana, found that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386(A) did not apply retroactively in the matter. The companies appealed.


OVERVIEW: The companies alleged they had been named as defendants in approximately 500 silicosis suits filed in Louisiana, Texas, and Mississippi. The plaintiffs in the silicosis suits claimed they were exposed to silica dust over long periods of time, with some exposure dates ranging from 1965 to 2003. The companies sought a declaration that the LIGA owed them indemnity and/or defense for exposure dates during the years 1977 through 1982, when the companies were insured by a now insolvent insurer. In reversing the trial court's judgment, the court of appeal found that retroactive application of the amendment to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1386(A) to the companies was unconstitutional. The reviewing court held retroactive application of the statute was not prohibited. The Louisiana Legislature specifically provided that the statute was to be applied to all pending claims and there was no constitutional infirmities. The companies were entitled to indemnity for the years 1977 through 1982 from the LIGA, but only after the pro rata shares of all insurers that provided coverage in the Louisiana suits against the companies were determined by judgment or settlement.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

Newman Marchive P'ship v. City of Shreveport


No. 07-C-1890


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-1890 (La. 04/08/08); 979 So. 2d 1262; 2008 La. LEXIS 793



April 8, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Newman Marchive P'ship v. Hightower, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8945 (W.D. La., Feb. 6, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO.
Newman Marchive P'ship v. City of Shreveport, 962 So. 2d 1075, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1576 (La.App. 2 Cir., 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; WRIT OF MANDAMUS DISSOLVED; PETITION DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: City filed a writ of certiorari to challenge the judgment of the Second Circuit Court of Appeals, Parish of Caddo, Louisiana, requiring the city to pay the unpaid interest on a judgment obtained by plaintiff claimant from city funds.


OVERVIEW: The claimant sued the city for breach of contract relative to renovations to a stadium. After the trial court awarded the clamant $ 251,304.34, the court of appeal amended the judgment by increasing it to $263,674.10, together with legal interest from the date of judicial demand. When the city failed to pay the judgment, the claimant brought the instant litigation, filing a petition for writ of mandamus. The City made an unconditional tender to the claimant of the principal amount of the judgment, but refused at the same time to pay the legal interest, which amounted to $ 70,301.66. The court of appeal required the city to pay the remainder of the judgment, finding that because the city had appropriated up to $ 15 million to a retained risk fund, a fund established specifically to pay legal settlements and judgments, mandamus was appropriate. The reviewing court held that the claimant could not compel the city through a writ of mandamus to pay the judgment. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5109(B)(2) required a specific appropriation of funds to pay a particular judgment before disbursement of those funds could be compelled by writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeal was reversed, the peremptory writ of mandamus was dissolved, and the claimant's petition was dismissed.

State v. Lanclos


No. 07-OK-0082 c/w 07-KA-0716


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-0082 (La. 04/08/08); 980 So. 2d 643; 2008 La. LEXIS 794



April 8, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication April 22, 2008.

As Corrected June 20, 2008.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE FIRST PARISH COURT, PARISH OF JEFFERSON.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to a violation of improper equipment and was issued a fee and fine slip, which ordered him to pay court costs in addition to the fine for the offense. The Traffic Hearing Officer (THO) denied defendant's motion to strike a portion of the fine under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:57(G) as unconstitutional. The First Parish Court of Jefferson Parish, Louisiana, subsequently granted defendant's motion. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended the trial court erred in finding that the fine in question was unconstitutional. The supreme court disagreed, holding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:57(G), requiring courts to assess an additional $ 5.00 cost on defendants who received a traffic citation from an officer of the Greater New Orleans Expressway Commission, was unconstitutional as it was a "tax" funded through the judiciary in violation of the doctrine of separation of powers. Section 32:57(G) was a charge that had as its primary purpose the raising of revenue, and was, therefore, a "tax." As provided in the statute, the $ 5.00 cost was collected for the purpose of supplementing police salaries and acquisition and maintenance of police equipment. Funding police salaries and the maintenance of police equipment were the responsibility of the local tax collection authorities, not the judiciary.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Meaux v. Galtier


NO. 07-CA-2474


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-2474 (La. 01/25/08); 972 So. 2d 1137; 2008 La. LEXIS 162



January 25, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by Meaux v. Galtier, 977 So. 2d 923, 2008 La. LEXIS 594 (La., Mar. 14, 2008)
Rehearing denied by Meaux v. Galtier, 978 So. 2d 337, 2008 La. LEXIS 889 (La., Apr. 18, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: IN RE: Appeal on Behalf of John Hammond and Geraldine Hammond, Parish of Lafayette, 15th Judicial District Court No. 2003-1042-H2.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed and remanded to the district court.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants sought review of an order from a trial court (Louisiana), which denied their exception of prescription/peremption in plaintiff's action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought an action against defendants. The trial court denied defendants' exception of prescription/peremption. On appeal, defendants claimed that the trial court erred in declaring La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 191 unconstitutional. The court found that nothing in the trial court's judgment declared a law or ordinance unconstitutional. The issue of constitutionality was raised in a filing by plaintiff captioned as a memorandum. However, under La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 852, a memorandum was not a pleading recognized under the Louisiana Code of Civil Procedure and was not a proper method to challenge the constitutionality of a statute. Accordingly, there was no proper declaration of unconstitutionality and, therefore, no basis for the exercise of the court's appellate jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeal and remanded the case for further proceedings.

State v. Lee


NO. 2005-KA-2098


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-2098 (La. 1/16/08); 976 So. 2d 109; 2008 La. LEXIS 156



January 16, 2008, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Lee, 2008 La. LEXIS 1093 (La., Mar. 7, 2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lee v. Louisiana, 555 U.S. 824, 129 S. Ct. 143, 172 L. Ed. 2d 39, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 6561 (2008)
Post-conviction relief dismissed at State v. Lee, 2015 La. LEXIS 1722 (La., Sept. 18, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE, HONORABLE RICHARD D. ANDERSON, JUDGE.
State v. Lee, 964 So. 2d 967, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1035 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 16, 2007)
State v. Lee, 879 So. 2d 173, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 841 (La.App. 1 Cir., Apr. 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, Parish of East Baton Rouge, (Louisiana), of first-degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the trial court erred by denying his motion to suppress evidence. The supreme court found that the collection of defendant's DNA pursuant to the subpoena under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 66 was improper, but that the evidence would have been inevitably discovered. The State's attempt to file a subpoena duces tecum through the use of art. 66 was a circumvention of the mandates for the issuance of a search warrant based upon probable cause. However, due to the sheer size and complexity of the search for the serial killer, other agencies working independently from the task force received tips naming defendant as a suspect before and after the illegal search. Law enforcement already suspected defendant and had an established operational procedure to investigate him at the time the DNA was obtained and matched. Law enforcement then acquired probable cause to arrest defendant and secure his DNA to identify him as the victim's assailant as well as the other murders. Consequently, defendant's DNA would have been inevitably collected and matched to his victims. Thus, the trial court properly denied defendant's motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

142 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Kinchen v. Livingston Parish Council


NO. 07-C-0478


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


07-0478 (La. 10/16/07); 967 So. 2d 1137; 2007 La. LEXIS 2322



October 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 30 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LIVINGSTON.
Kinchen v. Livingston Parish Council, 959 So. 2d 896, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 245 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 9, 2007)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer filed a class action petition for declaratory judgment and damages, alleging that an ordinance was unconstitutional, that the assessment and collection of a tax was unlawful. The courts below determined that a parish's exception of no cause of action would lie. The taxpayer filed a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Livingston, Louisiana.


OVERVIEW: The parish passed an ordinance that purported to require the payment of a documentary transaction tax upon execution by parties of any instrument affecting immovable property located in the parish. The taxpayer argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:2110 did not control, as it applied only to ad valorem taxes and not to other taxes such as the tax at issue. If the statute did indeed apply only to ad valorem taxes, and did not, then, provide the exclusive remedy for protesting other types of taxes such as the documentary transfer tax at issue, then the taxpayer need not have pled in her petition the procedures contained within the statute, and the courts below erred in sustaining the parish's exception of no cause of action. The supreme court found that the legislature did not intend for § 47:2110 to provide the exclusive remedy for protesting taxes such as the documentary transfer tax at issue. Consequently, the taxpayer did not need to have pled in her petition the procedures contained within the statute. Further, because the exception of prescription likewise depended upon the applicability of § 47:2110 to the instant suit, that exception also fails.


OUTCOME: The decisions of the lower courts were reversed. The matter was remanded to the trial court for disposition in accordance with the decision.

Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton


No. 2007-C-0290


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-0290 (La. 10/16/07); 966 So. 2d 545; 2007 La. LEXIS 2326



October 16, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 30, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RAPIDES.
Int'l Paper Co. v. Hilton, 950 So. 2d 1, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2606 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 15, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant company, located in a pre-existing industrial area, brought an action against respondent taxing entities for a newly established millage it paid under protest, contending that it was not subject to inclusion and taxation by a newly created special service district. A judgment was rendered in favor of the taxing entities, and the Louisiana Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Rapides Parish, affirmed. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling that the assessment of the ad valorem taxes against the company was proper, and further concluded that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.16 had been tacitly repealed. On review, the company challenged, inter alia, the appellate court's finding that the company could be subject to inclusion and taxation by a newly created special service district, and that § 33:130.16 had been tacitly repealed. The supreme court concluded that § 33:130.16 had not been tacitly repealed as it and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1203 could be harmonized and were not in conflict with each other. After reviewing La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.11 et seq. and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 51:1202, 1203, the supreme court also concluded that industrial areas were to be excluded from inclusion and taxation only from those special districts providing services specifically enumerated in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:130.15 (repealed 1995, now codified at La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 51:1202). Because recreational services were not listed in the statutes, the company could be included in the recreation district at issue and, thus, could also be taxed in this district.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Deculus v. Welborn


No. 2007-C-1888


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-1888 (La. 10/1/07); 964 So. 2d 930; 2007 La. LEXIS 2076



October 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication October 17, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
ON WRITS OF REVIEW FROM THE LOUISIANA COURT OF APPEAL (EN BANC) FOR THE FIRST CIRCUIT PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Deculus v. Welborn, 970 So. 2d 1057, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1696 (La.App. 1 Cir., Sept. 19, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A candidate challenged a decision from the Louisiana Court of Appeal for the First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge, which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff objectors in a dispute over the candidate's eligibility to run for re-election.


OVERVIEW: The candidate was elected to serve the remainder of a term after another senator left his office. Thereafter, the candidate was elected to two consecutive terms. When he sought to run again, the objectors argued that he was ineligible. The district court dismissed the petition filed by the objectors. The court of appeal found that the candidate was ineligible, and this appeal followed. In affirming the court of appeal, the supreme court determined that La. Const. art. III, § 4(E) prohibited the candidate from running again. After looking at the legislative history, the supreme court determined that the date of election was determinative in an analysis of the applicability of term limits. The date that the secretary of state promulgated the election was the date upon which the candidate was officially elected. Here, the candidate was elected to serve the unexpired remainder of the first term as of December 18, 1997, which was prior to the halfway point of that term. It was finally noted that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:601(B) was irrelevant for purposes of the constitutional term limitation found in La. Const. art. III, § 4(E).


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

145 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


City of New Orleans v. La. Assessors' Ret. & Relief Fund


No. 05-CA-2548


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-2548 (La. 10/01/07); 986 So. 2d 1; 2007 La. LEXIS 2077



October 1, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by City of New Orleans v. La. Assessors' Ret. & Relief Fund, 2008 La. LEXIS 3 (La., Jan. 7, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] 
On Appeal from the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge. Honorable Timothy E. Kelley, Judge.
864 So. 2d 200, 2004 La. LEXIS 224 (La., Jan. 26, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A city and mayor sued the Louisiana Assessors' Retirement Fund and state treasurer, challenging the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11:1418. The Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana) declared the statute unconstitutional under La. Const. art. VII, § 26(C), and art. VI, §§ 26(B) and 32, but denied the other constitutional challenges. The Fund and state treasurer appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to the district court's conclusions, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 11:1481 did not require a percentage of taxes dedicated to other purposes to be diverted from those purposes for which the taxes were enacted in order to finance the Fund; therefore, the statute did not violate La. Const. art. VI, §§ 26(B) and 32. The statute did not distribute revenue sharing funds to an entity not entitled to receive those funds, in contravention of La Const. art. VII, § 26(C). The district court properly rejected the challenge under La. Const. art. II, §§ 1 and 2, because as a political subdivision of the state, the city was not protected by those sections. La. Const. art. XII, § 10(C), did not apply as the statute did not attempt to enforce a judgment against the city or seize public funds as the result of a judgment emanating from a lawsuit. The statute did not violate La. Const. art. VII, § 19, where the city failed to show that the amounts collected exceeded the 5.75 mill ceiling. Finally, the statute did not violate La. Const. art. I, § 3, as there was no evidence that it created a legislative classification or that any classification did not suitably further an appropriate state interest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed as to the conclusion that the statute violated several provisions of the Louisiana Constitution, but was affirmed as to the conclusions that the statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine, the constitutional prohibition against seizure of public funds, the constitutional ceiling on state ad valorem taxes, and the equal protection guarantees of the United States and Louisiana Constitutions.
