Sims v. Mulhearn Funeral Home, Inc.


NO. 2007-CA-0054


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2007-0054 (La. 05/22/07); 956 So. 2d 583; 2007 La. LEXIS 1238



May 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication June 6, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita. Honorable Benjamin Jones, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and RENDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In plaintiff beneficiary's suit for breach of contract, breach of fiduciary duty, negligent misrepresentation, and negligent infliction of emotional and mental distress, defendants, a funeral home and an insurer, appealed a judgment of the Fourth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Ouachita that had denied their motion for summary judgment and held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 22:253(A), as amended by 2004 La. Acts 689, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The beneficiary argued that two industrial life insurance policies issued in 1958 and 1963, respectively, each with a face value of $500, required payment in full of her husband's 2003 funeral. The district court declared 2004 La. Acts 689 unconstitutional, finding that the history of the Act, which amended La. Rev. Stat. Ann. 22:253(A), did not support the legislature's declaration that the Act was interpretive and, therefore, subject to retroactive application. On appeal, the court held that the district court erred in reaching the constitutional issue because the issue was resolvable by applying the unambiguous language of the contracts. The contracts clearly relied upon the incorporated policy schedules to limit the total cash value of each policy to $500. The contracts' detailed description of funeral benefits, upon which the beneficiary relied, were subject to the face amounts shown on the schedules. Any other interpretation of the parties' intent was absurd. The funeral home and the insurer did not breach the contracts by crediting the beneficiary in the amount of $1,000 toward the total cost of her husband's $5,998 funeral and requiring her to pay the difference.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and awarded summary judgment to the funeral home and the insurer. The court pretermitted addressing whether the Act was unconstitutional.

State v. Kennedy


No. 05-KA-1981


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-1981 (La. 05/22/07); 957 So. 2d 757; 2007 La. LEXIS 1244



May 22, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected July 5, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State v. Kennedy, 2007 La. LEXIS 1618 (La., June 29, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by, Motion granted by Kennedy v. Louisiana, 128 S. Ct. 829, 169 L. Ed. 2d 625, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 408 (U.S., 2008)
Reversed by, Remanded by Kennedy v. Louisiana, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 5262 (U.S., June 25, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of Jefferson, Honorable Ross LaDart, Judge.
State v. Kennedy, 851 So. 2d 313, 2003 La. LEXIS 2219 (La., Aug. 12, 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Twenty-Fourth Judicial District Court, For the Parish of Jefferson (Louisiana), found defendant guilty of aggravated rape of the victim, his eight-year-old stepdaughter, under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:42. The jury unanimously decided that defendant should be sentenced to death. The trial court denied his motion for a new trial. Defendant appealed his death sentence to the supreme court pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D)(2).


OVERVIEW: The victim's videotaped accusations of rape were admissible and did not violate the Confrontation Clause because the victim was physically present to testify. In addition, the supreme court stated that child rapists as a class of offenders, unlike the young or mentally retarded, shared no common characteristic tending to mitigate the moral culpability of their crimes. Furthermore, the execution of child rapists would serve the goals of deterrence and retribution just as well as execution of first-degree murderers would. Moreover, short of a first-degree murderer, the supreme court could think of no other non-homicide crime more deserving of the death penalty. Thus, the supreme court held that the death penalty for the rape of a child under 12 was not disproportionate under the Eighth Amendment. Therefore, defendant's death sentence for raping an eight-year-old child was proper. Also, pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art 905.9 and La. Sup. Ct. R. XXVIII, the supreme court found that the sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion or prejudice, the evidence supported the statutory aggravating factors, and the sentence was not disproportionate to the offense.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed defendant's conviction and death sentence.

State v. King


No. 06-KK-2383


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-2383 (La. 04/27/07); 956 So. 2d 562; 2007 La. LEXIS 907



April 27, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] 
Released for Publication May 11, 2007.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT PARISH OF LASALLE.
State v. King, 944 So. 2d 1268, 944 So. 2d 1268, 2006 La. LEXIS 3539 (La., Dec. 15, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a town chief of police, was charged with malfeasance in office. Defendant filed a motion to recuse the district attorney alleging the prosecutor possessed strong personal feelings of animosity towards him that would conflict with the fair and impartial administration of justice. The trial court denied the motion, but the Louisiana Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, LaSalle Parish, reversed. The Stated sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State contended defendant failed to prove that the district attorney had a personal interest in the cause which was in conflict with the fair and impartial administration of justice such that he should have been recused pursuant to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 680(1). The supreme court disagreed, finding that the district attorney's personal animosity toward defendant stemming from the district attorney's belief that defendant started or spread a salacious rumor about him and a member of his family was a factor in making certain prosecutorial decisions; as such, the supreme court concluded that the district attorney's ability to fairly and impartially conduct defendant's trial was called into question. Consequently, the district attorney should have been recused in accordance with art. 680(1), and the trial court erred in denying defendant's motion to recuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Ruiz v. Tanner, 2013 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 173516 (W.D. La., Oct. 10, 2013)

State v. Ruiz, 931 So. 2d 472, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 1248 (La.App. 3 Cir., May 24, 2006)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine and distribution of cocaine. The Louisiana Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Iberia Parish, affirmed. Defendant sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant averred that charging him under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:982 as a substantive offense constituted structural error, requiring per se reversal of the conviction; therefore, her argued, the appellate court wrongly applied a harmless error analysis to the fact of the jury's exposure to defendant's criminal history. The supreme court disagreed, holding that although treating § 40:982 as a substantive element of the offense and including the allegations of the prior offense or offenses in the charging instrument was erroneous, this was not a structural error as it did not necessarily render the criminal trial fundamentally unfair or an unreliable vehicle for determining guilt or innocence. Furthermore, defendant's failure to object to the inclusion of the prior convictions in the bill, his failure to object to the presentation of evidence of these convictions to the jury, and his failure to request a limiting instruction from the trial court, thereby waived any error.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed and the case was remanded for sentencing.

Arrington v. Galen-Med, Inc.


NOS. 06-C-2923, 06-C-2944, 06-C-2968


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-2923 (La. 02/02/2007); 947 So. 2d 719; 2007 La. LEXIS 322



February 2, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Health Care Indemnity Inc.; Louisiana, State of; Galen-Med, Inc. formerly d/b/a; Lake Area Medical Center; - Defendant(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of Calcasieu, 14th Judicial District Court Div. B, Nos. 97-4329; to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, No. 04-1235.
Arrington v. ER Physicians Group, 940 So. 2d 777, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2164 (La.App. 3 Cir., Sept. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Writ granted. The court of appeal's judgment of unconstitutionality is vacated. Case remanded to the court of appeal.



CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a medical center, the Louisiana Patients' Compensation Fund (PCF), and the State of Louisiana, sought review of an order from a Louisiana court of appeals, which, in a medical malpractice action, awarded summary judgment to plaintiffs and declared that the limitation of liability in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) was unconstitutional under La. Const. art. I, § 22.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs brought a medical malpractice suit against the medical center and a physician. The trial court approved a settlement in the amount of $ 100,000 between plaintiffs and the physician. The trial court also approved a settlement of plaintiffs' claim against the PCF in the amount of $ 500,000. Plaintiffs filed a motion for summary judgment, seeking to have the trial court declare the limitation of liability in La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) unconstitutional. Defendants moved for summary judgment. The trial court denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment, but granted defendants' motions. The court of appeals granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiffs, finding the $ 500,000 cap on medical malpractice damages unconstitutional under La. Const. art. I, § 22. On review, the court found that plaintiffs did not plead La. Const. art. I, § 22 as a ground for finding La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) unconstitutional. In the absence of properly pleading and initial consideration of such ground by the trial court, the court of appeals erred in declaring § 40:1299.42(B) to be in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 22.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the court of appeals. Because the court of appeals pretermitted the remaining issues in the appeal, the court remanded the matter to the court of appeals for consideration of those matters.

Taylor v. Clement


NOS. 06-C-2518, 06-C-2581, 06-C-2600


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-2518 (La. 02/02/2007); 947 So. 2d 721; 2007 La. LEXIS 323



February 2, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by Taylor v. Clement, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 1377 (La.App. 3 Cir., July 6, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Clement, Emily Sue Curatrix; Clement, Richard J. M. LPCF; - Defendant(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of Calcasieu, 14th Judicial District Court Div. B, Nos. 99-191; to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, No. 04-1069.
State v. Clements, 940 So. 2d 796, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 2171 (La.App. 3 Cir., Sept. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: Writ granted. The court of appeal's judgment of unconstitutionality is vacated. Case remanded to the court of appel.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The district court granted appellant doctor's motion for summary judgment, thereby finding that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B), the cap on medical malpractice damages, was constitutional. However, nothing in the trial court's ruling discussed La. Const. art. I, § 22. The Court of Appeal (Louisiana) reversed, finding the cap unconstitutional for failing to provide an adequate remedy as guaranteed under La. Const. art. I, § 22.


OVERVIEW: The doctor and intervenor patients' compensation fund appealed, seeking to reverse the court of appeal's holding. Appellee parents had pleaded La. Const. art. I, § 22 as a ground for unconstitutionality, but did not rely on that ground in their motion for summary judgment. Therefore, the question of whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) violated La. Const. art. I, § 22 was never briefed and argued before the district court, nor was that issue passed upon by the district court in its ruling denying the parents' motion for summary judgment. Under those circumstances, the Supreme Court of Louisiana had to conclude that any purported violation of La. Const. art. I, § 22 was not made an issue in the district court. In the absence of initial consideration of that ground by the district court, the court of appeal erred in declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) unconstitutional because it was in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 22. The supreme court declined the parents' request to exercise its discretionary jurisdiction to consider whether the statute violated any other constitutional provisions.


OUTCOME: The writs were granted. The court of appeal's judgment of unconstitutionality was vacated on procedural grounds and the case was remanded to the court of appeal for consideration of the remaining issues.

Arrington v. Galen-Med, Inc.


NOS. 06-C-2968, 06-C-2923, 06-C-2944,


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA

February 2, 2007, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] IN RE: Health Care Indemnity Inc.; Louisiana, State of; Galen-Med, Inc. formerly d/b/a; Lake Area Medical Center; - Defendant(s); Applying for Writ of Certiorari and/or Review, Parish of Calcasieu, 14th Judicial District Court Div. CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff survivors filed a medical malpractice suit against defendant physician and defendant medical center. The trial court approved a settlement between the survivors and the physician. The court also approved a settlement with the patients' Compensation Fund (PCF) in the amount of $ 500,000. The Court of Appeal, Third Circuit (Louisiana) reversed, finding the cap on medical malpractice damages unconstitutional. The parties sought review.


OVERVIEW: The survivors argued that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) violated the separation of powers doctrine pursuant to La. Const. art. II, §§ 1 and 2; due process pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 2; the state constitutional prohibition against special laws pursuant to La. Const. art. III, § 12; and judicial power pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 16. Nevertheless, this issue was never briefed and argued before the district court, nor was that issue passed upon by the district court in its ruling denying plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment. Any purported violation of La. Const. art. I, § 22 was not specially pleaded, nor was it made an issue in the district court. The intermediate court of appeal erred in declaring § 40:1299.42(B) to be unconstitutional in violation of La. Const. art. I, § 22.


OUTCOME: The writs were granted. The judgment of the intermediate court of appeal declaring the statute to be unconstitutional was vacated and set aside. The case was remanded to the intermediate court of appeal to consider the remaining issues in the appeal.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parents filed a medical malpractice suit against defendants, a doctor and others. The district court found that the statute was constitutional. The Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Louisiana, reversed the judgment. The parties sought review.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) to be unconstitutional pursuant to La. Const. art. I, § 22. It was well-established that litigants had to raise constitutional challenges in the trial court rather than in the appellate courts, and that the constitutional challenge must have been specially pled and the grounds for the claim particularized. Const. art. I, § 22.


OUTCOME: The writs were granted. The judgment of the court of appeal declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.42(B) to be unconstitutional in violation of La. Const. art. Alex v. Rayne Concrete Serv.


NOS. 2005-C-1457 C/W 2005-C-2344 C/W 2005-C-2520


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-1457 (La. 1/26/07); 951 So. 2d 138; 2007 La. LEXIS 305



January 26, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by Alex v. Rayne Concrete Serv., 2007 La. LEXIS 826 (La., Mar. 30, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ACADIA.
Alex v. Rayne Concrete Serv., 915 So. 2d 931, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2039 (La.App. 3 Cir., Sept. 9, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED TO TRIAL COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual sued defendant concrete company and insurer for work-related injuries suffered on a job site. After an appeal of the jury verdict, the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Acadia (Louisiana) held, inter alia, that the individual was entitled to have his Batson/Edmonson challenge heard on appeal, rather than solely on application for supervisory writ. Certiorari was granted on the parties' consolidated writ applications.


OVERVIEW: The primary legal issue was the proper procedural mechanism by which a party could seek review of a Batson/Edmonson challenge in a civil case. An intermediate appellate court was allowed to review a Batson/Edmonson challenge in a civil case on supervisory writ application or on appeal as that practice was in line with the procedure utilized in criminal cases and was consistent with the practice regarding challenges for cause in civil cases and challenges in federal courts. On the merits, the lower court's ruling that the trial court erred in granting a peremptory challenge of two prospective jurors was affirmed. However, the concrete company's reasons were not sufficient as to one prospective juror to meet the Batson/Edmonson standard. Because the trial court was manifestly erroneous in finding that the individual did not carry his burden of proving purposeful discrimination as to that juror, the lower court erred in conducting a de novo review of the record and in rendering judgment. Instead, the matter was remanded so the trial court could conduct a new trial.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the lower court's consideration of the Batson/Edmonson ruling on appeal and its ultimate conclusion that the concrete company's reasons in support of peremptory challenges against two prospective jurors was sufficient. The judgment was reversed as to the lower court's conduct of a de novo review in rendering judgment. The case was remanded so the trial court could conduct a new trial.

State v. Draughn


NO. 2005-KA-1825


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-1825 (La. 01/17/07); 950 So. 2d 583; 2007 La. LEXIS 10



January 17, 2007, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication March 30, 2007.
Rehearing denied by State v. Draughn, 2007 La. LEXIS 827 (La., Mar. 30, 2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Draughn v. La., 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11989 (U.S., Nov. 5, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF CADDO HONORABLE LEON EMANUEL, III, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to La. Const. art. 5, § 5(D), defendant appealed a judgment of the First Judicial District Court for the Parish of Caddo (Louisiana), convicting him of first-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for stabbing the 64-year-old victim to death, allegedly while attempting a robbery. On appeal, the court held that the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction because: (1) specific intent to kill or inflict great bodily harm on the victim could be inferred from the fact that the perpetrator stabbed or cut the victim 61 times; (2) a rational juror could have reasonably found proven beyond a reasonable doubt that the victim's $ 20 was taken from her, as defendant's blood was found near the victim's purse and its contents, and the victim's wallet and checkbook contained no money, credit cards, or checks; (3) the fact that the stab wounds to the victim's face and neck were almost exclusively to her right side, showing that the perpetrator knew that the victim could only see out of her right eye and did not want the victim to identify him; (4) there was evidence that the victim would not open her door to a stranger; (5) there was no forced entry into the victim's home; and (6) defendant's DNA was found at the scene in eight locations.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


06-0575 (La. 11/29/06); 943 So. 2d 1028; 2006 La. LEXIS 3304; 25 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1339; 153 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P60,313



November 29, 2006, Decided

On remand at Marks v. New Orleans Police Dep't, 2007 La. App. LEXIS 495 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 28, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, ORLEANS CIVIL SERVICE COMMISSION.

DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Orleans Civil Service Commission affirmed a hearing examiner's decision upholding a police officer's suspension but finding that his termination was unjustified. The Fourth Circuit Court of Appeal reversed, holding that appellant police department circumvented the minimum standards of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:2531(B)(7) by not acting within 60 days. The police department filed a petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The police department suspended and terminated the police officer after he took an unmarked police vehicle out of state without permission and obtained a speeding ticket. A hearing examiner recommended that the suspension be upheld, even though the department's investigation was not completed within 60 days as required by § 40:2531(B)(7), because the officer was not prejudiced by the delay, and the Commission agreed. On appeal of the reviewing court's judgment, the court reversed. The court held that because § 40:2531(B)(7) did not provide a penalty provision, and because the hearing examiner determined that the officer was not prejudiced by the delay, the reviewing court erred by imposing the penalty of dismissal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case was remanded for consideration of the police department's other assignments of error.

 

163 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Voicestream GSM I Operating Co., LLC v. La. PSC


05-CA-2578, c/w, 05-CA-2579


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-2578 (La. 11/29/06); 943 So. 2d 349; 2006 La. LEXIS 3306



November 29, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 13, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE HONORABLE WILLIAM A. MORVANT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff wireless carriers filed a direct appeal of a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which declared that a state universal service fee (SUSF) was not a tax and therefore was within the authority and jurisdiction of defendant, the Louisiana Public Service Commission (LPSC), granted by the Louisiana Constitution and the Federal Telecommunications Act of 1996.


OVERVIEW: The LPSC's order mandated that all telecommunications service providers, including the wireless carriers, were to contribute to the SUSF. The carriers had filed a petition for declaratory judgment and injunctive relief under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 49:963, seeking to enjoin the enforcement of the order. The lower court granted LPSC's motion for partial summary judgment and denied the carriers' request for a preliminary injunction under La. Code Civ. Proc. art. 3601. On review, the court affirmed, finding that the SUSF assessment was a subsidy assessment that did not constitute an improper tax in violation of La. Const. art. IV, § 21 and art. VII, § 1. The contributions associated with the SUSF were imposed only on end-user revenues from the carriers and were not intended to raise revenue. Rather, the LPSC was using its regulatory authority to allocate the costs for the administration of a regulatory program as permitted under the Telecommunications Act of 1996, specifically 47 U.S.C.S. §§ 253, 254. Thus, there was no showing that the LPSC's implementation of the SUSF was arbitrary, capricious, or a clear abuse of discretion or not based on the factual evidence presented.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision.

 

164 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Batiste


NO. 2005-K-1571


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-1571 (La. 10/17/2006); 939 So. 2d 1245; 2006 La. LEXIS 2876



October 17, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF REVIEW TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS. ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
State v. Batiste, 904 So. 2d 766, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1578 (La.App. 4 Cir., May 11, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State filed a petition for a writ of certiorari to challenge a decision from the Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana), which affirmed a lower court's decision to grant defendant's motion to quash a bill of information in a case alleging video voyeurism.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a bill of information alleging video voyeurism. The State entered a nolle prosequi, but later reinstated the charge. The district court quashed the bill of information, and the court of appeal found no error. In reversing, the supreme court determined that the dismissal of a case was not a bar to subsequent prosecution under La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 693 absent certain limited exceptions. However, a motion to quash was appropriate in certain cases if the prosecutor was favoring the State at the expense of defendant. In this case, the nolle prosequi was entered because the victim was not present for trial and was wavering in her commitment to going forward with the case. The State did not violate any of the time constraints imposed by La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 578. As such, it was an abuse of discretion to grant the motion to quash. Next, the speedy trial rights applied to the states by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment were not violated. The four Barker factors were analyzed. The 19-month delay was attributable to both parties, the right was not asserted until a motion to quash was filed, and defendant suffered no prejudice to his case.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the lower courts were reversed, and the matter was remanded to the district court for further proceedings.

Bush v. Nat'l Health Care


NO. 05-C-2477


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-2477 (La. 10/17/2006); 939 So. 2d 1216; 2006 La. LEXIS 2883



October 17, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF VERNON, STATE OF LOUISIANA.
Bush v. Nat'l Health Care, 923 So. 2d 150, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2301 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 2, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A doctor filed a petition for a writ of certiorari to challenge a decision from a Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Vernon (Louisiana), which denied the doctor's claim of prescription in a medical malpractice case filed by plaintiff parents and affirmed a trial court's decision on liability and damages.


OVERVIEW: The parents alleged that the doctor unnecessarily delayed their son's transfer to another medical facility, which caused the loss of a testicle. They filed a medical malpractice case against the doctor exactly one year later, but filed a patient compensation fund claim more than one year later. The court case was dismissed due to prematurity until the medical review panel issued an opinion. Thereafter, the parents filed another court action, and the doctor's exception of prescription was denied. The court of appeal affirmed, and the doctor sought review. In reversing, the supreme court determined that the court of appeal erred by failing to hold that the LeBreton case applied retroactively. The supreme court analyzed the three Lovell factors in making its determination, which included the establishment of a new principal of law, the prior history of the rule in question, and the inequity imposed by retroactive application. The filing of the claim before the panel suspended prescription under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:1299.47(A)(2)(a). Because retroactive application was warranted, the exception of prescription was sustained.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeal was reversed.

 

166 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers


NO. 05-C-2274


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-2274 (La. 10/17/2006); 945 So. 2d 665; 2006 La. LEXIS 2881



October 17, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF LIVINGSTON.
Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 927 So. 2d 328, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2018 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 25, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, an economic development district requested a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal First Circuit, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court granting the motion to strike challenges by defendant citizens to a bond resolution.


OVERVIEW: The district was a political subdivision of the State, created to facilitate economic growth in an area comprised of 75 acres. The project at issue consisted of a retail outlet and was to be funded to the issuance of bonds by the district through sales tax increments under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.4A. A hearing on the peremptory exception of peremption was held. The court held that the individual defendants did not demonstrate how the right to assert the challenge had an ascertainable monetary value. Because the bonds for which the resolution pertained were issued by a local political subdivision and constituted revenue bonds under a sales tax increment financing plan, both La. Const. art. VI, § 35(B) and La. Rev. Stat. 33:9038.4L were applicable with their respective peremptive periods. The individual defendants failed to challenge the provisions within the 30-day peremptive period, and therefore, the right to challenge the provisions made for the security and payment of the bonds, was perempted. The court found no procedural due process was required beyond that established to notify the public of the resolution by publication in the official journal of the district.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Bd. of Dirs. of the Indus. Dev. Bd. of the City of Gonzales, La., Inc. v. All Taxpayers


No. 2005-C-2298


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-2298 (La. 9/06/06); 938 So. 2d 11; 2006 La. LEXIS 2312



September 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication October 13, 2006.
Rehearing denied by Bd. of Dirs. v. All Taxpayers, 2006 La. LEXIS 2862 (La., Oct. 13, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ASCENSION.
Bd. of Dirs. v. All Taxpayers, 929 So. 2d 743, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2199 (La.App. 1 Cir., Oct. 7, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant taxpayers sought a writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Ascension (Louisiana), which affirmed the judgment of the trial court holding that the Tax Increment Financing Act (TIF Act), La. Rev. Stat. § 33:90381 et seq., did not violate La. Const. art. VII, § 14. The action arose when plaintiff city, pursuant to the TIF Act, resolved to issue tax increment revenue bonds.


OVERVIEW: After making agreements with the State and some retail establishments to issue tax increments, the city adopted Gonzales, La., Ordinance no. 2820 creating an economic district. The city filed a petition for motion for judgment seeking a declaration of the validity of the project. The taxpayers filed a response. The court affirmed, and held: (1) the project at issue was authorized by the TIF Act; (2) La. Const. art. VII, § 14 sought to prohibit a gratuitous alienation of public property; (3) the project did not constitute a prohibited loan, pledge or donation of public funds in that the project documents clearly stated that the bonds were not secured by the full faith and credit of the state or of any political subdivision; (4) the agreements indicated that the project would bring substantial employment opportunities for the citizens of Louisiana; (5) the taxpayers failed to establish equal protection violation because the TIF Act was enacted to promote economic development, which served private businesses as well as the public interest, and as such, it was rationally related to legitimate governmental interests.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals.

State v. All Prop. & Cas. Ins. Carriers Authorized & Licensed to do Business in Louisiana


No. 2006-CD-2030


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2006-2030 (La. 08/25/2006); 937 So. 2d 313; 2006 La. LEXIS 2214



August 25, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 25, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, THE HONORABLE KAY BATES, PRESIDING.
State v. All Prop. & Cas. Ins. Carriers, 936 So. 2d 807, 2006 La. LEXIS 2314 (La., Aug. 22, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurance companies filed a petition for Writ of Certiorari to the Nineteenth Judicial District Court (Louisiana), which found that 2006 La. Acts 729 and 802 extending the prescriptive periods under which certain insurance claims arising from two hurricanes could be filed and which might have altered the contractual provisions of insurance policies regarding the time period in which to bring a claim, were constitutional.


OVERVIEW: In the aftermath of two devastating hurricanes that caused extensive property damage and displacement of citizens of Louisiana, the governor issued executive orders that resulted in the Acts at issue. The court affirmed, and held that the Acts, including the resultant La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:658.3, indicated the intent that the provisions be applied both retroactively and prospectively for the types of claims described therein. Also, the Acts were substantive in nature. The Acts did not violate the Contracts Clause of the U.S. or Louisiana Constitutions because, while the extension of the prescriptive period in which to file claims constituted a substantial impairment of the contractual relationship between the insurers and their policyholders, they were enacted to protect the health and general welfare of the citizens. Further, the extension of the prescriptive period was based upon a legitimate public purpose, and the substantial impairment was of the type that could be anticipated in the industry. The court also held that no Supremacy Clause violation occurred because the Legislature made no attempt to regulate the federally-regulated National Flood Insurance Program.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

169 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turner


NO. 2005-KA-2425


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-2425 (La. 07/10/2006); 936 So. 2d 89; 2006 La. LEXIS 2133



July 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Turner, 2006 La. LEXIS 2452 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turner v. Louisiana, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 3188 (U.S., Mar. 19, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE ELEVENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF SABINE, HONORABLE STEPHEN B. BEASLEY, JUDGE.
State v. Turner, 922 So. 2d 527, 2006 La. LEXIS 281 (La., Jan. 27, 2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with two counts of first-degree murder and filed its notice of intent to seek the death penalty. Defendant claimed he was mentally retarded and thus not subject to a sentence of death and filed a motion to declare unconstitutional La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.5.1. La. The Eleventh Judicial District Court of Sabine Parish, Louisiana, declared art. 905.5.1 unconstitutional, and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the State challenged the trial court's findings that La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.5.1 was unconstitutional. The supreme court held that the trial court erred in declaring the article unconstitutional as the legislature's choice of permitting the issue of whether defendant was mentally retarded (and thus not subject to a death sentence) to be submitted to the jury did not offend constitutional guarantees; nothing in the U.S. Supreme Court's jurisprudence suggested that requiring the jury rather than the trial court to decide whether defendant had established mental retardation violated due process or U.S. Const. amend. VIII. Defendant failed to show that the article was facially unconstitutional and that it seriously affected his rights, as required for a person to have standing to bring a constitutional challenge. His challenge to La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 905.5.1(G) was speculative because the trial court had taken no action that precluded it from either conducting a pretrial hearing on the issue of mental retardation or instructing the jury of the prohibition of executing the mentally retarded.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the matter was remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Leger


NO. 2005-KA-0011


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-0011 (La. 07/10/2006); 936 So. 2d 108; 2006 La. LEXIS 2146



July 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by State v. Leger, 2006 La. LEXIS 2446 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Leger v. Louisiana, 549 U.S. 1221, 127 S. Ct. 1279, 167 L. Ed. 2d 100, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 2289 (2007)
Writ denied by State ex rel. Leger v. State, 135 So. 3d 631, 2014 La. LEXIS 799 (La., 2014)
Writ denied by State v. Leger, 2015 La. LEXIS 1531 (La., June 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE SIXTEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ST. MARY. HONORABLE CHARLES L. PORTER, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the 16th Judicial District Court for the Parish of St. Mary (Louisiana) convicting him of first-degree murder in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:30 and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting the victim to death while trying to recapture his ex-girlfriend who had jumped out of a van after being kidnapped by defendant. On appeal, the court held that even though the trial court erred by admitting into evidence a statement defendant made to police officers during an interrogation because the officers failed to honor defendant's invocation of his right to remain silent, the error was harmless because the State presented overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. Defendant's ex-girlfriend positively identified him as the person who tied her up and kidnapped her at gunpoint, and the victim's wife, who was also shot by defendant, identified him as the shooter. Evidence obtained from defendant's home and vehicle corroborated the ex-girlfriend's account. The trial court did not err by admitting into evidence statements defendant made while being booked because the statements were not the product of a custodial interrogation. The officer specifically informed defendant that he was not there to obtain a statement and it was defendant who initiated asking questions about the crime.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence were affirmed.

In re Melancon


05-CA-1702


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-1702 (La. 07/10/2006); 935 So. 2d 661; 2006 La. LEXIS 2141



July 10, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing denied by In re Melancon, 2006 La. LEXIS 2449 (La., Sept. 1, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM TWENTY-FIRST JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF TANGIPAHOA, HON. WAYNE RAY CHUTZ, PRESIDING.
In re Melancon, 916 So. 2d 122, 2005 La. LEXIS 2710 (La., Nov. 28, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; PETITION DISMISSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In petitioner employee's action for a declaratory judgment, respondent Louisiana Office of Workers' Compensation Administration (OWCA) challenged a judgment of the Twenty-First Judicial District Court, Tangipahoa Parish (Louisiana) that declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208(E) unconstitutional and issued an injunction permanently enjoining the OWCA from enforcing or implementing the fraud forfeiture provisions of § 23:1208(E).


OVERVIEW: The employee had filed a claim for workers' compensation benefits, and the employer responded, asserting that the employee violated the fraud provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 23:1208 that provided for a forfeiture of benefits. The employee filed a petition for a declaratory judgment declaring that § 1208(E) violated his equal protection rights. The trial court held that § 1208(E) was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that the record provided no basis for the trial court's judgment. The court found that the employee's petition was the only pleading of record and that the employee failed to establish that he had standing to challenge the constitutionality of § 23:1208 by presenting evidence or documents to show he was a person whose legal relations were affected by § 23:1208 as required by La. Code Civ. Proc. Ann. art. 1872. Therefore the court held that it could not be judicially determined that § 23:1208 violated the employee's equal protection rights. The court noted that the employee failed to present evidence to show he was an employee; that he had filed a workers' compensation claim; or that the employer had filed a fraud counterclaim under § 23:1208.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and dismissed the employee's petition for a declaratory judgment.

 

172 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Brisco


No. 04-K-3039


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-3039 (La. 07/06/2006); 933 So. 2d 754; 2006 La. LEXIS 2132



July 6, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication July 20, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Iberia.
State v. Brisco, 887 So. 2d 660, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2701 (La.App. 3 Cir., Nov. 10, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; SENTENCE REINSTATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of assault by drive-by shooting in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:37.1. The Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Iberia, Louisiana, affirmed defendant's conviction but vacated his five-year sentence and remanded the case for resentencing. The State petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for shooting into the home where his wife and children were staying. The appellate court vacated defendant's sentence on the ground that the firearm sentencing provisions set out in La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. art. 893.1 et seq., did not apply and that the trial court was not required to impose the maximum sentence as mandated by art. 893.3(C). On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the State could invoke the firearm sentencing provisions of art. 893.1 et seq., even though an element of assault by drive-by shooting also formed the basis for limiting the discretion of the trial court in sentencing. When the legislature amended the firearm sentencing provisions it clearly intended that they apply to felonies defined as crimes of violence by La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:2(13), and among the felonies enumerated was assault by drive-by shooting under § 14:2(13)(bb). Therefore, the legislature intended that the prosecution have the discretion to invoke the firearm sentencing provisions despite the fact that discharge of a firearm was an essential element of the underlying offense.


OUTCOME: The judgment vacating defendant's sentence was reversed, and his five-year sentence was reinstated.

 

173 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Word of Life Christian Ctr. v. West


2004-C-1484


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2004-1484 (La. 04/17/2006); 936 So. 2d 1226; 2006 La. LEXIS 1190



April 17, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected May 18, 2006. Released for Publication September 15, 2006.
Rehearing granted by, Clarified by Word of Life Christian Ctr. v. West, 936 So. 2d 1226, 2006 La. LEXIS 2567 (La., Sept. 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ASCENSION.
Word of Life Christian Ctr. v. West, 879 So. 2d 213, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1252 (La.App. 1 Cir., May 14, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Louisiana trial court granted appellee church's motion for summary judgment and denied the motion for partial summary judgment brought by appellant, Ascension Parish, Louisiana, Sales and Use Tax Authority (parish), on the parish's sales/use tax assessment against the church in connection with the purchase and use of airplanes. The court of appeals affirmed. The parish petitioned for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The parish argued that a "taxable moment" occurred when the church's airplanes were withdrawn from intestate transportation and came to rest in Louisiana. The supreme court noted that if the church or similar resident consumers could travel out-of-state and purchase airplanes or other tangible personal property and not pay a sales or use tax, then import those goods into Louisiana for subsequent use in interstate commerce, and be immune from Louisiana use tax because they ultimately used, or planned to use, the goods in interstate commerce, then they effectively circumvented decades of use tax jurisprudence. Once the planes were imported and hangared in Louisiana, when they had been withdrawn from interstate commerce and came to rest in Louisiana, Louisiana's tax on storage and use was effective and a taxable moment occurred in Louisiana. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305(E) spoke to taxing both planes in Louisiana since they came to rest there and became a part of the mass of Louisiana property. Because the taxable moment contemplated by the parish ordinances did not occur in Ascension Parish, it did not have the statutory authority to impose a use tax on the airplanes.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Sherman


NO. 05-K-0779


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-0779 (La. 04/04/2006); 931 So. 2d 286; 2006 La. LEXIS 1096



April 4, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Sherman, 2006 La. LEXIS 2129 (La., June 30, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF RAPIDES.
State v. Sherman, 896 So. 2d 1194, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 514 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 2, 2005)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Court of Appeal for the Third Circuit, Parish of Rapides (Louisiana) reversing defendant's conviction for possession of a Schedule II controlled dangerous substance with intent to distribute under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967 on the ground that defendant's motion to suppress should have been granted.


OVERVIEW: Officers approached defendant after observing that his motorcycle was partially parked on a road's shoulder. One officer asked defendant if he had a driver's license; defendant responded that he did not. While searching defendant, the officers found a bag containing several rocks of crack cocaine and arrested him. On appeal of defendant's conviction, the appellate court held that his motion to suppress the cocaine should have been granted. The court disagreed and reversed. The court held that probable cause to arrest defendant existed for driving without a license under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 32:402B(1) when defendant stated that he did not have a driver's license. The officers' search of defendant was proper, given that it was a search incident to a lawful arrest, even though the arrest had not yet taken place, because the search did not serve as part of the arrest's justification.


OUTCOME: The judgment reversing defendant's conviction was reversed, and the trial court's judgment was reinstated. The case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

Badeaux v. Southwest Computer Bureau, Inc.


No. 05-CA-0612 c/w 05-CA-0719


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-0612 (La. 03/17/2006); 929 So. 2d 1211; 2006 La. LEXIS 776



March 17, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication June 23, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ASCENSION, HONORABLE PEGRAM MIRE, JR., JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; VACATED IN PART; and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant couple brought a defamation action against appellee company. A claim was made under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 18:1463. The husband was an election candidate but that had not been asserted in the complaint. The 23rd Judicial District Court, Parish of Ascension (Louisiana) sustained the exceptions of no right of action and no cause of action, declared § 18:1463 unconstitutional, and dismissed the claims with prejudice. The couple appealed.


OVERVIEW: The couple had established a right of action in their suit. They clearly belonged to the class of persons that had a legal interest in the subject matter of the litigation at issue. However, they failed to state a cause of action for damages under § 18:1463 because the statute exclusively provided injunctive relief and granted no other civil remedy to them. In their petition, the couple sought damages, which were not recoverable under § 18:1463. Even if the petition sought injunctive relief, the couple would not have been entitled to injunctive relief because the election was over and the husband was no longer an affected candidate. The district court could have resolved the issue of whether the couple stated a cause of action for defamation under § 18:1463 on nonconstitutional grounds and should have done so. And, because their petition had not alleged facts sufficient to establish the general tort of defamation, the couple should have been granted leave to amend the petition to state a cause of action for the general tort of defamation, without consideration of the constitutionality of § 18:1463. The district court's declaration of unconstitutionality was premature.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment granting the company's exceptions of no right of action and no cause of action was reversed. The case was remanded to allow the couple leave to amend the petition to state a cause of action for the general tort of defamation. The district court's declaration of unconstitutionality was vacated.

 

176 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Beauclaire v. Greenhouse


No. 2005-CA-0765


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2005-0765 (La. 02/22/2006); 922 So. 2d 501; 2006 La. LEXIS 647



February 22, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Appeal from the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles. Honorable Mark A. Jeansonne, Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a school board and a bus driver, appealed a decision of the Twelfth Judicial District Court for the Parish of Avoyelles (Louisiana) granting the motion to strike the jury filed by plaintiffs, a husband and wife, in plaintiffs action resulting from a vehicular accident between plaintiffs and a school bus driven by the driver.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs argued that defendants failed to comply with the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:5105, and further, that § 13:5105(D) was an unconstitutional deprivation of their right to equal protection under La. Const. art. I, § 3. The trial court found that the statute violated plaintiffs' right to equal protection. The court noted that the waiver against the prohibition of a jury trial did not select the mode of trial; it merely allowed the possibility of trial by jury. The court held that the third level of scrutiny applied. The court had previously found that § 13:5105(D) applied in every possible locality throughout the state as well as to every political subdivision in the state. The school board waived the prohibition against civil jury trials by resolution passed prior to plaintiffs filing suit. Thus, the waiver was in effect prior to suit being filed. The court found that at the time suit was filed either party was entitled to request a jury trial. Thus, there was no discrimination. Because both parties had equal access to a jury trial, and were treated the same, there was no violation of the equal protection clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court.

Savage v. Prator


No. 04-C-2904


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-2904 (La. 01/19/2006); 921 So. 2d 51; 2006 La. LEXIS 145



January 19, 2006, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO.
Savage v. Prator, 886 So. 2d 523, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2370 (La.App. 2 Cir., Oct. 6, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED; INJUNCTION VACATED; REMANDED TO DISTRICT COURT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After being informed by appellant sheriff's office that an ordinance prohibiting cockfighting would be enforced, respondent game clubs filed a petition seeking injunctive relief and a declaration that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The trial court found that appellant Parish improperly invaded the state's police power by enacting the ordinance; the Second Circuit Court of Appeal, Caddo Parish, Louisiana, affirmed. The Parish sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the Parish challenged the appellate court's holding that Caddo Parish, La., Ordinance No. 2432 (an animal cruelty ordinance which extended its protections to "fowl") contradicted the state's animal cruelty statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:102.1, which exempted "fowl" from its applicable provisions. The clubs suggested that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 14:102.1(D) legislatively excluded "fowl" from the provisions of the statute, indicating the legislature's implicit endorsement of cockfighting. The supreme court disagreed with the clubs, finding that the state had passed no general law which could be interpreted as an attempt to preempt the field with regard to authorizing, prohibiting, or regulating cockfighting. Local governments therefore could authorize or prohibit the conduct of cockfighting tournaments within municipal boundaries. As such, the supreme court held that Caddo Parish, La., Ordinance No. 2432, § 4-14 prohibiting cockfighting did not offend a Louisiana constitutional or statutory provision. And as there was no unconstitutionality or illegality regarding the ordinance, the preliminary injunction preventing the enforcement of the ordinance was improper.


OUTCOME: The rulings of the lower courts were reversed, the preliminary injunction was vacated, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

State v. Scott


No. 04-KA-1312


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-1312 (La. 01/19/2006); 921 So. 2d 904; 2006 La. LEXIS 148



January 19, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1]
Rehearing denied by State v. Scott, 2006 La. LEXIS 767 (La., Mar. 10, 2006)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Scott v. La., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 6759 (U.S., Oct. 2, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE TWENTY-THIRD JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ASSUMPTION, HONORABLE ALVIN TURNER, JR., JUDGE.
State v. Dunn, 831 So. 2d 862, 2002 La. LEXIS 3065 (La., Nov. 1, 2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Twenty-Third Judicial District Court, Parish of Assumption, (Louisiana) of two counts of first degree murder. Defendant was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the removal of his appointed counsel unconstitutionally interfered with the attorney-client relationship and violated his right to counsel of choice. The supreme court disagreed. The relationship between lead counsel and associate counsel had deteriorated and they could not work together to represent defendant. It was reasonable for the district court to retain lead counsel and to substitute associate counsel because the district court specifically found that lead counsel had filed all the necessary motions for the defense, including a successful motion for a change of venue, and had "gone beyond the call of duty" in her representation. The district court had defendant's letter expressing his desire that associate counsel remain on his case, and was therefore aware of his position on the issue. Additionally, defendant was present at the hearing on the motion to substitute lead counsel and to vacate the order substituting another attorney for associate counsel. Additionally, the supreme court found that the record contained reasonable grounds to doubt whether defendant was mentally retarded and exempt from capital punishment.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed. The case was remand for a hearing to determine whether defendant was mentally retarded such that he was exempt from the death penalty.

State v. Jackson


No. 2004-K-2863


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2004-2863 (La. 11/29/2005); 916 So. 2d 1015; 2005 La. LEXIS 2483



November 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication December 13, 2005.
On remand at State v. Jackson, 925 So. 2d 54, 2006 La. App. LEXIS 505 (La.App. 2 Cir., Mar. 8, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF OUACHITA.
State v. Jackson, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 3266 (La.App. 2 Cir., Nov. 11, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by bill of information in the Fourth Judicial District Court, Parish of Ouachita, Louisiana, with several offenses, including attempted first degree murder of a peace officer. Defendant entered a plea to aggravated assault on a peace officer. Defendant appealed his sentence. The Louisiana Court of Appeals found that the trial court was without jurisdiction to accept the plea. The State sought certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The only facts of relevance were that the defendant knowingly and voluntarily pleaded guilty to aggravated assault upon a peace officer with a firearm after being charged by bill of information with attempted first degree murder of a peace officer. Certiorari was granted to consider whether a trial judge lacked jurisdiction to accept a defendant's informed and voluntary guilty plea to a crime that was not responsive to the crime charged in the bill of information when the district attorney had not filed a written amendment to the bill. The supreme court also considered whether the trial judge's acceptance of such a plea was an error patent that required reversal of the conviction on appeal. The supreme court noted that in this case defendant stood by his plea on appeal and in argument before the lower appellate court. The failure of the district attorney to amend the bill to conform to the plea agreement under these circumstances could not be considered to render the plea unintelligent or involuntary. The trial judge was not without jurisdiction to accept a defendant's knowing and voluntary guilty plea simply because the plea was unresponsive to the charges.


OUTCOME: The supreme court reversed the judgment and the matter was remanded to the court of appeal for consideration of defendant's appeal.

In re Jordan


NO. 04-B-2397


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-2397 (La. 06/29/2005);  913 So. 2d 775; 2005 La. LEXIS 2104



June 29, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1]
State v. Cousin, 710 So. 2d 1065, 1998 La. LEXIS 980 (La., Apr. 14, 1998)



DISPOSITION: Roger W. Jordan, Jr., Louisiana Bar Roll number 19642, is suspended from the practice of law for a period of three months.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Louisiana Office of Disciplinary Counsel (ODC) filed a disciplinary proceeding against respondent attorney. The ODC filed an objection to a finding that the attorney did not violate the Louisiana Rules of Professional Conduct and to the dismissal of the formal charges.


OVERVIEW: The attorney, an experienced prosecutor, was the senior counsel in a death penalty case. He obtained a statement from a witness regarding an identification. However, he failed to disclose this information to the defense, as required by La. St. Bar art. XVI, R. 3.8. After the murder conviction was overturned, disciplinary proceedings were instituted against the attorney. In imposing a suspension, the court determined that a prosecutor had a duty to disclose exculpatory evidence under Brady and La. Code Crim. Proc. Ann. arts. 718, 719(a), 722. The statement in question was covered by Brady because there was a reasonable probability that the proceeding would have been different had the evidence been disclosed to the defense. The record showed that the witness in question was the only one that positively identified defendant as the shooter. The court looked to La. Sup. Ct. R. XIX, § 10(C) in deciding the appropriate sanction for the knowing violation. The only aggravating circumstances was the attorney's substantial experience as a prosecutor. There were many mitigating circumstances. As such, the period of suspension was deferred in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The court entered an order suspending the attorney from the practice of law for three months. The suspension was deferred in its entirety subject to no further misconduct by the attorney in a subsequent one-year period.

 

181 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Skipper


NO. 04-KA-2137


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-2137 (La. 06/29/2005);  906 So. 2d 399; 2005 La. LEXIS 2103



June 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Appeal from the Criminal District Court, for the Parish of Orleans, Honorable Frank D. Marullo, Judge.



DISPOSITION: GRANTING OF MOTION TO QUASH BILL OF INFORMATION AFFIRMED; RULING FINDING LA. R.S. 40:982 TO BE UNCONSTITUTIONAL REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Criminal District Court, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) granted defendant's motion to quash an information charging him with being a second felony drug offender and declared unconstitutional La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:982. By placing the fact of his prior conviction in the bill of information for possession of cocaine, a violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, his federal and state constitutional rights were violated. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: Section 40:982 granted to the State the right to seek an enhanced sentence when a person was convicted of a drug-related offense if, prior to the commission of the instant conviction, the offender had been convicted of any other drug-related offense. The issue was whether § 40:982 created an additional substantive element to the charged offense, which had to be placed in the bill of information, read to the jury, proven at trial, and found by the jury beyond a reasonable doubt, or whether it was a sentencing enhancement provision, subject to a separate proceeding after conviction which was not presented to the jury before a determination of guilt was made. Resolving a split among the circuits, the Supreme Court of Louisiana held that § 40:982, when properly applied, was a sentencing enhancement to be implemented after conviction similar to the Habitual Offender Law, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:529.1, and was constitutional. La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:982 was not a substantive element of the instant drug-related offense which it sought to enhance, possession of cocaine in violation of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 40:967, and thus the prior conviction should not have been in the information.


OUTCOME: The granting of the motion to quash was affirmed and the trial court's determination of the statute's unconstitutionality was reversed.

 

182 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Allen


NO. 03-KA-2418


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


03-2418 (La. 06/29/2005); 913 So. 2d 788; 2005 La. LEXIS 2107



June 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Allen v. La., 2006 U.S. LEXIS 3892 (U.S., May 15, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE THIRTY-NINTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF RED RIVER HONORABLE LEWIS O. SAMS, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. [Pg 37].


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Thirty-Ninth Judicial District Court, Parish of Red River (Louisiana) of first degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that five of the State's peremptory challenges were made on the basis of race and the prosecutor repeatedly misrepresented the record and gave other pretextual reasons for striking African-American prospective jurors. The supreme court disagreed. The jury seated consisted of nine white jurors and three African-American jurors. Towards the end of voir dire, the defense made one Batson challenge. At the time the defense lodged the challenge, nine jurors had been chosen, three of whom were African-Americans. In total, the State exercised ten peremptory challenges. It excused five white jurors and five African-American jurors. The defense exercised nine peremptory challenges, all against white jurors. The State proffered non-racial reasons for its peremptory strikes of all five African-American jurors. The defense's Batson challenge had already failed when the State proffered its reasons because the trial court clearly found no discernible pattern of discriminatory intent. Thus the burden never shifted to the prosecution to explain the racial exclusion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

183 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers


NO. 05-CA-0374


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-0374 (La. 06/29/2005);  908 So. 2d 623; 2005 La. LEXIS 2092



June 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication August 10, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
World Trade Ctr. Taxing Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 894 So. 2d 1185, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 296 (La.App. 4 Cir., Feb. 1, 2005)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.21 A, created appellant World Trade Center Taxing District, a special taxing district. The district filed a motion for judgment on the statute's validity. The trial court found it valid. Appellee intervenor hotel association appealed. The Court of Appeal, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) found the statute unconstitutional as it created an exemption from the hotel occupancy tax. The district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The court of appeal held the WTC tax increment financing (TIF) statute unconstitutional as a special law in violation of La. Const. art. III, § 12(A)(7) because it created an exemption from the hotel occupancy tax where certain proceeds of the tax presently secured outstanding bonds and, additionally, the exemption was not uniform, in violation of La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D). The Supreme Court of Louisiana held that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.21 created an exemption from the hotel occupancy taxes that the proposed hotel in the WTC taxing district would otherwise have been subject to. But for the WTC TIF statute, the Orleans Parish hotel occupancy taxes would have been collected when the WTC hotel began functioning. The hotel occupancy taxes were imposed on all hotels in Orleans Parish; to prevent the levy of a hotel occupancy tax on a hotel in Orleans Parish involved the enactment of an exemption. The legislature was prohibited under La. Const. art. VI, § 29(D) from enacting tax exemptions where those taxes secured bonds already authorized. The unconstitutional portion of the statute was not severable, thus La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.21 was unconstitutional in its entirety.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

184 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Mallard Bay Drilling, Inc. v. Kennedy


No. 2004-C-1089


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2004 1089 (La. 06/29/2005); 914 So. 2d 533; 2005 La. LEXIS 2101



June 29, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF IBERIA.
Mallard Bay Drilling, Inc. v. Kennedy, 869 So. 2d 954, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 699 (La.App. 3 Cir., Mar. 31, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, Third Circuit, Parish of Iberia, Louisiana, appellant department of revenue (DOR) challenged the decision affirming the judgment of the district court granting the refund requested by respondent corporate taxpayer on its claim for tax paid on purchases of diesel fuel used for production of motive power on the taxpayer's drilling barges.


OVERVIEW: The issues involved whether 2002 La. Acts 40, amending La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.1, could be applied retroactively and also the imposition of sales taxes on diesel fuel sold, delivered, and consumed in Louisiana by drilling barges in the court of their offshore drilling activities. The court reversed, and held that because 2002 La. Acts 40 represented new substantive law passed under the guise of interpretive legislation, it could only have prospective effect and could not be applied in the case. The district court and the court of appeal focused exclusively on the third element of the exemption under La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:305.1(B) and failed to specifically consider whether the drilling barges were "ships or vessels." The drilling barges could not move under their own power and were towed from one job location to the next, and were thus "barges" rather than "vessels" for purposes of § 47:305.1. Further, the board of tax appeals' findings that the fuel was sold, delivered, and consumed in Louisiana were adequately supported by the record. When the fuel was consumed in the taxpayer's drilling operations in Louisiana, it came to rest and became a part of the state's property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the court of appeals.

 

185 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Willis-Knighton Med. Ctr. v. Caddo-Shreveport Sales & Use Tax Comm'n


NO. 04-C-0473


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-0473 (La. 06/22/2005); 903 So. 2d 1071; 2005 La. LEXIS 1973



June 22, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication July 6, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, SECOND CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CADDO.
Willis-Knighton Med. Ctr. v. Caddo-Shreveport Sales & Use Tax Comm'n, 903 So. 2d 1071, 2005 La. LEXIS 804 (La., Apr. 1, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A writ of certiorari for rehearing was filed in the Court of Appeal, Second Circuit, Parish of Caddo (Louisiana) regarding a decision of the Supreme Court of Louisiana in which it had eschewed a disjunctive reading of the two paragraphs of La. Civ. Code Ann. art. 466 and the use of the societal expectations test as a method of determining what was a component part of a building within the meaning of the first paragraph of that article.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court granted rehearing for the sole purpose of considering the retroactivity of its decision insofar as it discussed the proper interpretation of art. 466, and its definition of a component part of an immovable. Weighing the factors whether a judicial decision should be accorded prospective effect only, it concluded that its opinion should be given prospective effect only. While that opinion did not change the substantive law but rather simply applied the law as it had existed since the 1978 Civil Code Revisions, the court noted that Louisiana appellate courts had employed a disjunctive reading of art. 466, and in doing so, had drawn on the societal expectations test as a measure for determining what items could be considered component parts under the first paragraph of art. 466. Because the courts, and no doubt individuals, had relied on that approach, and there was no clear indication that foreshadowed its demise, the supreme court found that the instant case was one which was appropriate for prospective application. The court adhered to its original opinion eschewing a disjunctive reading of the two paragraphs of art. 466 but it was to be applied prospectively.


OUTCOME: The rehearing was granted.

187 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Cunningham


No. 04-KA-2200


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-2200 (La. 06/13/2005); 903 So. 2d 1110; 2005 La. LEXIS 1851



June 13, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Released for Publication June 27, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] ON APPEAL FROM THE APPELLATE DIVISION OF CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS, FRANK MARULLO, JR., CALVIN JOHNSON, AND JULIAN PARKER, JUDGES.

ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE APPELLATE DIVISION OF CRIMINAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF ORLEANS.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the ruling of the Appellate Division of Criminal District Court for the Parish of Orleans (Louisiana) declaring La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:499-501 unconstitutional and reversing defendant's conviction for possession of marijuana. At issue was whether §§ 15:499-501 deprived defendant of the right to confront and cross-examine the witness in violation of U.S. Const. amend. VI and La. Const. art. I, § 16.


OVERVIEW: The statutes in question allowed a certificate of analysis to be accepted by the trial court as prima facie proof of the substance tested without live testimony of the person performing the analysis. The court reversed, holding that the statutes did not infringe upon defendant's constitutional right to confrontation because defendant merely had to subpoena the person who performed the examination or analysis of the evidence. Once a defendant requests the subpoena, the certificate of analysis has no evidentiary value and the State must call the relevant witnesses to prove its case. Because the good-faith certification of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:501(B)(2) was imposed only on defendant and not the State, it was not construed as an unconstitutional violation of the confrontation clause. Consequently, the burden to demonstrate good faith was featherweight so as not to adversely impact defendant's right to confrontation, and defendant, who did not avail himself of the opportunity to subpoena the report-preparer, could have satisfied the good-faith requirement by merely indicating a preference for live testimony.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the court of appeals decision and defendant's conviction and sentence were reinstated. The matter was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Plainview Area Ass'n v. State


NO. 05-CA-0791


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-0791 (La. 04/29/2005); 900 So. 2d 837; 2005 La. LEXIS 1257



April 29, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by Plainview Area Ass'n v. State, 907 So. 2d 923, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 1759 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 29, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] In Re: Appeal from the Eleventh Judicial DIstrict Court for the Parish of Sabine, No. 48,239, Division A; Court of Appeal Third Circuit, No. CA-04-1221.
Plainview Area Ass'n v. State, 832 So. 2d 1172, 2002 La. App. LEXIS 3739 (La.App. 3 Cir., Dec. 11, 2002)



DISPOSITION: Trial court judgment on remand is vacated and set aside. Remanded to address the merits of DOTD's appeal taken from the trial court's original judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The trial court found on remand that the passage of La. Const. art. VII, § 27 and the enactment of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:757 impaired the contract between appellee landowners and appellant State, through the Louisiana Department of Transportation and Development (DOTD). The DOTD appealed. A Court of Appeals (Louisiana) transferred the case to the supreme court.


OVERVIEW: The road was completed by the DOTD in 1960, after which it performed an overlay of the road in 1976. However, no maintenance of the road had been performed since that time. Without addressing the trial court's factual finding that the road was part of the public road system, the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of whether La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 48:757 and La. Const. art. VII, § 27 impaired the contractual relations of the parties and, if so, whether the passage of the statute and the constitutional article were reasonable and necessary in the furtherance of an important public purpose. Pretermitting the merits, the supreme court found that the appellate court erred in remanding the case to the trial court for consideration of the constitutional issues. In the current case, if the appellate court found that the trial court's factual finding that the road was within the public road system was supported by the record, there would have been no need to reach the constitutional issues. Therefore, the appellate court acted prematurely in remanding the case to the trial court for consideration of the constitutional issues.


OUTCOME: The supreme court vacated and set aside the trial court's remand judgment. The case was remanded to the appellate court so that it could to address the merits of the DOTD's appeal taken from the trial court's original judgment.
