Sabine Parish Police Jury v. Comm'r of Alcohol & Tobacco Control


NO. 04-C-1833


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-1833 (La. 04/12/05); 898 So. 2d 1244; 2005 La. LEXIS 941



April 12, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 26, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF SABINE.
Sabine Mfg. v. Sabine Parish Police Jury, 880 So. 2d 871, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1601 (La.App. 3 Cir., June 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner police jury filed a petition against respondent Commissioner of Alcohol and Tobacco Control to prohibit the state from issuing a permit to sell alcohol. Respondent business filed two suits against the police jury and the sheriff for denying the issuance of a permit. The appellate court (Louisiana) affirmed the ruling that the ward adopted the rules governing the sale of alcohol held by the larger election district. A writ was granted.


OVERVIEW: A portion of the ward, which previously voted to prohibit the sale of alcoholic beverages (to become "dry"), had become a part of an election district that never voted to prevent the sale of alcoholic beverages. The police jury argued that La. Rev. Stat. 26:81(B)(1) and La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:273(A)(1) prohibited the state from issuing a permit to sell alcohol in any subdivision of the state where alcohol sales had been prohibited by referendum vote. The supreme court was asked to determine the effect on the local option election after the parish was restructured. At issue was the proper interpretation to be given La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:583 (amended 1997), its relationship to other local option laws, and its application. The supreme court found that the provisions of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:583 dictated that the portion of the ward included in the election district must take on the sales characteristics of the election district. The local option status of the entirety of the election district could be changed only by a referendum election and conducted pursuant to the provisions of the local option laws, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 26:581 et seq. (amended 1997).


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision of the court of appeal, which affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the Commissioner and the business.

 

190 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


State v. Citizen


No. 04-KA-1841


* On September 23, 2004, this Court ordered that this appeal and a writ application filed in State of Louisiana v. Adrian Citizen, 04-KD-1154, be "consolidated for oral argument, hearing, and decision."


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-1841 (La. 04/01/2005); 898 So. 2d 325; 2005 La. LEXIS 805



April 1, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication April 15, 2005.
Later proceeding at State v. Citizen, 916 So. 2d 1040, 2005 La. LEXIS 2601 (La., Dec. 9, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE 14th JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU, HONORABLE ALCIDE GRAY, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated murder cases, defense counsel challenged the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:304 and 15:571.11 in her motion to determine the source of funds to provide a competent defense. The 14th Judicial District Court, Parish of Calcasieu (Louisiana) found that the statutes were unconstitutional and ordered the parish police jury (CPPJ) to make available $ 200,000 for attorney fees. The CPPJ and the State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that because §§ 15:304 and 15:571.11, when read together, barred it from ordering the use of surplus funds to pay the defense costs for indigent defendants, they were unconstitutional. The Supreme Court of Louisiana held that the trial court's ruling that the statutes violated defendants' rights of due process, right to counsel, and equal protection was erroneous. The constitution stated that indigent defendants were entitled to the assistance of counsel and that the legislature had to provide a uniform system for securing and compensating qualified counsel. The statutes clearly meet the constitutional requirements because they, along with La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:144 et seq. and 15:151 et seq., specifically provided the medium for state funding for indigent defense. The next issue was whether the trial court exceeded the constitutional function of the judiciary in ordering the CPPJ to set aside funding for indigent defendants. The legislature clearly determined that the state, not the parishes, would pay for indigent defense pursuant to the mandate of La. Const. art. I, § 13. Thus, the trial court erred in ordering the CPPJ to fund the indigents' defense.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. Unless adequate funds were identified and made available in a manner authorized by law, upon motion of defendants, the trial judge could halt the prosecution of the instant cases until adequate funds became available to provide for the indigent defendants' constitutionally protected right to counsel or take other measures consistent with protecting their constitutional or statutory rights.

Reed v. Reed


NO. 05-CA-0375


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


05-0375 (La. 03/24/05); 897 So. 2d 584; 2005 La. LEXIS 686



March 24, 2005, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] In Re: Appeal from the 32nd Judicial District Court for the Parish of Terrebonne, Division C. No. 129,074.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Louisiana district court declared La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:236.2(C) and (D) to be unconstitutional. The State of Louisiana on behalf of defendant invoked the appellate jurisdiction of the supreme court pursuant to La. Const. art. V, § 5(D).


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that the issue of constitutionality was not properly raised. By failing to specially plead the constitutionality of La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 46:236.2(C) and (D), plaintiff failed to utilize the proper method to challenge constitutionality of these provisions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded to the district court to allow plaintiff to specifically plead the unconstitutionality of the statute and for the issue to be fully litigated.

 

193 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Bridges v. AutoZone Props.


No. 2004-C-0814


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2004-0814 (La. 03/24/2005); 900 So. 2d 784; 2005 La. LEXIS 688



March 24, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication May 13, 2005.
Later proceeding at Bridges v. AutoZone Props., 900 So. 2d 784, 2005 La. LEXIS 1510 (La., May 13, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEAL, FIRST CIRCUIT, PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE.
Bridges v. AutoZone Props., 873 So. 2d 25, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1 (La.App. 1 Cir., Jan. 5, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Revenue sought to recover income taxes and franchise taxes on the properties and taxable capital in Louisiana of respondent, the majority shareholder of a real estate investment trust (REIT). The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, East Baton Rouge Parish, Louisiana, sustained the dismissal of the action for lack of personal jurisdiction. The Department sought certiorari review.


OVERVIEW: The REIT, which organized as a corporation domiciled in Nevada pursuant to 26 U.S.C.S. § 856(a), was not converted to a trust simply by its business operations in Louisiana. Therefore, the state laws applicable to trusts, specifically, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:287.93(A)(7), did not apply to it. However, International Harvesters and similar cases provided constitutional support for the Department's tax assessment against the majority shareholder. There was no question that the state had afforded many protections and benefits, including police protection, fire protection, and street sanitation, to the REIT's 68 retail stores located within its borders. Thus, a nexus existed for jurisdictional purposes, which was not broken by the pass-through nature of the REIT. The majority shareholder owned 100 percent of the REIT. The REIT generated some $10 million of rental income from store locations in Louisiana. Louisiana extended protection and benefits to the REIT. Therefore, International Harvester provided authority for the exercise of jurisdiction under Louisiana's long-arm statute, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 13:3201.


OUTCOME: The lower courts' judgments were reversed, and the case was remanded to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

194 of 2253 DOCUMENTS


Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers


No. 2004-C-1674


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2004-1674 (La. 02/04/05); 894 So. 2d 325; 2005 La. LEXIS 327



February 4, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, 2005 La. App. LEXIS 2018 (La.App. 1 Cir., Aug. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Livingston.
Denham Springs Econ. Dev. Dist. v. All Taxpayers, Property Owners & Citizens of the Denham Springs Economic Dev. Dist., 885 So. 2d 1153, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 1467 (La.App. 1 Cir., June 4, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee economic development district alleged that it was authorized to collect "sales tax increments" used to secure the issuance of bonds for financing a development. Appellant taxpayers contended that the proposed bond issuance was improper. The trial court found that the bonds were valid pursuant to La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 33:9038.4(A)(5). The Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of Livingston (Louisiana) affirmed. The district appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue was whether the taxing authority could use the dedicated funds, previously dedicated to a specified purpose by a vote of the people, for a purpose other than their dedicated use, to fund a new economic development project. The supreme court found that § 33:9038.4, as written, prohibited dedicated taxes from being used for purposes other than their dedicated purpose. Section 33:9038.4(A)(1) gave the district the power to issue bonds; however, § 33:9038.4(A)(5) restricted the use of previously dedicated funds. The provisions of § 33:9038.4(A)(5) clearly indicated that sales tax increments could only be used where such use was permitted by the electorate. That interpretation was consistent with La. Const. art. VI, § 29. Clearly, the voters were never made aware of other permitted uses for the funds and did not agree to other uses. Should the taxing entities seek to redirect the revenue derived from the tax proceeds, they would be required to re-submit a proposition to the voters of the parish for approval. Thus, the court found that § 33:9038.4(A)(5) did not allow taxing entities to pledge or re-direct funds, previously dedicated to other uses absent voter approval.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower courts was reversed.

Unwired Telecom Corp. v. Parish of Calcasieu


No. 03-CA-0732


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


03-0732 (La. 01/19/05); 903 So. 2d 392; 2005 La. LEXIS 121



January 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 2, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, THIRD CIRCUIT, PARISH OF CALCASIEU.
Unwired Telcom Corp. v. Parish of Calcasieu, 2003 La. LEXIS 3452 (La., Dec. 12, 2003)
Unwired Telecom Corp. v. Parish of Calcasieu, 838 So. 2d 854, 2003 La. App. LEXIS 187 (La.App. 3 Cir., Feb. 5, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, reversed in part, and remanded on rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee parish collector assessed use taxes against appellant cellular telephone company. Relying on Mercury Cellular Telephone Co. v. Calcasieu Parish, the trial court ordered the company to pay all assessed use taxes. The Court of Appeal of Louisiana, Third Circuit, Parish of Calcasieu held that 2002 La. Acts 85 retroactively redefining La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 47:301 was unconstitutional. The company appealed.


OVERVIEW: In the limited setting in the instant case, the supreme court found that judicial economy was best served by exercising its supervisory jurisdiction. The company argued that the legislature's provision for the retroactive application of 2002 La. Acts 85 did not violate the Louisiana Constitution. It argued that the legislature did not modify well-established procedures or any applicable tax, but clarified the Mercury court's addition of requirements to the relevant ordinances relative to the taxation of cellular telephones transferred to customers at discounted prices as part of its sales of cellular telecommunication services. The supreme court found that the act was retroactive and that an analysis of the constitutional implications was needed. The legislature had sought to change the Mercury decision. By passing the Act in order to abrogate the appellate court's interpretation and application of a long-standing revised statute, the legislature clearly assumed a function more properly entrusted to the judicial branch of government. Even though the legislature had the authority to change the law after the Mercury, the changes could only have prospective application.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower courts regarding the assessment of interest, penalties, and attorney fees was reversed and the case was remanded to the trial court. In all other respects the judgment of the court of appeal was affirmed.

Champagne v. Ward


No. 2003-CC-3211


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


2003-3211 (La. 01/19/05); 893 So. 2d 773; 2005 La. LEXIS 127



January 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 2, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: ON WRIT OF CERTIORARI FROM THE COURT OF APPEAL, FOURTH CIRCUIT, PARISH OF ORLEANS.
Champagne v. Ward, 866 So. 2d 834, 2004 La. LEXIS 730 (La., Feb. 20, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Reversed; Mississippi law applies.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, a driver injured in Louisiana, was a resident of Mississippi and his vehicle was covered by an insurance policy issued in Mississippi. The driver sought uninsured/underinsured motorist (UM) coverage against appellant insurer. The insurer moved for summary judgment claiming Mississippi law controlled. The trial court denied the motion and the Court of Appeal of Louisiana, Fourth Circuit, Parish of Orleans affirmed. The insurer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The policy contained a clause which reduced the UM coverage by the amount collected from the liability insurance covering the owner of the underinsured vehicle. The issue was whether Louisiana law automatically applied to a foreign UM policy in a multistate case when the accident occurred in Louisiana and involved a Louisiana resident, or whether Louisiana courts had to engage in a choice-of-law analysis to determine which state's law was applicable. Following the legislature's enactment of former La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 22:1406(D)(1)(a)(iii) by 1987 La. Acts 444, courts had differed on the impact of the amendment. The court held that a choice-of-law analysis, codified in La. Civ. Code Ann. arts. 3515 and 3537, was the appropriate way to determine which state's law applied. The court found that Mississippi had a more substantial interest in the uniform application of its laws governing insurance contracts than Louisiana had in providing an insurance remedy to an out-of-state resident injured while transitorily in Louisiana. The application of Louisiana law would have resulted in the abrogation of the Mississippi contract.


OUTCOME: The lower courts' determinations that Louisiana law automatically applied to automobile accidents occurring in Louisiana was reversed.

Cheron v. LCS Corr. Servs.


No. 04-CC-0703


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-0703 (La. 01/19/05); 891 So. 2d 1250; 2005 La. LEXIS 130



January 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 2, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: On Writ of Certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge.
Cheron v. LCS Corr. Serv., 872 So. 2d 1094, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 334 (La.App. 1 Cir., Feb. 23, 2004)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant department of corrections applied for writ of certiorari to the Court of Appeal, First Circuit, Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which concluded that the trial court correctly denied the department's exception of prematurity in plaintiff inmate's action for injuries he allegedly sustained while incarcerated in a correctional facility.


OVERVIEW: The inmate claimed he experienced several severe symptoms while incarcerated and that due to the facility personnel's ignoring of his repeated requests for medical attention, he contracted a potentially fatal kidney disease. The department claimed that the inmate failed to exhaust administrative remedies per La. Rev. Stat. Ann. §§ 15:1172, 15:1184. When the inmate's cause of action arose, La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1172, contained in the Corrections Administrative Remedy Procedure did not require exhaustion of administrative remedies. The court denied the affirmed the decision of the court of appeal, and held that even procedural laws were not accorded retroactive effect where such retroactivity would operate unconstitutionally to disturb vested rights. The department did not sustain its burden of establishing the existence of an available administrative remedy at the time the inmate filed suit. The court of appeal correctly concluded that La. Rev. Stat. Ann. § 15:1171-1179 as amended by Act 89 could not be applied retroactively to a case in which a claimant would be divested of vested rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeal.

Forum for Equal. PAC v. McKeithen


No. 04-CA-2477, No. 04-CA-2523


SUPREME COURT OF LOUISIANA


04-2477 (La. 1/19/05); 893 So. 2d 715; 2005 La. LEXIS 131



January 19, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] Released for Publication February 2, 2005.
Companion case at Forum for Equal. PAC v. McKeithen, 893 So. 2d 738, 2005 La. LEXIS 128 (La., Jan. 19, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: ON DIRECT APPEAL FROM THE NINETEENTH JUDICIAL DISTRICT COURT, FOR THE PARISH OF EAST BATON ROUGE. HONORABLE WILLIAM A. MORVANT, JUDGE.
Forum for Equal. PAC v. McKeithen, 886 So. 2d 1172, 2004 La. App. LEXIS 2407 (La.App. 1 Cir., Oct. 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. STAY DISSOLVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the Louisiana Secretary of State, and a city, appealed a decision of the Nineteenth Judicial District Court, for the Parish of East Baton Rouge (Louisiana), which ruled in favor of Plaintiffs, a political action committee, a group, and individuals, and declared La. Const. art. XII, § 15 unconstitutional in violation of La. Const art. XIII, § 1(B).


OVERVIEW: An amendment to the Constitution of Louisiana, La. Const. art. XII, § 15, was approved by the voters, and plaintiffs filed suit against defendants alleging that the election was defective and that the amendment was unconstitutional. The district court declared the amendment unconstitutional on the grounds that it contained more than one object. The court reversed, and held that the single object rule as stated in La. Const. art. XIII, § 1(B) required that an amendment to the constitution embody a single plan and that every provision was germane to that plan. Given the clear language of the title of the amendment, "Defense of Marriage," one could logically conclude the object of the amendment was "defense of marriage," and the central theme running throughout the legislative committee meetings was the need to protect the civil tradition of marriage through the adoption of a constitutional amendment. Examining each provision of the amendment, the court held that the only contract or legal instrument whereby the State was mandated to bestow all or substantially all the rights created by said contract was the contract of marriage between one man and one woman.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the district court.
